Dear Dr. Mohammad Mokhbar,
Honorable Acting President
Referring to letter No. 51877 dated 1402/3/28, in accordance with Articles 123 and 131 of the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Iran, the "Law on the Seventh Five-Year Development Plan of the Islamic Republic of Iran" approved in a public session on Tuesday, 1403/3/1, which was deemed in accordance with the expediency of the system by the Honorable Expediency Council in implementation of Article 112 of the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Iran and Article (200) of the Internal Regulations of the Islamic Consultative Assembly on 2/4/1403, is hereby notified in the attachment.
Speaker of the Islamic Consultative Assembly - Mohammad Baqer Qalibaf
National Planning and Budget Organization
Pursuant to Article 131 and in implementation of Article 123 of the Constitution of the Islamic Republic of Iran, the following is annexed to the "Law on the Seventh Five-Year Development Plan of the Islamic Republic of Iran" which was approved in a public session of the Islamic Consultative Assembly on Tuesday, June 1, 1403, and was deemed in accordance with the expediency of the system by the Council of Experts on 2/4/1403, with the approval of Clause "A" of Article (11) and the amendment of Clause "P" and Note (2) of Clause "C" of Article (8), Clause "T" of Article (10) and Note (1) of Clause "T" of Article (102), and was received by the Islamic Consultative Assembly through Letter No. 910/18992 on 12/4/1403, and is hereby notified for implementation.
Acting President - Mohammad Mokhbar
Law on the Seventh Five-Year Development Plan of the Islamic Republic of Iran (1403-1407)
Article 1- The terms and abbreviations used in this law have the following meanings:
A- Program: Seventh Five-Year Progress Plan (1403-1407)
B- Organization: National Planning and Budget Organization
C- Executive agencies: Ministries, government institutions subordinate to the executive branch, and government companies subject to Article (4) of the Public Accounts Law of the country approved on 1/6/1366 and subject to Article (4) of the Civil Service Management Law approved on 2/7/2007.
Note 1: The definition of "executive apparatus" in other laws remains valid with respect to this law.
Note 2: Government institutions subordinate to the executive branch, as well as government companies mentioned in this clause, whose application to the law requires mentioning or specifying their names, are subject to this clause.
D- Non-governmental public institutions and organizations: Non-governmental public institutions and organizations subject to Article (3) of the Civil Service Management Law and Article (5) of the National Public Accounting Law and its Note.
E- Central Bank: Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran
C- Credit institution: Bank and non-bank credit institution subject to clause "h" of Article (1) of the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran Law approved on 30/3/1402
G- Parliament: Islamic Consultative Assembly
Chapter 1 - Economic Growth
Article 2- In implementing paragraph (1) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan announced by the Supreme Leader on 20/6/1401, and in order to achieve the following quantitative goals, action will be taken in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:
Table No. (1) - Quantitative objectives of economic growth performance indicators
Performance measure
One known
Average annual growth in the program
Economic growth of 8 percent
Total factor productivity growth of 2.8 percent
(A thirty-five percent (35%) share in providing eight percent (8%) economic growth)
Net employment growth 3.9 (annual average, one million jobs) percent
Oil exports grow by 12 percent
Non-oil exports grow by 23 percent
Oil sector growth of 9 percent
Water, electricity and gas sector growth of 8 percent
Transportation and warehousing sector growth of 10 percent
Mining sector growth of 13 percent
Industrial sector growth of 8.5 percent
Construction sector growth of 9 percent
Agricultural sector growth of 5.5 percent
Communications sector growth of 11 percent
Other services sector growth of 6.5 percent
Note - In order to increase the productivity of total factors of production, the organization is required, in cooperation with the relevant executive bodies, to prepare the necessary programs to improve productivity by separating different sectors through technology units, private companies and knowledge-based companies, including annual operational schedules, provision of resources and preparation, division and distribution of duties and authorities, designation of those responsible for implementing the programs in each sector, effective supervision and accountability and responsibility for achieving total factor productivity in all sectors in accordance with the schedule with a share of thirty-five percent (35%) of eight percent (8%) of economic growth by the end of the first year of the program, and to take legal action annually to monitor and report on the productivity of total factors of production and the implementation of the programs. Public non-governmental institutions and organizations are also subject to this ruling.
The country's administrative and employment organization is required to submit a report on monitoring employee productivity in the public sector and its implementation to the organization and the parliament every six months. The organization is required to send economic growth performance indicators to the parliament annually.
Equipping resources
Article 3 - The following measures shall be taken to strengthen the provision of financial resources for production:
A- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to prepare, in cooperation with the organization, the Central Bank, and other executive agencies, a plan to finance the target economic growth in the following year, including the amount of financial resources required and the method of securing them from the capital market, banking resources, investment, and foreign financing, in compliance with Article 80 of the Constitution, insurance, production, and sale of property and assets, resources of the National Development Fund, and other resources within the framework of the laws, by the end of each year, and submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval, and submit its report to the Parliament every three months.
The Minister of Economic Affairs and Finance shall be responsible for preparing an efficient plan for the full realization of the resources subject to this clause. The executive regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance in cooperation with the Organization and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers. The responsibility for implementing all duties and realizing resources assigned to other executive bodies pursuant to this regulation shall lie with the highest authority of the executive body.
B- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required, within three months of the entry into force of this law, to provide a suitable platform for the general public to invest in projects with high returns or foreign exchange in the form of a public offering of shares of the project's public joint-stock company and the issuance of debt securities (currency-rial), and to take steps to remove obstacles to financing the private and cooperative sectors, including through the issuance of debt securities (currency-rial).
C- The Central Bank is authorized to grant permission to banks to issue special term certificates of deposit in order to finance projects and to notify the banking network of the instructions for issuing the said certificates, and to determine and announce the ceiling in rials for the issuance of these certificates by the end of Farvardin each year.
Business environment
Article 4- In order to improve the business environment and boost production, the following measures will be taken:
A- The government is required to make tariff protections time-bound and review the commercial interest rate on imports in accordance with the country's commercial and industrial policies within three months of the entry into force of this law.
B- The Ministry of Industry, Mine and Trade (Trade Development Organization of Iran) is required to provide the necessary conditions for the establishment, development and support of private companies, cooperatives and companies affiliated with public non-governmental institutions and institutions that are export intermediaries, including export management companies, partnerships (consortia) and export accelerators, by the end of the first year of the program. The Ministry of Industry, Mine and Trade is required to submit a report on the performance of this paragraph to the Parliament every six months.
C- In order to prevent any over-declaration or under-declaration in the import or export of goods:
1- The Central Bank is required to reform foreign exchange policies and foreign exchange exchange infrastructure in a way that eliminates the possibility of over-declaration in imports and under-declaration in exports of goods.
2- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance (Customs of the Islamic Republic of Iran) is required to reform customs mechanisms, so that, starting from the first year of the program, it annually issues and values 
"Tariff Specific Codes (TSCs)" for at least ten imported goods with the highest customs tariff base and ten exported goods with the highest export value in the previous year.
D- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance (the National Tax Affairs Organization) and the Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare (the insurance organizations) are required to establish a process for collecting insurance premiums by the National Tax Affairs Organization in order to expedite and facilitate the processes of paying and collecting taxes and insurance deductions from business units by the end of the first year of the program at the latest.
The Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare, in cooperation with the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance and competent authorities or boards of trustees, is required to prepare the relevant executive regulations, including the executive mechanism and the compilation of the list of individuals whose wages and salaries have been declared by employers, and submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval. The Tax Affairs Organization of the country is required to act in such a way that the insurance premiums are deposited by employers directly into the accounts of the insurance organizations.
Note - In implementing this ruling, the Social Security Organization is required to take steps by the end of the first year of the program to electronicize the process of issuing account statements in such a way that in all contract contracts, the type of contract, the calculation of the insurance premium rate and the obligations of the parties are determined systematically at the time of issuing the contract row. The Ministries of Economic Affairs and Finance (National Tax Affairs Organization) and Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare (Social Security Organization) are required to send a report on the performance of this clause to the Planning and Budget and Economic and Social Accounting Commissions of the Parliament every three months.
E- In order to clarify the business environment and facilitate the calculation of the risk of conducting financial transactions and interactions between individuals in terms of judicial records, the Judiciary is required to first announce to the inquired person the possibility of online inquiry of the records of definitive financial convictions and insolvency of individuals in civil and criminal courts, such as the number and repetition of convictions, the type of act committed, the type and amount of the conviction, the amount of financial convictions paid and unpaid, the status of the debtor's insolvency from paying the judgment and the cost of the proceedings, and the status of the fulfillment of obligations of individuals in the registration enforcement departments, in a structured manner through the National Information Exchange Center, after the request of the inquirer and the confirmation of the inquired person, and after the final confirmation of the inquired person, it shall first announce to the inquired person and send it to the inquirer.
Note - Non-pecuniary convictions, as well as cases where the judge has ordered not to publish the contents of the verdict due to the possibility of corruption, are excluded from the scope of this clause.
C- The National Real Estate and Documents Registration Organization is required, in cooperation with the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance, to launch an electronic commercial office system from the beginning of the second year of the program, replacing the seals of commercial offices subject to Articles (6) to (14) of the Commercial Law approved on 1/23/1311.
G- In order to protect the rights of citizens, the judiciary is obliged to inform individuals of the ban on leaving the country issued by the courts within 24 hours through the electronic judicial notification system (SANA), stating the reason. Also, the Police Command of the Islamic Republic of Iran is obliged to notify individuals of the ban on leaving the country issued by the courts or other legal authorities, in accordance with paragraph (3) of Article (16) of the Passport Law approved on 11/20/1351, with subsequent amendments and additions.
Note - Cases where, in the judge's judgment, due to security reasons, the accused is prohibited from leaving the country are excluded from the scope of this clause.
Popularization of the economy
Article 5 - In order to popularize the economy, attract private sector participation, and reduce government and non-governmental public institutions and organizations, the following measures will be implemented:
A.
1- Executive bodies are required, within the framework of the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution and in compliance with the Law on the Implementation of the General Policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, approved on 6/8/13811, with subsequent amendments and additions, to gradually transfer all their shares in companies, including manufacturing, service and commercial companies, with the exception of cases where the transfer is prohibited in the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, by the end of the second year of this law at the latest.
This ruling does not prevent the Privatization Organization from carrying out its legal duties, and the aforementioned organization is required, in addition to monitoring and implementing this section, to directly take action to transfer the units covered by this section if the transfer is not completed by the due date through the relevant agencies, so that the transfer is completed by the end of the third year.
The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to submit a report on the performance of this component to the Planning and Budget, Accounting and Economic Committees of the Parliament every three months.
2- Public non-governmental institutions and organizations and all pension funds are required to transfer their management or control shares and those of the companies they own by the end of the second year of the program, in compliance with the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution. In cases where there is a compelling interest in the existence of management or control shares, with the proposal and responsibility of the highest authority of the relevant body and the approval of the Supreme Council for the Implementation of the General Policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, the subject of the Law on the Implementation of the General Policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution and the approval of the Council of Ministers, only within the limits and time limit of the interest stipulated in the Council of Ministers' resolution, non-governmental public institutions and organizations and pension funds are exempt from the transfer of management or control shares.
The aforementioned shares must be offered on the capital market at least once a year. In the event of refusal to offer by the end of the first year of the program, twenty percent (20%) of the share of dividends of non-governmental public institutions and organizations shall be collected as tax from the aforementioned company, and five percentage points shall be added to the aforementioned tax rate each year. The shares of the company owned by non-governmental public institutions and organizations producing public and exclusive goods and services within the framework of the main missions and duties stipulated in the laws governing the aforementioned institutions and organizations shall be exempt from the scope of this ruling. This exception shall not prevent the transfer of the aforementioned shares by the aforementioned institutions and organizations with their consent.
Violators of this ruling, including real and legal members of the assembly and CEOs of companies who obstruct the implementation of the aforementioned ruling, will be sentenced to five years of dismissal from public and government services and a ban on membership in and management of commercial companies.
The organization is required to compile the performance of the agencies covered by this section and send a consolidated report every six months to the Planning and Budget, Economic and Social Accounts, and Accounting Commissions of the Parliament. The agencies covered are required to cooperate with the organization in this regard, and failure to implement this provision will be considered a violation and will be investigated by the competent authorities.
B- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to take the following measures, in cooperation with other executive agencies, by the end of the second year of the program, with the aim of aligning the management powers of the government and public non-governmental institutions and organizations in enterprises with the amount of their shares:
1- In order to strengthen the position of minority shareholders, provide appropriate mechanisms for submitting proposals by minority shareholders for consideration by the board of directors and company assemblies and increase the transparency of transactions with related parties based on Article (129) of the bill amending part of the Commercial Code approved on 12/24/1347 through measures such as disclosing details of the transaction subject, transaction price, price determination process, reasons for not conducting transactions with unrelated parties, and an expert report on the pricing of the aforementioned asset.
2- In order to prevent the creation of non-transparent structures through the acquisition of shares of main companies by their subsidiaries and affiliates, the beneficiaries of the aforementioned main companies should be identified, the transferable shares should be determined, and the desired shares should be transferred in accordance with the list announced by this Ministry, in compliance with the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution and its implementing law.
Note - In the event that shares of public joint-stock companies are acquired by their subsidiaries or affiliates, in the first year, twenty-five percent (25%) of the profits belonging to the subsidiaries or affiliates will be collected as tax, and from the second year onwards, fifty percent (50%) of the profits belonging to the subsidiaries or affiliates will be collected as tax in addition to the legal tax. Also, from the third year of implementation of the plan, the owners of these shares will not have voting rights and will not be included in the quorums related to calling and holding general meetings and their decisions.
Violating managers are sentenced to two years of suspension from public and government services, and a ban on membership in the board of directors and executive management of commercial companies, and the return of double the salaries and benefits received during that management period. Managers of companies that have at least one management seat directly or indirectly (through intermediaries) owned by public joint-stock companies registered with the Securities and Exchange Organization are required to submit a list of the companies they own and their percentage of ownership in them to the Securities and Exchange Organization.
The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance (Securities and Exchange Organization) is required to take steps to ensure that the announcement of the composition of shareholders with voting rights in each company by the Central Securities Depository and Settlement Company is made in accordance with the provisions of this paragraph. Any issuance of a decree by government officials for membership in the board of directors of companies transferred in implementation of the Law on the Implementation of General Policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, exceeding the percentage of government ownership in the said companies, is prohibited.
The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to submit a report on the performance of this section to the Planning and Budget, Accounting and Economic Committees of the Parliament every six months.
C- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to take action by the end of the first year of the program to attract private sector participation and facilitate the transfer process, in compliance with the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, based on the following conditions:
1- Using the debt repayment method through the transfer of ownership of shares and company shares to non-governmental public institutions and institutions, private and cooperative sectors, and pension funds, in compliance with the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, will be possible only through public auction and with the possibility of offsetting the transaction price with the claims of the aforementioned institutions from the government, in compliance with Article 53 (53) of the Constitution.
2- If the defects in the transfer contracts are not due to the buyer's negligence or fault, alternative solutions should be used to the extent possible - such as amending or renewing the contracts, as the case may be - with the buyer's consent and in compliance with the laws. If, in the judgment of the arbitration panel under Article (30) of the Law on the Implementation of General Policies, Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, these defects result in the invalidity or termination of the contract, the government is obliged to pay the amounts paid by the buyer and the expert value of the investment made by the buyer (which is determined by an official expert or experts of the judiciary in accordance with the relevant laws), adjusted to the current price based on the official expert's opinion.
In cases where the subject of investment is movable property and the buyer intends to transfer it, the buyer has the option of transferring it, otherwise, the fee will be paid based on the consent and official expert opinion.
3- The transfer of government property and assets, except for shares or government company shares in transferable enterprises, to non-governmental public institutions and entities is permitted only after two public calls and only from the 100% private or cooperative sector and the private and cooperative sectors do not welcome the call.
The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to submit to the Parliament every six months a list of government assets and properties that have been transferred to public institutions after two public calls.
D- In the event that public joint stock companies are acquired by shareholders who, according to the Competition Council, have a conflict of interest in the value chain of that company and are considered to be an example of anti-competitive behavior, in addition to being deprived of their voting rights in the board of directors and statutory assemblies, the aforementioned shareholders are required to transfer their shares within two years in such a way that they are not the main or alternate members of the board of directors of these companies, with or without voting rights.
E- Any illegal withdrawal for one's own benefit or that of another, or unauthorized appropriation of property belonging to credit institutions, Islamic Azad University, pension funds and organizations, and their affiliated companies, as well as non-governmental companies whose shares or capital are partly owned by executive agencies, by persons to whom the aforementioned property has been entrusted in accordance with their duties, shall be considered embezzlement or illegal appropriation, as the case may be.
C- In line with the popularization of the economy, the government is obliged to use the capacities of the private and cooperative sectors, jihadi groups whose licenses are issued by the Basij Mostazafin Organization or through competent legal authorities or revolutionary institutions or the Basij Construction Organization with the approval and coordination of the Basij Mostazafin Organization, non-governmental organizations, and also by using capital market tools, to provide the possibility of people's participation in economic and development activities, including rural development, watershed management and watershed management, construction, operation and management of health-treatment centers and sports, cultural and artistic venues, construction and operation of railway and road projects, construction and production of housing, urban plans (projects), domestic and foreign commercial services, social services, technical, engineering and communication and information technology services, and the like, through the methods of purchasing services, entrusting management, public-private partnership, leasing, operation, and other methods stipulated in permanent laws, in such a way that a portion of the enterprises of the agencies responsible for carrying out the above-mentioned tasks is reduced annually. The organization is required to prepare the relevant regulations and submit them to the Council of Ministers for approval.
Employment
Article 6 - In order to develop employment, especially employment resulting from the creation of small home businesses (up to two employees), small workshops (up to seven employees) and small workshops (up to twenty employees), with priority for establishment in deprived and rural areas, the following measures will be taken from the first year of the program:
A- The Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare is required to cooperate with executive agencies and institutions, organizations and companies providing business development services to establish or develop small home businesses and small and micro workshops;
1- Prepare an annual quantitative plan, broken down by quota, for the ministries of Jihad, Agriculture, Industry, Mines and Trade, Cultural Heritage, Tourism and Handicrafts, Education, Communications and Information Technology, Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare, Islamic Culture and Guidance, and the Presidential Vice-President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy, the Martyr and Veterans Affairs Foundation, the Imam Khomeini Relief Committee (RA), the National Welfare Organization, the Construction Mobilization Organization, the National Prisons and Security and Educational Measures Organization, as well as institutions, organizations and companies providing business development services with provincial distribution for job creation from the establishment and development of businesses.
2- To select institutions, organizations, and companies that provide business development services with a model, experience, and facilitation network and are non-governmental in nature, including "public non-governmental institutions and organizations, Imam Khomeini Relief Committee (RA), Barakat Foundation of the Executive Headquarters of the Imam's Order (RA), Alavi Foundation, Foundation for the Oppressed of the Islamic Revolution, Basij-e-Sazandegi Organization, National Welfare Organization, charity centers affiliated with charitable institutions and organizations, and other charitable institutions and centers, jihadi groups, non-governmental organizations, and the private sector" as a liaison between the government and the people and to determine quotas for each of them with the tasks of identifying the capacities of the business environment, identifying and assessing the qualifications of applicants, facilitating, and promoting businesses.
The quota for creating businesses for the entities subject to this section is determined in such a way that it increases by at least ten percent (10%) each year compared to their performance in the previous year.
3- Institutions and agencies in charge of employment, in cooperation with the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance and the Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare, are required to create the necessary incentives to develop and strengthen institutions supporting small home businesses, such as companies active in market development, supply of inputs and business services.
The report of empowered individuals from this component is submitted annually by the aforementioned agencies and institutions to the government and parliament.
Note 1- The Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare can transfer the quotas of each agency based on their annual performance. Executive agencies and institutions, organizations and companies providing business development services can transfer the notified quotas up to twenty-five percent (25%) between provinces based on the performance of their provincial units.
Note 2 - In addition to fulfilling their quota, institutions, organizations, and companies providing business development services can assume the executive agency role of achieving their goals based on contracts concluded with the aforementioned executive agencies.
B- Bank facilities granted to small home businesses and small workshops are in the form of Qarz al-Hasanah (goodwill loans) and in the case of small workshops, in the form of low-cost facilities.
Note 1: The difference in the rate of low-cost facilities granted to small workshops is financed through the government's financial partnership with banks or by paying the difference in the rate of facilities.
Note 2 - The organization is required to foresee in the annual budget bills the annual goals of this type of business, which are approved by the Supreme Employment Council upon the proposal of the Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare, as well as the amount of facilities they need, the required Qarz al-Hasana resources and public budget resources to help with infrastructure, interest subsidy on facilities, assistance and facilities, and integration with bank resources.
Note 3: In addition to determining the share of operating banks in granting Qarz al-Hasana resources, the Central Bank is required to develop chain financial methods, increase the scope of collateral coverage, such as calculating the difference in collateral value from the balance of the facility, profits from contracts and other verifiable assets, improve the mechanisms of credit assessment, collateralization, guarantees and underwriting, and create the necessary incentives for banks to accelerate the filing of facility granting files and create communication networks (channels) with the public. The Central Bank is responsible for the proper implementation of this note.
Note 4: Granting bank facilities to applicants for establishing and developing small home businesses is done solely on the basis of a credit assessment or obtaining a promissory note from the applicant.
Note 5 - Institutions, bodies, and companies providing business development services that are established according to the law are subject to the provisions of this article.
The Central Bank is required to submit a report on the performance of Notes (1), (3) and (4) of this clause to the Parliament every six months.
C- In order to develop labor market statistics and information databases and job search systems for the use of all sectors, including the private sector, municipalities, and non-governmental organizations, and to monitor their activities, the Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor, and Social Welfare, in cooperation with the Statistical Center of Iran and other information authorities, is required to design and establish a "National Labor Market Information System" within a maximum of three months from the entry into force of this law, including an annual description and analysis of the labor market situation, an estimate of the future status of the labor market in the short, medium, and long term, broken down by skills, specialties, and geographical distribution, an estimate of labor market demand, broken down by educational level, gender, and regional distribution (up to the county level), and the announcement of job standards in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law and the Law on Facilitating the Issuance of Business Licenses approved on 12/24/1400 with subsequent amendments and additions within the framework of the International Standard Classification of Occupations and Professions (ISCO) in compliance with Islamic principles.
D- The Ministry of Agricultural Jihad is required, within the framework of the laws and in line with the efficiency of the capacities and empowerment of rural and tribal women, to formulate a program for the development of rural small businesses based on the competitive advantage of the regions and the completion of the value chain, to establish a national network of women's cooperatives with the aim of training in the production and marketing cycle, self-regulation and ranking of cooperatives, providing employment creation facilities and tax support for cooperatives based on the ranking system, and to launch local markets.
Chapter 2 - Reforming the Banking System and Curbing Inflation
Article 7- In order to implement paragraph (2) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and to achieve the following quantitative goals, action shall be taken in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:
Table No. (2) - Quantitative objectives of performance indicators for banking system reform and inflation control
Performance measure
One known
Quantitative goal at the end of the program
Liquidity growth of 13.8 percent
Inflation 9.5 percent
Reducing unauthorized overdrafts by "credit institutions" from the Central Bank by 100 percent
With a 20% reduction each year
Capital adequacy ratio of credit institutions at least 8 percent
The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance and the Central Bank are required to submit an annual report to the Parliament on reforming the banking system and curbing inflation.
Financial structure of the banking system
ماده۸ ـ
A- In order to reform the financial structure of the banking system and resolve the imbalances of credit institutions, the following measures will be taken:
1- The board of directors, upon approval by the extraordinary general assembly of each credit institution, whether governmental or non-governmental, whose capital adequacy ratio at the time of the entry into force of this law is less than the ratio stated in Table No. (2) of Article (7) of this law, is required to submit to the Central Bank, within two months of the entry into force of this law, the credit institution's capital increase plan to achieve the goal stated in the aforementioned table. The Central Bank is required to notify the credit institution of the aforementioned plan within a maximum of two months, either directly or with the necessary amendments for implementation.
2- The capital increase of non-governmental credit institutions shall be carried out in the following order:
1-2- Non-governmental credit institutions are required to submit the capital increase plan notified by the Central Bank to their extraordinary general assembly for approval and begin the legal process of capital increase after notification by the Central Bank.
2-2- If, after two months from the deadline for the extraordinary general meeting referred to in subparagraph (1) of this paragraph, for any reason, including failure to hold a general meeting of the non-governmental credit institution, failure to approve the capital increase announced by the Central Bank at the extraordinary general meeting, or failure to implement the resolution of the extraordinary general meeting, the capital increase of the non-governmental credit institution is not carried out in accordance with the plan announced by the Central Bank, the powers of the extraordinary general meeting to increase capital shall be transferred to the Central Bank, and the Central Bank shall be obliged to increase the capital of the non-governmental credit institution in question by offering shares on the stock market and securities market by disqualifying the current shareholders.
3-2- The Central Bank is responsible for supervising the implementation of the capital increase program of non-governmental credit institutions and improving their capital adequacy ratio, and the Central Bank is required to submit a report on the implementation of the capital increase program and the status of the capital adequacy of non-governmental credit institutions to the President, the Speaker of the Parliament, and the Supreme Steering Council of the program referred to in paragraph "A" of Article (118) of this law every six months.
3- The capital increase of state-owned banks is carried out in the following order:
1-3- The Minister of Economic Affairs and Finance and the Head of the Organization are required to prepare, within one month of the entry into force of this law, a plan to increase the capital of state-owned banks and how to secure the resources required to implement the said plan, and submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval.
2-3- All resources resulting from the revaluation of state-owned banks’ assets that, according to the Central Bank’s judgment, can lead to an improvement in the bank’s capital adequacy and their annual net profit shall be spent only on increasing capital until the bank’s capital adequacy ratio reaches the ratio specified in Table (2). The Minister of Economic Affairs and Finance is responsible for the strict implementation of this paragraph. Any transfer of state-owned banks’ assets to other executive bodies during the years of the program is prohibited. The revaluation of state-owned banks’ assets during the implementation of the program is exempt from tax.
3-3- The Minister of Economic Affairs and Finance is responsible for implementing the program to increase capital and improve the capital adequacy ratio of state-owned banks, and the Central Bank is responsible for supervising the proper implementation of the aforementioned program. The Minister of Economic Affairs and Finance and the Governor of the Central Bank are required to submit the status of the capital adequacy of state-owned banks and the progress of the program mentioned in part (1-3) to the President, the Speaker of the Parliament, and the Supreme Steering Council of the program every six months.
B- In order to ensure transparency in the activities of credit institutions, improve their balance sheets, and expand the Central Bank's information oversight of the country's banking network:
1- The Central Bank is required to launch the “Banking Network Real Estate System” and the “Banking Network Shareholding System” within one month of the entry into force of this law, submit the relevant executive instructions for approval by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank, and provide access to the aforementioned systems to all credit institutions.
Credit institutions are required to enter information related to real estate under their ownership or real estate they claim ownership of in the "Banking Network Real Estate System" in the order announced by the Central Bank.
Credit institutions are also required to include information related to their shares or partnership interests in companies, including listed and unlisted companies, and information related to other shareholders, real estate, real estate, stocks, and other assets belonging to the aforementioned companies in the "Banking Network Shareholding System" in the order announced by the Central Bank.
The Central Bank is required to prepare the aforementioned systems in such a way that all required information regarding real estate, immovable property, and shares belonging to governmental and non-governmental credit institutions, whether directly owned by the credit institution or wholly or partially owned by the credit institution through companies whose shares the credit institution owns in whole or in part, is recorded in the aforementioned systems.
The responsibility for accurately entering the requested information and updating it lies with the board of directors of the credit institution. The board of directors of the credit institution is jointly and severally liable with the board of directors for the correct and accurate entry of the requested information. Intentional concealment of assets that directly or indirectly belong to a bank or non-bank credit institution or registration of false information with the intention of concealing the characteristics of the said assets is considered a violation. The violating credit institution is subject to the penalties of subparagraph (2) and following paragraph (b) of Article (23) of the Central Bank Law, and the violating managers or employees are sentenced by the Central Bank's disciplinary board to dismissal from service in the government and the banking network for up to three years.
The deadline for registering information related to real estate, immovable property, and shares of credit institutions in the systems subject to this subsection is six months after the notification of the Central Bank's instructions in this regard.
After the expiration of the above deadline, if any assets belonging to credit institutions are discovered that are not registered in the systems subject to this section, they will be transferred to the banking network asset management company subject to paragraph "P" of this article, in accordance with this law, and any transfer or verification of them by credit institutions will be invalid and ineffective.
Real estate, immovable property, and shares that are acquired by credit institutions after the expiration of the aforementioned period will be subject to the provisions of this section in terms of the requirement for registration and the legal effects resulting from their failure to register in the above systems.
2- The following provisions are applicable to real estate, immovable property and shares held by credit institutions:
1-2- Credit institutions are required to specify the portion of real estate, immovable property and shares in their possession, the maintenance of which is necessary for carrying out the banking profession and is not prohibited by law, stating the reason in the systems referred to in subparagraph (1) of this paragraph.
The guidelines for determining the properties, real estate, and shares subject to this component shall be approved by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank within the framework of the laws.
2-2- Other assets registered in the “Banking Network Real Estate System” and “Banking Network Shareholding System” other than the assets subject to item (1-2) are considered surplus assets. Credit institutions are required to transfer their surplus assets by the end of the second year of the program at the latest.
This deadline is three years for credit institutions whose capital adequacy ratio is equal to or greater than the limit specified in the table in Article (7) of this law.
3-2- The Central Bank is responsible for identifying real estate, immovable property and non-surplus shares of credit institutions and confirming that they are not surplus in the systems referred to in subsection (1) of this paragraph within the framework of the instructions mentioned in subsection (1-2), and the Governor of the Central Bank must report to the Supreme Board of the Central Bank in this regard. The objection of the credit institution to the Central Bank’s identification shall be considered within the framework of Article (22) of the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran Law.
4-2- Real estate, real estate and surplus shares belonging to credit institutions since the beginning of 1395 or since the time of acquisition if their ownership was transferred to the credit institution after the aforementioned date, are subject to the tax mentioned in clauses “b” and “c” of Article (17) of the Law on Removing Barriers to Competitive Production and Improving the Country’s Financial System, approved on 2/1/1394. The National Tax Affairs Organization is obliged to determine and collect the deferred tax related to the aforementioned clauses by the end of the second year of the program.
5-2- If the credit institution is unable to transfer the real estate, real estate and surplus shares for any reason, including the absence of a buyer, it may transfer the said assets to the Banking Network Asset Management Company. The Banking Network Asset Management Company is obliged to purchase the real estate, real estate and shares belonging to the credit institutions at the following prices, upon request:
- Stocks with active board prices, at most at the board price
- Unlisted shares at a maximum of book value minus fifteen percent (15%)
- Real estate, at a maximum of book value minus fifteen percent (15%)
The Bank Network Asset Management Company can issue Islamic financial bonds and transfer them to credit institutions whose assets have been transferred to the Bank Network Asset Management Company. The said bonds are subject to verification by the Central Bank; however, they cannot be traded in the market or transferred to others without the approval of the Supreme Board of the Central Bank. Other characteristics of the said bonds are determined by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank within the framework of the laws. In calculating the capital adequacy ratio of credit institutions, the Islamic financial bonds issued by the Bank Network Asset Management Company are considered to have a risk factor of zero.
6-2- If the credit institution definitively transfers the real estate, real estate and shares subject to sub-section (2-2) of this clause to the banking network asset management company or any other person other than the credit institution and its subsidiaries and affiliates by the end of the third year of the program, the State Tax Affairs Organization is obliged to suspend the collection of the tax subject to paragraphs "b" and "c" of Article (17) of the Law on Removing Barriers to Competitive Production and Improving the Country's Financial System. If, for any reason, the aforementioned assets are returned to the credit institution in question, the State Tax Affairs Organization is obliged to collect the aforementioned tax.
Note 1- The National Deeds and Real Estate Registration Organization (General Department of Registration of Companies and Non-Commercial Institutions) and the National Civil Registration Organization are required to provide all information requested by the Central Bank regarding the assets registered in the “Banking Network Real Estate System” and the “Banking Network Shareholding System” and the legal and natural persons related to the aforementioned assets, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law, immediately online to the Central Bank. The highest authority of the aforementioned organizations is responsible for the accurate and complete implementation of this ruling, and in case of refusal to implement this ruling, the court will sentence him to dismissal from service in the government and the banking network for up to three years.
Note 2- Registration of assets in the "Banking Network Real Estate System" and the "Banking Network Shareholding System" is solely for the purpose of transparency of credit institutions' activities and expanding the Central Bank's information oversight of the banking network, and cannot be relied upon as evidence of ownership in legal disputes between credit institutions and other persons.
C- The "Banking Network Asset Management Company" shall be established under the Deposit Guarantee Fund and with the capital of that fund, with the aim of generating, marketing, and selling surplus assets of unsound (irretrievable) banks, at the discretion of the Central Bank, within a maximum of six months from the entry into force of this law.
The articles of association and regulations governing the establishment, operation, and dissolution of the Bank Network Asset Management Company, the pricing and transfer of assets, and the settlement of accounts between the said company and credit institutions shall be prepared by the Central Bank in cooperation with the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers after approval by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank. Any income recognition, revaluation, and transfer of assets of the credit institution to the Bank Network Asset Management Company shall be subject to zero tax rate for a single period during the implementation of the program.
Complaints related to this paragraph shall be handled solely within the framework of Article (22) of the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran Law. If the plaintiff is recognized as a victim by a final court decision, the damages incurred shall be compensated solely in financial terms by the Central Bank within the limits stipulated in the law and the court ruling. If the damages are proven to be due to the negligence or fault of individuals, the Central Bank shall be obliged to file a lawsuit against the individuals involved in causing the damages through legal authorities.
D- A "single owner" whose shares in a non-governmental credit institution exceed the permitted limits specified in Article (5) of the Law on the Implementation of General Policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution shall have no voting rights or the right to participate in capital increases with respect to the surplus shares, and the aforementioned rights and all proceeds from the surplus shares, including cash dividends and proceeds from the increase in the value of the surplus shares (the difference between the amount obtained from the sale of the surplus shares and the value of the surplus shares at the time of transfer to the Fund), shall be transferred to the Deposit Guarantee Fund pursuant to this law. If the amount of shares of the "single owner" does not decrease to the permitted limits within one year after the amount of shares exceeds the permitted limit, the Deposit Guarantee Fund may offer the surplus shares on the stock exchange and return the proceeds from the sale to the shareholder after deducting the relevant costs and the proceeds from the increase in the value of the surplus shares. If the increase in the number of shares of the "single owner" beyond the permitted limits has occurred forcibly, the provision of this paragraph shall be implemented one year after the forcible transfer of the excess shares to the "single owner".
E- Article (95) of the Law on the Fifth Five-Year Development Plan of the Islamic Republic of Iran, approved on 10/15/2010, with subsequent amendments and additions, shall be enforced in relation to the Deposit Guarantee Fund, taking into account the following:
1- The Deposit Guarantee Fund is required to pay the guaranteed deposits of depositors in liquidated credit institutions after the announcement of the Supreme Board of the Central Bank.
2- After the guaranteed deposits are paid, all rights and claims of depositors up to the amount paid by the Deposit Guarantee Fund shall be transferred to this Fund. The payment of guaranteed amounts to depositors is subject to their written consent to this matter.
3- The ceiling for guaranteeing deposits subject to the Fund's guarantee shall be approved by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank at least once every two years upon the proposal of the Central Bank, with the aim of stabilizing and sounding the banking system and protecting the rights of retail customers, taking into account the inflation rate.
C- Compensation of obligations and payment of debts of credit institutions in transition shall be carried out, respectively, from the following locations:
1- In the event of a finding of fault, the assets of the guilty shareholders or guilty managers shall be seized based on the arrangements set forth in Note (1) of this paragraph, with priority given to shares in the credit institution, other rights in the credit institution, and other assets, in compliance with Subsection (2) of Note (2) of this paragraph.
2- Assets of the credit institution in circulation, including the assets subject to sub-paragraph (1) of Note (2) of this paragraph.
3- Shares and other rights of non-fault shareholders
Note 1: The authority for determining the fault of the guilty shareholders or guilty managers is the Special Branch for Handling Banking Disputes, subject to Article (35) of the Law of the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran. The extent of the responsibility of each guilty shareholder or guilty manager in compensating for the obligations and paying the debts of the credit institution, depending on whether he is at fault or not, is determined by the aforementioned branch.
Note 2- In the following cases, the Attorney General of the country and the prosecutors of the provincial capitals are required to seize the assets in question immediately after the announcement of the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran or the appointed director:
1- Assets whose deed is not in the name of the credit institution in question, but the Central Bank or the credit manager, based on evidence and the approval of the Attorney General of the country or the prosecutor of the provincial capital, claim that the said assets actually belong to the credit institution in question.
2- Assets that are not in the name of the guilty or accused shareholders or the guilty or accused managers, but the Central Bank or the managing director, based on evidence and the Emirati, and with the approval of the Attorney General of the country or the prosecutor of the capital province, claim that the said assets actually belong to the said shareholders or managers.
Any transaction and transfer of the aforementioned assets shall be prohibited and suspended from the time the Central Bank or the appointed administrator notifies the Attorney General or the provincial prosecutor and their approval until the issuance of a final court ruling. The judiciary is required to make arrangements to handle the cases subject to this paragraph with due regard to other important matters requiring attention, with urgency.
Note 3- The phrase “and any collusion in the payment of large-scale banking facilities, including preferential financing for private shareholders and other persons related to credit institutions (subject of Clause “G” of Article (1) of the Law on the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran) and failure to repay large-scale banking facilities” is added to the end of Clause “A” of Article (1) of the Law on the Punishment of Disruptors in the Country’s Economic System, approved on 1990/9/1, with subsequent amendments and additions.
G- In order to create prosperity in the productive sectors of the country's economy through sustainable financing of major development projects and national capital asset acquisition projects, the government is required to transform one of the specialized banks into the "Development Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran" by amending its statute with existing capital and facilities by the end of the first year of the program, and to have its statute approved by the parliament.
The government is also authorized to take legal action to establish "sectoral development banks" using the capacity, capital, facilities, and human resources of other state-owned banks and submit the statutes of these banks to the Council of Ministers for approval.
The Central Bank is required to submit a report on the performance of this section to the Parliament's Economic Committee every six months.
Supervision of credit institutions and unorganized money markets
Article 9 - In order to implement complete and comprehensive supervision over credit institutions, organize unorganized monetary institutions and markets, promote transparency and soundness, and reduce the ratio of non-performing loans to facilities, the following shall be carried out:
A- The Central Bank is required to prepare, within the framework of the laws, by the end of the first year of the program, guidelines for the establishment, operation, management, and supervision of credit institutions, divided into types, including comprehensive, commercial, specialized, savings and housing facilities, development, and charitable loans, in accordance with the nature and specific requirements of each, and to notify them after approval by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank.
B- Credit institutions, members of the “credit institution group” and their shareholders, owners, managers and auditors, and branches of foreign banks within the country are required to cooperate with the Central Bank’s inspectors and submit statistics, information and documents to the Central Bank within the stipulated time frame and in accordance with the requested conditions. Failure to comply with the provisions of this paragraph within the stipulated time frame and in accordance with the notified framework or submitting false, incomplete or misleading information to the Central Bank is considered a crime and the perpetrator, upon complaint by the Central Bank, shall be sentenced to one or more of the seventh-degree ta’zir penalties referred to in Article (19) of the Islamic Penal Code approved on 2/2/1391 with subsequent amendments and additions.
Note - The term "credit institution group" refers to a credit institution and companies in which the credit institution owns at least ten percent (10%) of its shares or, at the discretion of the Central Bank, has appointed at least one member of the board of directors of the said company.
C- Participation of credit institutions and their subsidiaries in the establishment of financial institutions subject to the Securities Market Law of the Islamic Republic of Iran approved on 1/9/2005 without obtaining a license from the Central Bank is prohibited. The perpetrator shall be sentenced by the Central Bank’s disciplinary board to one of the penalties in parts (2) and following, paragraph “b” of Article (23) of the Central Bank Law of the Islamic Republic of Iran.
D- Companies, institutions and financial institutions affiliated and affiliated with credit institutions, with the exception of market-driven investment funds, are not allowed to purchase or hold the shares of the respective credit institution directly or indirectly. The managers of the aforementioned companies, institutions and financial institutions shall be sentenced to one or more of the seventh-degree ta’zir punishments referred to in Article (19) of the Islamic Penal Code, as the case may be, unless they are subject to a more severe punishment.
E- The National Real Estate Registration Organization is required to register and maintain information on all owners of at least one percent (1%) of the shares or capital of legal entities other than companies registered with the Securities and Exchange Organization within six months of the entry into force of this law, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law, and to publish any voluntary or compulsory transfer of ownership of the aforementioned shares or capital in its information system and provide the necessary access to the Central Bank. All legal entities subject to this clause are required to provide the information on shareholders and any changes to it to the National Real Estate Registration Organization, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law. The receipt of all legal fees related to the establishment of a company or other matters that, according to laws and regulations, require registration with the company registration authority and the receipt of fees, in the case of companies subject to this clause, by the National Real Estate Registration Organization is subject to the inclusion of the above-mentioned information in the aforementioned system, and if failure to implement the legal duties of this clause results in damage, compensation must be made in accordance with the laws. Managers and guilty individuals are legally liable.
C- In order to facilitate the process of granting micro-loans, promote and expand the tradition of Qarz al-Hasana, and legalize the activities of Qarz al-Hasana funds, the Central Bank is required to:
1- Facilitate and accelerate the credit assessment system and the collateralization model for goods.
2- Prepare the executive instructions for the establishment and operation of Qarz-ul-Hasanah funds in order to develop these funds in a lawful manner and submit them to the approval of the Supreme Board of the Central Bank. The Central Bank may, within the framework approved by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank, use the capacity of Qarz-ul-Hasanah banks, the Islamic Economic Organization of Iran, or Qarz-ul-Hasanah Funds Centers under its own responsibility in supervising Qarz-ul-Hasanah funds.
Note - The Qarz al-Hasanah Funds Associations are formed within the framework of the Law on the Establishment and Activities of Professional and Professional Organizations, approved on 17/11/1401. Regarding the Qarz al-Hasanah Funds Associations, the Deputy Director of Regulation and Supervision of the Central Bank participates with the right to vote in the working group on the subject of paragraph "A" of Article (2) of the aforementioned law. The professional qualifications of the members of the board of directors of the associations subject to this note must be approved by the Central Bank.
Monetary policies
Article 10- In order to reform the framework and implement monetary policy, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Central Bank is prohibited from granting new credit to credit institutions without receiving collateral. The type and amount of acceptable collateral shall be determined by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank.
B- In order to determine the obligation and repay the debt of the government and state-owned companies to the banking network:
1- The equivalent of the audited claim of credit institutions on the government and state-owned companies, Islamic financial bonds with a maturity of up to five years shall be made available to the creditor credit institutions. Islamic financial bonds related to government debt shall be issued and guaranteed by the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance (National Treasury) and Islamic financial bonds related to state-owned company debt by the debtor state-owned company. These bonds shall be delivered to credit institutions within a maximum of three months from the entry into force of this law. The responsibility for implementing this clause shall be borne by the Minister of Economic Affairs and Finance and the Chairman of the General Assembly of the debtor state-owned company, as the case may be. The said bonds shall be subject to Article (27) of the Securities Market Law of the Islamic Republic of Iran. Also, these bonds shall be substituted for the current debt of the government or state-owned companies to the credit institution and their equivalent shall be deducted from the debt of the government or state-owned company registered in the books of that credit institution. Only the interest on the said bonds shall be foreseen in the annual budget of the government or state-owned company, as the case may be.
2- The Islamic financial bonds subject to this clause have interest coupons and their interest is paid in the order stated in section (3). The interest rate of these bonds is equivalent to the interest rate approved by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank for long-term bank deposits.
3- Interest on Islamic financial bonds related to government debt is paid by the Treasury and interest on Islamic financial bonds related to government companies' debt is paid by the debtor government company. If the debtor government company fails to pay the interest on the bonds within 48 hours before the interest payment date, the Treasury is obliged to withdraw the equivalent of the said amount from the accounts of the company in question with the Treasury and deposit it into the account of the credit institution holding the bonds. Also, if the Treasury fails to pay the interest on the bonds related to government debt within 48 hours before the maturity date of the interest coupon, the Central Bank is obliged to withdraw the equivalent of the said amount from the Treasury's account with the Central Bank and deposit it into the account of the credit institution holding the bonds.
4- The Islamic financial securities subject to this clause are only exchangeable between credit institutions and the Central Bank and cannot be transferred to others. As the case may be, they will be replaced by the government or the issuing state company until the end of the repurchase program or with new Islamic financial securities.
5- The Central Bank is authorized to accept the said securities as collateral by applying a verification coefficient determined by the Supreme Board of the Central Bank.
6- From the time this law comes into effect, any use of banking network resources by the government and state-owned companies must be made in the form of delivering Islamic financial securities tradable in the capital market to credit institutions.
Note - The contracts used to issue Islamic financial securities subject to this clause (principal and interest) must be approved by the Central Bank's Jurisprudential Council.
The ceiling of the bonds subject to this paragraph is two million five hundred thousand billion (2,500,000,000,000,000) rials, of which at least one million billion (1,000,000,000,000,000) rials shall be issued by the government and the rest by state-owned companies and made available to credit institutions. The share of each state-owned company and each credit institution from these bonds shall be determined by a working group composed of the head of the organization, the Minister of Economic Affairs and Finance, and the Governor of the Central Bank no later than one month after the entry into force of this law.
C- In order to improve the processes of granting facilities, the Central Bank is obliged to:
1- In order to achieve justice in the distribution of banking resources, the granting of facilities should be managed in such a way that the ratio of facilities to deposits for deprived and underprivileged provinces and regions increases by at least twenty percent (20%) compared to the beginning of the program during the years of program implementation. The Central Bank is required to submit an annual report on the performance of this component to the Planning and Budget, Accounting, Economic and Social Commissions of the Parliament.
2- Direct bank resources towards production by using various methods, including opening domestic letters of credit (LC) and contract-based financing (factoring) and promoting productive certificates of credit (GAM).
In the event of concluding a contract to grant facilities or creating an obligation without obtaining a unique ID issued by "Samat" or if "Samat" information does not match the provisions of the concluded contract, the facility interest and the fee for the letter of guarantee and letters of credit will not be accepted as an acceptable tax expense for the beneficial legal entity.
D- In order to regulate banking operations:
1- By the end of the first year of the program, credit institutions are required to modify their internal systems in such a way that no commitment or payment of funds under the title of facilities is possible without obtaining a unique identifier issued from the centralized facility and commitment information system (SAMAT).
2- Granting a unique “Samat” ID is subject to the approval of the contracting party in that system. The text of the contract registered in the “Samat” system and the paid, undue and deferred installments must always be visible to the contracting party. The Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran is obliged to provide the necessary infrastructure to implement the provisions of this section within one year from the date of entry into force of this law. In contracts where the beneficiary (the beneficiary or the applicant for issuing a guarantee or opening a letter of credit) is a legal entity, the confirmation of the contract is carried out by the representative of the legal entity in the Samat system. The legal entity must officially introduce its representative to the credit institution.
3- In case of failure to comply with the obligation mentioned in parts (1) and (2) of this clause, the violating credit institution and the involved managers shall be sentenced by the Disciplinary Board of the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran to the penalties specified in parts (2) and following of paragraph "b" of Article (23) of the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran Law, in accordance with Article (22) of the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran Law.
In the event of concluding a facility agreement or creating an obligation without obtaining a unique ID issued by "Samat" or if "Samat" information does not match the terms of the concluded contract, the facility interest and guarantee fees and documentary credits will not be accepted as acceptable tax expenses for the beneficial legal entity.
E- The Central Bank is required to submit to the Central Bank's Supreme Board of Directors the instructions for paying credit facilities in current accounts for household heads with regular income, pensions, or subsidies by the end of the first year of the program.
C- The Central Bank is required to plan in such a way that by the end of the third year of the program, paper checks will not be issued in the banking system.
Note - Paper checks issued by banks before and after the entry into force of this law are valid until they are fully used and spent in subsequent years.
Currency policies
ماده۱۱ـ
A- In implementing paragraph (2) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan aimed at establishing stability in the general level of prices and exchange rates;
1- Executive agencies, credit institutions, exchange offices and state-owned or state-owned companies-affiliated exporters, non-governmental public institutions and organizations, and other natural and legal issuers are required to provide this bank with all information related to their foreign exchange assets and foreign exchange income flows under the rules and in accordance with the method specified by the Central Bank. The supply of foreign exchange in the possession of executive agencies, credit institutions, exchange offices and state-owned or state-owned companies-affiliated exporters, and non-governmental public institutions and organizations must be carried out in coordination with the Central Bank within the framework of this law and the Law on Combating Smuggling of Goods and Foreign Exchange approved on 3/20/1391 with subsequent amendments and additions.
2- Small exporters, including exporters of technical and engineering services, knowledge-based and creative industrial products, horticultural and agricultural products, and handicrafts, can offer the foreign exchange from their exports at the Iranian Foreign Exchange and Gold Exchange Center or, after notifying the Central Bank, use it by themselves or other importers to import permitted goods for which the Central Bank has agreed to provide foreign exchange. The small exporters subject to this section are determined by the Council of Ministers, based on the type and volume of goods or services exported, upon the proposal of the Minister of Industry, Mines, and Trade, and in cooperation with the Ministers of Agricultural Jihad and Cultural Heritage, Tourism, and Handicrafts, and the Vice President for Science, Technology, and Knowledge-Based Economy.
B- Advertising for the illegal purchase and sale of foreign currency in the media and virtual space, depending on the circumstances, is subject to the sixth or seventh degree penalties referred to in Article (19) of the Islamic Penal Code.
C- The responsibility for stabilizing the exchange rate, reducing inflation to a single digit, and directing banks' liquidity and credit toward productive activities within the framework of its legal duties and authorities lies with the Central Bank.
Chapter 3 - Reforming the budget structure
Article 12- In order to implement paragraph (3) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and to achieve the following quantitative goals, action shall be taken in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:
Table No. (3) - Quantitative objectives of performance indicators for budget structure reform
Performance measure
One known
Quantitative goal
At the end of the program
The ratio of capital asset acquisition credits to the general budget is 25 percent.
The ratio of government and state-owned companies' debt, including their debt to the National Development Fund, to GDP is 40.
Percentage
The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to submit a monthly report to the Parliament on the ratio of government and state-owned companies' debt, including their debt to the National Development Fund, to GDP.
Budget overview
Article 13 - In order to regulate and consolidate the budget, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The bill and resolution of the Parliament regarding the annual budget of the entire country should not contain non-budgetary provisions, nor should it lead to amendments to permanent laws or five-year development plans.
B- The organization is required to work with the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance and the Central Bank to establish an integrated and intelligent government financial management system in compliance with Article (30) of the National Plan and Budget Law approved on 11/20/1351, based on the following criteria:
1- All credits (including expenditure credits and acquisition of capital assets) are allocated from public and private sources in the form of electronic credits to the executive branch. The liquidity of the credits is guaranteed by the National Treasury within the announced allocations, and all government payments are deposited by the National Treasury from the credit accounts support account to the final beneficiary.
Note - The Ministry of Intelligence, the Atomic Energy Organization of Iran, the Armed Forces of the Islamic Republic of Iran, military and security institutions, and government institutions that are not subordinate to the executive branch are exempt from the scope of this ruling.
2- All subsidiary bank accounts of executive agencies, including the accounts of account holders and payroll agents, are defined as credit accounts under the main credit account of the executive agency, and their payments are made from the main credit account's supporting account to the ultimate beneficiary.
3- The remaining balance of the credit account of the capital asset acquisition of executive agencies at the end of the fiscal year, which was financed by the National Treasury, is carried over to the following year, and the National Treasury and relevant executive agencies are allowed to pay and use it for a maximum of six months.
The executive regulations of this paragraph shall be prepared by the organization in cooperation with the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance and the Central Bank and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
C- Executive agencies that use the country's entire budget resources and have program assignments are required to submit their operational plan to the organization every year based on the program assignments, including the goals of the desired year, performance indicators, risks to achieving the goals, necessary resources, financing methods, related development plans, and the performance report for the previous year within the framework announced by the organization, no later than the end of August each year for use in preparing the next year's budget bill.
The organization is required to take action to guide, evaluate, and coordinate the implementation of the program and monitor its proper implementation by observing paragraph "A" of Article (118) of this law and using all its legal tools and capacities. The organization is required to prepare the annual budget bill in a program-based manner that contains executive programs and quantitative goals in order to achieve the goals of this law and the legal goals of the main agencies and submit it to the parliament by the government. These programs are the basis for issuing payment allocations and supervision by the Court of Accounts of the country.
Note - The Ministry of Intelligence, the Atomic Energy Organization of Iran, the Armed Forces of the Islamic Republic of Iran, military and security institutions, the Guardian Council, the Parliament, and government institutions that are not subordinate to the executive branch are exempt from the provisions of this paragraph.
Oil and gas revenue
ماده۱۴ـ
A- The government is required to allocate one-third of three percent (3%) of the income from the export of crude oil, gas condensates, and net natural gas exports, based on each province's share in the production value of crude oil, gas condensates, and natural gas, which is valued based on the export price of these three products, to oil- and gas-rich provinces, and the remaining two-thirds to less developed cities, districts, and rural districts, which are determined by the organization based on underdevelopment indicators.
Note 1: The method of distributing income from one-third of offshore oil and gas fields in coastal provinces shall be approved and implemented by the Planning and Development Council of the relevant province.
Note 2: The executive regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the organization in cooperation with the Ministry of Petroleum and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
b)
1- In implementing paragraph (3) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan, the government is required, through the Ministry of Oil and using the domestic foreign exchange and rial resources of the relevant subsidiaries of the Ministry of Oil, after deducting the share related to the energy optimization account referred to in paragraph 5-2, paragraph "A" of Article (46) of this law, to deposit monthly at least sixty percent (60%) of the revenues from the export and domestic sale of all gas by-products, including ethane, propane, butane, pentane, sulfur, and gaseous liquids, exclusively into the "National Oil and Gas Investment" account, which will be opened in the name of the Ministry of Oil at the National Treasury from the beginning of the plan.
