Note 1-
1- The annual increase in employment in the mining and mineral industries sector during the implementation of the program is twenty percent (20%).
2- In implementing the provisions of this table, increasing added value must be observed by completing the value chain from raw materials to final products, while maintaining competitiveness and avoiding raw sales.
3- The production of all types of vehicles, as well as the scrapping of all types of worn-out vehicles, as well as the production of electric and electric-gasoline vehicles, is carried out in accordance with the provisions of general environmental policies.
Note 2 - The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to submit an annual report on the performance indicators of industry, mining and production growth to the Parliament.
Article 48 – In order to achieve general policies, including economic growth, the implementation of major national economic plans that are progressive, up-to-date, and based on foresight, and the completion of the value chain and economic leap, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The organization, in cooperation with the relevant ministries, is required to prepare several major national and pioneering economic plans, including the following, and submit them to the Council of Ministers for approval within three months of the entry into force of this law:
1- Strategic rail and maritime transit corridors
2- High-speed train on long and busy routes, including Tehran-Mashhad
3- Digital transformation in order to apply digital technology capabilities to transform operational procedures and processes, transform business at the country's bureaucratic levels, transform the scope of service delivery, and transform organizational culture by ensuring faster performance, higher security, and improved services using integrated digital solutions.
4- Developing the Makran and Arvand regions with an endogenous and exogenous approach with the aim of becoming a center for international production, trade and tourism exchanges.
5- Control and transfer of common and border waters, dredging of the Arvand River, and development of coastal cities and villages, observing the principles of coastal planning and development.
6- Developing production and business clusters with the aim of attracting foreign capital and developing export markets.
7- Development of the oil and gas exploration and extraction chain, petrochemical refineries and downstream petrochemical industries
8- Smartening and achieving the capability of injecting satellites into geostationary orbits
B- In order to expand the export of technical knowledge and technical services, design, engineering, and contracting of the country, with priority given to the industrial chain and mining industries, as well as to prevent raw material sales and complete the value chain and the economic leap approach, and in line with the development and promotion of the role and position of the mining and mining industries sector in the development of the country, the government is required to take the following measures during the implementation of the program:
۱–
1-1- Feasibility study and identification of target countries for the export of technical knowledge and technical services, design and engineering, and contracting, and the exchange of agreements for the development of cooperation in the mining and mineral industries sector, including exploration, exploitation, and processing.
2-1- Issuance of insurance policies and guarantees in the name of the exporter of technical knowledge transfer, design, engineering and contracting services by insurance companies, guarantee funds and the Iranian Export Guarantee Fund for exporters to export target countries.
3-1- Defining and providing special consular services to the aforementioned companies by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, as well as signing and exchanging cooperation agreements with export target countries.
4-1- Identifying and supporting Iranian companies with special capabilities to play an innovative role in the international arena and providing the opportunity for Iranian companies with the necessary capabilities to export technical knowledge and technical services, design and engineering, contracting, and manufacturing mining equipment and machinery in the international arena, including international exhibitions and global markets.
The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to submit a performance report of this component to the Parliament every six months.
2- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade (the National Geology and Mineral Exploration Organization) is required to publish all basic geological information (including geological, geochemical, geophysical and aerial maps) and, in compliance with Articles (13) and (17) of Chapter 4 of the Law on Publication and Free Access to Information approved on 6/11/1387, the contents of exploration reports of areas and zones at the end of the first year of the program and make them available to the public online. Also, all ministries, institutions, organizations and departments that take action to produce basic geological information are required to deliver all their produced information to this organization in accordance with the standards of the National Geology and Mineral Exploration Organization within the specified period.
The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to submit a report on the progress of this component and the level of cooperation of all relevant ministries, institutions, organizations and agencies, such as the Ministry of Oil and the Atomic Energy Organization of Iran, to the Parliament's Industries and Mines Commission every six months.
Note: Security issues must be observed when providing the aforementioned information to the Geological and Mineral Exploration Organization of the country.
3- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to determine the country's mining hubs in order to exercise its sovereignty and supervisory role over the exploration, extraction and processing of minerals in the country and to plan mineral development in these hubs after approval by the Supreme Council for Spatial Planning, in compliance with laws and regulations, needs assessment and the manner of conducting exploration operations, design and planning of production and mining operations, needs assessment and design of educational, research, technological and engineering consulting services.
4- The Iranian Mines and Mineral Industries Development and Renovation Organization (IMIDRO) and its subsidiaries are permitted to engage in “financial and technical partnerships in areas with exploration licenses, including exploration licenses from promising areas,” with the private sector that has financial and technical qualifications in accordance with the rules and regulations.
5- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is obliged to bring the average depth of mineral reserves exploration to the average global depth of exploration by taking the necessary measures and strategies, in compliance with the law on maximum use of the country's production and service capacity, supporting Iranian goods, and also through the transfer of technical knowledge and technology.
6- In order to achieve balanced development, sustainable employment, benefit the people of the region, and prevent migration within the mining area, the government is required to take the necessary measures to prioritize the use of local human resources and local companies. During the implementation of the program, in its mining plans and sub-plans (projects), and under equal conditions, it shall give priority to local contractors who are qualified for the county and province, and shall employ its required personnel from the local people of the county where the activity is located, respectively, from the nearest location, and in the event that there is no labor force in the county where the activity is located, from the nearest counties in the province where the activity is located.
The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to submit a performance report of this component to the Social Commission of the Parliament every six months.
Note 1: In giving priority to the use of local human resources and local companies in the aforementioned matters, these individuals (local human resources and local companies) must meet the necessary qualifications.
Note 2 - The phrase "under equal conditions" in this section includes both "selection of the contractor" and "selection of the required personnel."
7- Article (43) of the Law on the Sixth Five-Year Plan for the Economic, Social and Cultural Development of the Islamic Republic of Iran shall be implemented in compliance with the provisions of this chapter.
8- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required, in cooperation with the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade, to formulate an investment plan for the development of the country's railway infrastructure by development organizations and the private sector, giving priority to transporting mineral cargo via railway in line with the production plans of the mining sector and mineral industries during the implementation of the plan.
The executive regulations of this section will be prepared jointly by the Ministries of Roads and Urban Development and Industry, Mines and Trade, including providing investment incentive packages for the private sector and prioritizing the provision of the required infrastructure through domestic construction capacities, in compliance with relevant laws, within three months of the entry into force of this law, and will be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Note: Investment incentive packages for the private sector do not include items such as tax exemptions that require legislation, and these packages must be implemented within the framework of laws.
9- In order to realize the value chain of the mining and petrochemical industries, to protect the environment, and to reduce the consumption of polymers in downstream petrochemical industries and complementary and packaging industries, the government is required to take the necessary measures, support, and incentives within the framework of relevant laws and regulations to identify, explore, process, exploit, and produce mineral raw materials that replace polymers during the implementation of the program.
10- Ministries and their subordinate organizations, government institutions, institutions, non-governmental public institutions and institutions, and government companies, including companies requiring mention or clarification of names, that possess mining areas and areas are required to take action within a maximum of one year from the entry into force of this law, including assignment, obtaining the necessary licenses and observing legal formalities, or participation, or submitting a written plan with a commitment to implement according to the presented plan. Otherwise, the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to revoke the relevant licenses after the expiration of the aforementioned period. In the case of pension funds, priority will be given to submitting a written plan with a commitment to act according to the plan.
The provisions of this clause do not include legal, correct, valid and enforceable contracts determining obligations that have not been violated by the obligor.
11- County development and construction cooperatives formed by the indigenous people of the region are given priority in issuing licenses through the portal for issuing licenses and legal assignments of mines under equal conditions. The instructions for this section are submitted to the Supreme Council of Mines for approval upon the proposal of the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade.
12- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required, in cooperation with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Iranian Chamber of Commerce, Industries, Mines and Agriculture, to take the necessary measures to identify extraterritorial and marine mineral reserves and plan for the exploitation of these mines during the implementation of the program.
The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to submit a performance report of this component to the Industries and Mines, National Security and Foreign Policy Committees of the Parliament every six months.
13- The Environmental Protection Agency and the Natural Resources and Watershed Management Organization are required to respond to inquiries related to development plans and investor plans for industrial, mining, and exploration projects within a maximum of two months, and in the event of rejection of the aforementioned reports and requests, they must inform the beneficiaries of the reasons in writing, transparently, and documented in accordance with the relevant laws and technical regulations, and provide operational solutions to resolve the issue. Failure by the aforementioned organizations to respond within the specified deadline shall constitute approval.
14- In order to realize the government's rights in the exploitation of mines, the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to plan in such a way that by the end of the first year of the program, it will be possible to accurately calculate the amount of extraction from mines using smart systems.
15- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is obliged, through the Iranian Mines and Mineral Industries Development and Renovation Organization (IMIDRO), in compliance with the Law on the Implementation of General Policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, to allocate from the funds in excess of the approved credit special profit of the government share, declared profit and surplus over the tax of the projected performance.
In the annual budget laws and within the ceiling of public budget resources each year and in compliance with the principle
The fifty-third (53) of the Constitution shall take action to invest in the infrastructure of the mining and mineral industries sector, the exploration, extraction and exploitation of rare and scarce mineral elements, and the completion of unfinished projects of mines and mineral industries.
C- In order to sustainably supply the electricity needed by industries and mines, especially during peak consumption and imbalances in the country:
1- Industrial, mining and agricultural units are allowed to design and implement electricity production or efficiency improvement projects. The Ministries of Power, Oil and Agricultural Jihad, and Industry, Mines and Trade are required to implement this decree using the infrastructure available to them, in return for receiving the relevant fee (after depositing it to the National Treasury), in such a way that the electricity produced or saved is made available to the aforementioned units or their contracting parties without any restrictions in accordance with the contract concluded with the Ministry of Power. It is prohibited to cut off the electricity of these units in proportion to the amounts they produce or save and to set a ceiling for these units in supplying electricity from this location. In implementing this section, it is essential to comply with Article (4) of the Law on Removing Obstacles to the Development of the Electricity Industry.
The executive regulations of this part shall be prepared by the Ministry of Energy within three months of the entry into force of this law, in coordination with the Ministries of Petroleum, Agricultural Jihad, and Industry, Mines, and Trade, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
2- The construction and development of renewable power plants by mine operators or their contractual parties within or adjacent to the mining area, up to twenty percent (20%) of the investment in the power plant (with the approval of the Ministry of Energy), is subject to the exemption referred to in Note (5) of Article (14) of the Mining Law approved on 27/2/1377 with subsequent amendments and additions during the implementation period.
D- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade, in cooperation with relevant agencies, is required to prepare a document called “National Strategy for Industrial Progress and Promotion of the Country’s Value Chains” based on the criteria of land planning and balanced development, rejecting raw material sales and completing chains, stimulating exports and disseminating new technologies, and relying on the country’s advantages and priorities, including the electrical and microelectronic industries, automotive manufacturing with priority to electric and electric-gasoline (hybrid) vehicles, machine building and equipment manufacturing, downstream oil, gas and petrochemical industries, mining with priority to copper and rare earth elements, engineering, textile and clothing services, and recycling, along with obtaining the opinions of the Chambers of Commerce, Industries, Mines and Agriculture of Iran, Iranian Cooperatives, and Iranian Guilds, within the framework of the requirements and through legal procedures, and submit it for approval by the Council of Ministers within three months of the entry into force of this law.
This document is the basis for all government decisions, approvals, regulations, and circulars during the implementation of the program, and the establishment of any regulations contrary to it is prohibited. Also, all tax, tariff, banking facilities, and land transfers are stipulated in this document within the framework of the laws.
The provisions of this clause include amendments to the aforementioned document by the authority that issued it, except for amendments to that document within the framework of laws and at most once a year in the Council of Ministers.
Note 1- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required, in coordination and agreement with the Ministry of Oil, based on the aforementioned document, to review and implement all licenses issued in the field of petrochemical industry (especially methanol, urea and polyethylene production) and mineral industries (especially steel) that have not been put into operation by the end of 1403 due to reasons beyond its control, within the framework of this law and in accordance with the capacities of food supply, infrastructure supply, considerations of the National Land Planning Document, economy and economic feasibility, by the end of Shahrivar 1404 at the latest. Also, the Ministries of Oil and Power are required to issue licenses for the supply of food, energy and allocation of water to economic enterprises during the implementation period until the start of operation, on a timely basis and subject to operation within the specified schedule. Extension of these licenses will be permitted only based on the law and regulations.
Note 2- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to develop, in coordination with the Ministry of Interior, the Ministry of Agricultural Jihad and cooperation with other executive agencies in charge of production and employment plans and the Chambers of Commerce, Industries, Mines and Agriculture of Iran, the Chamber of Cooperatives of Iran and the Chamber of Guilds of Iran, based on the aforementioned document, a roadmap for the advantageous economic chains of the provinces in proportion to the local capacities and advantages and the role of the provinces in the national value chains, within two years of the entry into force of this law, and to approve it in the Supreme Council for Land Planning. The National Secretariat for the Management of the Advantageous Provincial Economic Chains shall be established in one of the relevant ministries and its provincial secretariats in the governorates, using the available facilities and forces, as determined by the President.
The organization and the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade are required to submit a report on the performance of this note to the Parliament's Industries and Mines Commission every six months.
Note 3 - All permits and needs assessments contained in this law are subject to Article (7) of the Law on the Implementation of General Policies, Article Forty-Four (44) of the Constitution.
E- In order to ensure coherent, transparent regulation and streamline regulations related to production chains, including raw and semi-raw materials and final products, the following measures will be taken:
1- Within the framework of the Law on the Implementation of General Policies, Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, especially Article (59) thereof, the Competition Council is obliged to take the necessary steps to establish at least three regulatory bodies in the priority areas of the aforementioned law by the end of the second year of the program. The government is obliged to take the necessary legal steps immediately after receiving the Competition Council’s proposal. If the implementation of this provision requires changes in the statutes and other laws related to the executive agencies, the government is obliged to take legal measures, including determining the duties of all relevant agencies, within the aforementioned period.
2- In order to develop employment and economic growth through private and cooperative sector investment:
1-2- Government pricing is prohibited, with the exception of subsidized basic goods, exclusive goods and services, and government services.
This ruling governs Article (21) of the Law on the Addition of Certain Articles to the Law on the Regulation of Part of Government Financial Regulations (2) during the implementation of the program.
Note 1- Subsidized basic goods are goods that have received a direct foreign exchange or rial subsidy, such as direct payment of part of the price of the goods by the government.
Note 2- Exclusive goods and services are only goods and services whose markets have been recognized by the Competition Council as examples of exclusive markets.
Note 3 - Government goods and services are goods and services that the government is the sole supplier of, and whose production and supply are under the ownership and control of the government, and the profits from their sale are directly at the disposal of the government.
2-2- In order to improve the performance and focus of the Competition Council on the use of various tools and with the aim of increasing the competitiveness of businesses in Iran, the Competition Council is required to determine instances and approve price regulation guidelines only in the case of markets subject to natural monopoly, the amount and conditions of access to the market of monopoly goods and services in each case.
3- During the implementation of the program, for those investment projects that begin their operations or are put into operation during the years of the program, it is prohibited to impose any taxes or impose new fees or new regulations that create restrictions on the activities of the investment projects subject to this law, except by a vote of two-thirds of the representatives present in the parliament. The government is obliged to determine the method of pricing energy or feed rates and other government-owned inputs used in these projects by concluding contracts for at least five years. Changing these rates is prohibited in addition to annual budget laws or other laws.
C- The Ministry of Petroleum is authorized to allocate the step-wise feed rate discounts referred to in Subsection (3) of Note (B) of Article (1) of the Subsidies Targeting Law, Amended 4/12/1393, to investors with long-term contracts throughout the downstream oil and gas value chain using feed-based “settlement bonds.” These bonds will be used to settle feed costs at face value only and will not be convertible.
The executive regulations of this clause, including the method of implementation, the method of distributing incentives in different parts of the value chain, and other regulations, will be prepared by the Ministry of Petroleum in cooperation with the Ministries of Industry, Mines and Trade, and Economic Affairs, Finance, and Organization within three months of the entry into force of this law and will be approved by the Council of Ministers.
G- In order to support and strengthen the development organizations subject to Article (5) of the Law on Removing Barriers to Competitive Production and Improving the Country's Financial System, as amended on 10/11/1395, with its subsequent amendments and additions, the following measures shall be taken:
1- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to deposit seventy percent (70%) of the funds from any type of transfer of shares and shares of affiliated and subsidiary companies of development organizations into the accounts of these organizations in order to participate with the non-governmental sector for the economic development of less developed areas, infrastructure development, completion of unfinished projects, performance of governance duties in new areas with advanced and high-risk technology, and preparation of enterprises for transfer, while observing the treasury turnover, in accordance with the law on the implementation of general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution. The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to consider the resources from the transfers subject to this section that have not yet been deposited into the accounts of development organizations as receivables of these organizations.
2- During the implementation of the program, the provisions related to the investment of development organizations shall be implemented solely within the framework of their founding law and statutes, the law implementing general policies, Article (44) of the Constitution, and this law, unless subsequent laws stipulate the repeal or amendment of the founding law and statutes of the aforementioned organizations.
3- The Iranian Mines and Mineral Industries Development and Renovation Organization is allowed to record the economic value of the mining exploitation licenses in its possession as assets and equity.
4- Executive agencies are allowed to use the technical and credit assistance referred to in paragraph "l" of Article (28) of the Law on the Addition of Certain Articles to the Law on the Regulation of Part of the Government's Financial Regulations (2) to increase the capital of the legal funds under their jurisdiction and to spend it proportionately through these funds in line with the objectives of the technical and credit assistance.
H- In order to enhance the position of small industries and industrial clusters in economic growth, the following measures will be taken:
1- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade (the specialized parent company of the Small Industries and Industrial Towns Organization of Iran) is authorized, as the case may be, in cooperation with the Ministries of Cultural Heritage, Tourism and Handicrafts, Communications and Information Technology, and Agricultural Jihad, the Environmental Protection Organization, and municipalities and rural districts, within the framework of the comprehensive urban and rural master plan, to establish specialized towns, areas, and complexes within urban and rural boundaries in the fields of information technology (IT), creative industries, handicrafts, manufacturing and service guilds, clean industries, and industrial waste.
2- The National Industrial Cluster Development Plan, in line with the national strategy for industrial progress and the promotion of the country's value chains, and including principles, processes, structure, goals, resources, institutional division of labor, and statistics, and the removal of obstacles to the development of industrial clusters and businesses, shall be prepared within the first year of the plan upon the proposal of the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers within the framework of the laws.
3- The “Small Industries Investment Guarantee Fund” will be changed to the “Small Industries Investment Support Fund” with the duties of granting facilities through credit institutions and issuing guarantees and insurance policies. The statute of this fund will be prepared at the proposal of the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade within three months from the date of entry into force of this law and will be approved by the Council of Ministers. The resources of this fund will be provided through a part of the revenues obtained from the implementation of Article (37) of the Law on Removing Barriers to Competitive Production and Improving the Country’s Financial System in the form of annual budget bills and capital increase.
In order to develop and manage industrial towns and areas as best as possible and prevent the wastage of resources and capacities available in them:
1- Termination of inactive contracts and expropriation of idle lands, which must be carried out due to violation of contractual obligations as determined by the competent legal authorities, in industrial towns and areas in each province is the responsibility of a working group consisting of the CEO of the provincial industrial town company, a representative of the governor, and a representative of the provincial Chief Justice.
The executive regulations of this section shall be prepared by the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Note 1- Contracts in which the assignee has not committed a contractual breach leading to termination or revocation are not subject to the provisions of this clause.
Note 2 - The assignments of the Law on the Protection and Exploitation of Forests and Rangelands, approved by the National Assembly on 25/5/1346, with subsequent amendments and additions, to ministries, government agencies, public institutions, and government institutions belonging to the Public Treasury are valid.
2- Any development of existing units located in industrial towns and areas within those towns and areas shall be solely within the framework of the regulations of the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade and within the limits of the approvals obtained for that town or industrial area, and shall be exempt from obtaining other permits and inquiries subject to compliance with the laws at the discretion of the aforementioned Ministry.
D- In order to facilitate and remove obstacles and growth of production:
1- In the case of non-criminal legal cases related to production units, as well as in relation to claims under Article (50) of the Social Security Law, any seizure and confiscation of machinery, production tools, equipment and raw materials of production units, arrest and imprisonment of the CEO or members of the board of directors that, as determined by the provincial production facilitation and removal working group, leads to a halt in production, is prohibited until the verdict is finalized.
2- Importing machinery with state-of-the-art technology to replace worn-out machinery is permitted, provided that it is not manufactured domestically or there is a lack of domestic production capacity, after approval by the Knowledge-Based Technologies Steering Council, subject to the Knowledge-Based Production Leap Law. Also, units with a renovation and reconstruction license are exempt from customs duties on the import of the aforementioned machinery equivalent to the value of energy carriers saved by these units.
3- One-third of the share of the cooperative sector from the resources for implementing the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution shall be allocated in the form of annual budgets to increase the capital of the Cooperative Development Bank and the Cooperative Investment Guarantee Fund, solely for granting facilities and risk coverage to national comprehensive cooperatives, with priority given to cooperatives active in the field of agriculture or energy supply, and cooperatives in border areas of deprived areas, and to stimulate cross-border exports. The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance shall be obliged to deposit the resources related to the cooperative sector resulting from the transfer of state-owned companies in an account specifically for the cooperative sector in the treasury.
4- The Ministry of Energy is required to take steps to ensure that the export of electricity is possible at least ten percent (10%) of the electricity production of newly constructed renewable power plants in the non-governmental, private, and cooperative sectors and three percent (3%) of the electricity production of newly constructed thermal power plants in the non-governmental, private, and cooperative sectors by providing the required infrastructure (with the cost paid by the non-governmental, private, and cooperative sectors).
In the event that the Ministry of Energy prevents electricity exports in accordance with the conditions mentioned in Article (17) of the Law on Removing Obstacles to the Development of the Electricity Industry, this Ministry is obliged to pay the average import and export rate of electricity from its domestic resources to the above-mentioned power plants at the end of each year for each kilowatt-hour reduction in the share of electricity exports of the non-governmental, private and cooperative sectors. The organization is obliged to submit a report on the performance of the institutions covered by this section to the Parliament every six months.
5- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is authorized to establish a national platform for the distribution network of goods and products (including industrial, agricultural, and e-commerce) by providing the necessary infrastructure to enhance the security of postal services and carry out postal operations and support (logistics) processes, and with the participation of postal operators and other activists in the field of transportation and distribution of goods, and to carry out the necessary organization for the popularization of distribution, subject to the non-entrepreneurship with the full agency of the private and public sectors. In this regard, the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology (National Postal Company of the Islamic Republic of Iran) is required to establish a portal for issuing a unique postal ID based on the sender's and recipient's postal ID (code) and shipping specifications on the platform in accordance with the National Data and Information Management Law.
6- The government is required to take the necessary legal action in preparing annual budget bills to allocate a credit line for buyers of Iranian knowledge-based products in target countries, in compliance with the seventy-seventh (77), eightieth (80), and one hundred and twenty-fifth (125) principles of the Constitution.
7- Products of petrochemical companies that have not been pre-sold and for which there is no commitment to export them, with the consent of their owners and the supervision of the relevant development organization in the Ministry of Oil, should be allocated as raw materials to downstream complexes or units along the petrochemical value chain, in the form of long-term contracts.
The executive regulations of this section, including incentives commensurate with the increase in production throughout the value chain, will be prepared by the Ministry of Petroleum in coordination with the Ministries of Industry, Mines and Trade, Economic Affairs, Finance and Organization, within a maximum of three months from the entry into force of this law, and will be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Chapter 11 – Housing Development
Article 49 – The government is required to take the following measures in implementing paragraph (9) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and in order to achieve the following quantitative goals in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:
Table No. (12) - Quantitative objectives of housing development performance indicators
Performance measure	One known	A quantitative goal at the end of the program
Strategic	Access to housing	Year	۷.۵
The extent of reduction in the area of 
worn and inefficient urban fabric	Percentage	۲۰
Industrial building production	Percentage	۱۵
Operational	Construction of urban housing	One thousand units	۱.۵۰۰
Construction of rural housing	One thousand units	۱.۰۰۰
Renovation of dilapidated and inefficient urban fabric buildings	One thousand units	۵۰۰
Other types of housing construction	One thousand units	۲.۰۰۰
The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit a report on housing development performance indicators to the parliament annually.
Supportive housing
Article 50 – In order to prepare and facilitate access to suitable housing, especially for qualified individuals, and in line with the quantitative and qualitative improvement of housing and in implementing the Housing Production Leap Law, the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to take the following measures during the implementation of the program:
A- Implement the program for the production and supply of supportive housing after approval by the Provincial Housing Council and then approval by the Supreme Housing Council, with the approach of supporting investment from the private, cooperative and non-governmental sectors, municipalities and other public non-governmental institutions and bodies within the framework of mutual agreements and using the approved support credit tools.
B- To provide land to eligible applicants for housing in government support plans, land under ownership attached to and within the boundaries of cities and land obtained under Articles (9), (10) and (12) of the Housing Production Growth Law shall be allocated to eligible applicants for housing construction after preparing urban development plans, implementing preparation plans and separating plots through the comprehensive housing support plan system based on Article (7) of the Housing Production Growth Law.
Note 1- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to plan and take action to add at least two-tenths of a percent (0.2%) of the land area to the country's residential capacity with a maximum density of sixty people per hectare, in villages, small and medium-sized cities, border areas, and settlements, in compliance with the land planning document, the Law on Preservation of Agricultural Land Use and Gardens, and Note (2) of Article (9) of the Housing Production Growth Law. In order to facilitate reverse migration of different segments of society, the five-year residence requirement will not be included in this transfer, and the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is authorized to make the transfer for 99 years.
Note 2 - Memorandums of Understanding and contracts for the support projects for dilapidated infrastructure, rural housing, and the National Housing Movement Project are not considered examples of contracts under Articles (38) and (41) of the Social Security Law and are subject to the provisions of Article (5) of the Social Insurance Law for Construction Workers, as amended on 22/6/1402.
C- Through an agreement with the owners of non-governmental lands without residential use, in compliance with Article (8) and Note (2) of Article (9) of the Housing Production Growth Law, the Law on Preservation of Agricultural Lands and Gardens, and the Land Use Planning Document, take action to provide land for the implementation of housing construction support projects or the construction of residential settlements by the private, cooperative, and public non-governmental sectors, with priority given to people's cooperatives, and in compliance with the regulations of the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development, including compliance with urban per capita rates and the provision of required infrastructure and superstructure services, and other laws and regulations.
The executive regulations of this clause, including the scope of application and the method of reaching an agreement with non-state land owners based on the added value resulting from the change in use, increase in density and occupancy level, and the like, shall be approved by the Council of Ministers within six months of the entry into force of this law by the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development, and after approval by the Supreme Council of Urban Development and Architecture of Iran.
Note - During the implementation of the program, in order to provide organizational housing needed by armed and security forces personnel, with priority given to border and deprived operational areas:
1- The General Staff of the Armed Forces of the Islamic Republic of Iran is authorized to provide the land required for the annual construction of ten thousand organizational housing units. The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is also required to change the use of the introduced lands in accordance with the detailed plan and land use planning, in compliance with other laws and regulations.
2- The government is authorized to provide land, necessary support, and infrastructure needed to construct one hundred thousand organizational housing units for the Islamic Republic of Iran Police Command Forces (FARACA) free of charge and to foresee the necessary resources in the annual budget.
3- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is authorized to provide the land required for the construction of at least three thousand organizational housing units for the Ministry of Intelligence, free of charge.
4- The Central Bank is required to determine the quota for payment of bank facilities required for the above institutional houses and to supervise its payment by the operating banks from the facilities of the Housing Production Leap Law.
5- The Islamic Republic of Iran Police Command (FARACA) is authorized, in coordination with the Central Bank, to make deposits to receive low-interest facilities from the facilities of the Housing Production Growth Law.
Note 3: The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to provide free land for the construction of Basij constituencies and areas, and radio and television stations in housing and urban regeneration support projects.
D- In order to plan the provision of per capita public and urban services such as cultural, sports, educational spaces and urban parks in settlements and population centers on the outskirts of cities and worn-out and inefficient urban textures, the government is allowed to transfer unused or barren lands belonging to itself or affiliated organizations and institutions to municipalities for the creation of urban public spaces and use in the aforementioned uses, while maintaining the ownership of the government. Municipalities are required to create urban spaces for public use from their own resources within a maximum of three years. The government is also allowed to exchange the aforementioned lands for the government's debt to the relevant municipality after exploitation at the regional price at the time of transfer and the type of use used.
Th-
1- Calculation and collection of annexation fees, change of use, or service share received by owners whose lands are annexed to the city limits in the form of revision plans or on a case-by-case basis to comprehensive, guiding, and detailed city plans by the Provincial Planning and Development Council or the Supreme Council of Urban Planning and Architecture of Iran; in the event of no land separation, it shall be done solely based on Note (4) of the Single Article of the Law on Determining the Status of Real Estate Located in Government and Municipal Plans, approved on 29/8/1367, and in the event of land separation, it shall be done solely based on Article (101) of the Municipal Law, approved on 11/4/1334, with subsequent amendments and additions.
In municipal reorganization plans and special plans where lands with different uses are converted to residential and separated, the fees for the conversion of use or the share of services received by municipalities are calculated and collected solely based on Article (101) of the Municipal Law.
2- If, for the implementation of housing production projects, government lands of other agencies or non-government agricultural and garden lands are entered into the city limits by the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development after obtaining the approval of the Supreme Council of Urban Development and Architecture of Iran and within its framework, in compliance with Note (2) of Article (9) of the Housing Production Leap Law, only all road networks plus a percentage of the land area shall be transferred to the municipality in accordance with existing laws without the need to pay any fees for change of use, service share, separation or entry into the area. In this case, the provision of all services and infrastructure is the responsibility of the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development and the government. The share of the owners who make their lands available to the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development for this purpose is a net percentage of the land with residential use, the method of its implementation shall be notified in accordance with the regulations prepared by the Ministry of the Interior in cooperation with the Ministries of Roads and Urban Development and Justice within the framework of the laws and approved by the Council of Ministers. Land annexed to city limits by the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is exempt from paying fees under the Law on the Preservation of Agricultural Land Use and Gardens, approved on 31/3/1995, with subsequent amendments.
Note 1: Endowments are treated in accordance with their respective regulations.
Note 2: Individuals may appeal to the judicial authorities regarding the share subject to this clause.
3- In the case of annexing state and non-state lands with different uses to the boundaries of villages, fees related to the Law on the Preservation of Agricultural Land Use and Gardens are not collected.
The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit an annual performance report on this article to the Parliament.
Rural housing
Article 51 – In order to develop, develop and prosper the country’s villages and in line with identifying and exploiting the existing capacities in rural areas, improving the situation, promoting social status, income level and quality of rural life and the status of villages, employment and production, constructing rural housing for the deprived, especially youth and young couples living in villages, creating sustainable livelihoods and perpetuating the population, paving the way for reverse migration to villages, expanding access to services and creating a platform for the prosperity and progress of justice-oriented and balanced villages, the following measures shall be taken:
A- In order to focus on the affairs of villages and tribes, increase the population of villages and distribute the population proportionately among them, reverse migration, boost production, diversify production by creating a supply and value chain, and create a production infrastructure, and provide a sustainable livelihood and income for villagers and tribes, and enhance their role in the national economy, progress and development, and eliminate poverty and deprivation from villages and tribal communities, and improve their quality of life, and achieve justice and revive the Jihadist culture with capable, responsible, and accountable management, the Ministry of Agricultural Jihad is required to take legal action on the following matters by the end of the second year of the program:
1- The "Organization of Iranian Nomadic Affairs" will be changed to the "Organization for the Progress and Development of Villages and Nomadic Affairs" and its provincial units will also be subject to the same decree.
2- All units with tasks related to the aforementioned objectives shall be withdrawn from other headquarters units of the Ministry of Agricultural Jihad and its functions and transferred to the organization subject to subsection (1) of this clause.
Note - The Islamic Revolution Housing Foundation, based on its legal duties and statutes, takes action, as appropriate, to secure land, construct and transfer livelihood-oriented housing, and review guiding plans and improve villages within the limits of national, provincial, and county resources and within the framework of annual budgets and internal resources.
B- Rural master plans and determination of village boundaries throughout the country are prepared by the County Housing Foundation Office based on the criteria approved by the Supreme Council of Urban Planning and Architecture of Iran and are reviewed and approved by a committee consisting of the Deputy Governor for Development (committee chairman), the Director General of the Provincial Housing Foundation (secretary), a representative of the Provincial Roads and Urban Development Department, a representative of the Provincial Agricultural Jihad Organization, a representative of the Provincial Environmental Protection Department, the County Governor, the Director of the County Housing Foundation, the relevant district prefect, and the head of the Islamic Village Council (supervisor) and the village headman (supervisor).
C- The Islamic Revolution Housing Foundation is required, in proportion to the size of the household and in compliance with Note (2) of Article (9) of the Housing Production Leap Law, to construct livelihood-oriented rural housing (for residence and economic and productive activities) by creating the necessary infrastructure and reviewing the scope of the guiding plans for landless villages and approving them in the relevant authorities, to transfer land to applicants without housing, with priority given to indigenous people (born in the village or with at least two years of residence history) for permanent residence in the form of a 99-year lease or definitive transfer. The executive regulations of this clause are prepared by the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development in cooperation with the Islamic Revolution Housing Foundation and are subject to approval by the Council of Ministers.
The Islamic Revolution Housing Foundation is required to submit an annual performance report on this section to the Parliament's Civil Engineering Committee.
D- The Islamic Revolution Housing Foundation is required to upload spatial information about the villages' boundaries into the Land Management Unit's window system by the end of the third year of the program, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law, and to submit a report on the performance of this section to the parliament every six months.
E- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required, in cooperation with the Islamic Revolution Housing Foundation, to improve and renovate at least two hundred thousand rural housing units annually by paying low-cost facilities and with an interest rate of five percent (5%) within the framework of Article (4) of the Law on Housing Production and Provision of the Difference in Facility Interest for the Period of Civil Participation and Installment Sales at the Approved Facility Interest Rate from the National Housing Fund. The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development and the Central Bank are required to submit a report on the performance of this clause to the Parliament every six months.
Housing in dilapidated and inefficient urban fabric
Article 52–
A- In order to encourage owners to participate in the renovation of dilapidated structures in the process of turning over dilapidated structures into new units or lands under their ownership, the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is authorized to apply a discount of up to forty percent (40%) on the expert price of the newly built units or the lands being exchanged, in compliance with the laws, or to price the lands or residential units located in dilapidated structures up to forty percent (40%) higher than the expert price.
The implementing regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development within three months of the entry into force of this law and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
B- All the supportive provisions and privileges of the Housing Production Leap Law apply to housing renovation in approved urban regeneration areas (worn and inefficient structures) up to five construction units per worn property lot.
Note - The government is authorized to take legal action regarding the generalization of the protective provisions and privileges of the Housing Production Growth Law to housing renovation within approved regeneration areas.
C- To encourage investors from the non-governmental, private, and cooperative sectors in new construction projects for local, tourism, cultural, educational, and sports industries in approved urban regeneration areas (worn and inefficient structures), legal action should be taken to apply exemptions and legal privileges for investment in deprived and less developed areas.
D- Housing renovation permits in approved urban regeneration areas (worn and inefficient structures) are issued by municipalities outside of the turn and within a maximum of three months of the applicant's request. While maintaining all branches prior to renovation, new branches are established with priority.
E- The provisions and privileges of approved urban regeneration areas (worn and inefficient structures) shall apply to the lands and properties immediately adjacent to and within these approved urban regeneration areas (worn and inefficient structures) which are used to implement compensated housing projects or provide services in these areas.
Note - The government is authorized to take legal action regarding the extension of the provisions and privileges of approved urban regeneration areas to lands and properties immediately adjacent to and adjacent to approved urban regeneration areas.
C- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required, in cooperation with the Ministry of Interior and municipalities, to identify all unsafe, critical and high-risk buildings of executive agencies in metropolitan cities and provincial centers through the Roads, Housing and Urban Development Research Center and the Fire and Safety Services Organization by the end of the first year of the program, and to make them safe by the owner or operator agencies by the end of the third year of the program.
The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit an annual performance report on this article to the Parliament.
Other manufacturing methods
Article 53 – In order to facilitate the construction of housing by the people, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to produce and store information on all comprehensive and detailed plans of metropolitan cities in digital form (digitization) by the end of the first year of the program, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law in the Comprehensive and Detailed Plans System, as well as to electronicize the process of obtaining permits related to the Supreme Council of Architecture and Urban Planning of Iran and the provincial commissions, Article (5) of the Law on the Establishment of the Supreme Council of Architecture and Urban Planning of Iran, amended on 31/3/1390. In the case of other cities, action must also be taken by the end of the third year of the program. Since the launch of this system, all approvals of the council and the aforementioned commissions are uploaded and announced online and immediately in the aforementioned system and can be implemented only after being uploaded to the aforementioned system. The implementation of comprehensive and detailed plans is periodically monitored and monitored through this system, and its performance report is published publicly, with priority given to metropolitan cities.
B- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to take the necessary legal action to amend the Building Pre-Sale Law approved on 12/10/1389 by the end of the second year of the program.
C- The National Land and Property Registration Organization and the authorities issuing construction completion certificates are required to issue a construction completion certificate for each unit of the building, a report of the separation of apartments (common areas), and a separate ownership document, if the issuance of a completion certificate for a building is subject to payment of a fine or debt, pursuant to a ruling by the Commission of Article (100) of the Municipality Law or other competent authorities. For each unit of that building that has paid the fine for the private parts determined by the Commissions subject to Articles (99) and (100) of the Municipality Law and the share of the building unit from the fine for the common parts (in proportion to the private area) determined by the said Commissions.
The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit a report on the performance of clauses "A", "B", and "C" of this article to the Civil Engineering Commission and the Deputy for Oversight of the Parliament every six months.
D- The specialized parent company for the development of new cities is allowed to participate, from its internal resources, in providing the resources needed to build freeways, highways, and urban-suburban railways inside and outside the boundaries of new cities (without establishing a new company and solely for connection to its parent city).
E- In order to support people without housing in all housing support projects, all stages of real estate documents in the name of the government or bank, subject to its provision in the annual budget, are exempt from the scope of Articles (123) and (124) of the Law on Registration of Documents and Real Estate, amended on 15/8/1384, and related regulations.
Providing financial resources
Article 54 – In order to provide part of the financial resources needed for the preparation, provision of infrastructure and superstructure services, and construction of supportive housing in the National Housing Movement and Housing, the subject of the Law on the Protection of the Family and Youth of the Population:
one thousand-
1- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is authorized to transfer part of the lands owned and in its possession, in accordance with the approved technical and economic justification plan, including the necessary technical specifications, including the number of residential units and the required urban per capita, through auctions in compliance with legal procedures, to investors, developers, mass builders, and non-governmental public institutions for the construction of housing, in the form of sale or lease or transfer of ownership after the land lease period. The resources obtained from it, after being deposited in the treasury, are deposited in the account of the National Housing Fund or are made available to this ministry in the form of ready-made residential units on the same lands. The definitive transfer of land ownership is conditional on construction within a certain schedule, and the urban infrastructure and per capita of the town are provided within the framework of the approvals of the Supreme Council of Architecture and Urban Development of Iran. At least five percent (5%) of the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development's share stated in the aforementioned contracts or its equivalent must be allocated through the Imam Khomeini Relief Committee (RA), the National Welfare Organization, and the Islamic Revolution Housing Foundation for supportive housing in cities and villages in accordance with the regulations that are prepared upon the proposal of the Ministry of Cooperation, Labor, and Social Welfare in cooperation with the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development, the Imam Khomeini Relief Committee (RA), the National Welfare Organization, and the Islamic Revolution Housing Foundation, and approved by the Council of Ministers.
Note - The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to foresee in the concluded contracts the condition of termination of the contract in case of delay in construction exceeding the specified limits and in case of unauthorized delay, to take action to reclaim the land, settle the expenses incurred at the current price and reassign it. The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit the performance report of this component to the Parliament annually.
2- In order to achieve the goals of this law and the Housing Production Leap Law and to provide part of the financial resources for housing development projects, the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is authorized, within the framework of annual budgets for housing projects for the disadvantaged, to exchange lands and properties under its ownership, after applying value addition, with the definitive demands of the contractors party to the aforementioned contracts.
3- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is authorized to provide part of the lands under its ownership and control to Bank Maskan by transferring ownership through its affiliated companies and organizations within the approved budget ceiling. The equivalent of the current valuation value of these lands shall be considered as an increase in the government's capital in Bank Maskan. Bank Maskan is obligated to make these lands productive within a maximum of three years from the time of transfer in order to increase the provision of facilities in the implementation of the Housing Production Growth Law. In case of failure to make these lands productive within the stipulated time, the aforementioned assets shall be returned to the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development at the current valuation value.
The executive regulations of this clause, including the method of evaluating and increasing the value of lands and properties, will be prepared by the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development, in cooperation with the organization and the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance, within three months of the entry into force of this law, and will be approved by the Council of Ministers.
B- If the operating banks do not fulfill the definitive obligations they have as per the notification of the Central Bank in relation to Article (4) of the Housing Production Growth Law, the Central Bank is obliged to reduce the growth of the balance sheet of the offending bank by the amount of the definitive obligations not fulfilled, in compliance with the law of the Central Bank of the Islamic Republic of Iran, and add the equivalent to the growth of the balance sheet of other banks that are not in arrears, with priority given to the Housing Bank. The Central Bank is obliged to announce to the Parliament every three months a report on the performance of credit institutions regarding the provision of housing construction facilities.
Improving productivity
Article 55 – In order to improve the quality and reduce the costs of housing construction, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to implement at least fifteen percent (15%) of the housing supply programs by the end of the program using modern technologies, industrialization (prefabricated and modular), and smart construction compatible with the country's climate and texture, with priority given to the construction of residential towns, mass construction, and the development of new cities. The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit a report on the performance of this clause to the Civil Engineering Commission and the Deputy for Oversight of the Parliament every six months.
B- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is responsible for reviewing the identity card.
The Civil Engineering Department should take action for all newly constructed buildings, as well as establish and manage its electronic issuance system in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law, so that it is possible to grade newly constructed buildings and developments in two categories: construction quality and energy efficiency, in four categories.
The phased completion of the technical-civil identity card is mandatory from the beginning of obtaining the construction permit and during the preparation of phase reports by supervising engineers until the issuance of the final work. Municipalities are required to refrain from issuing the final work for buildings without a technical-civil identity card approved by the National Construction Engineering System Organization and, as the case may be, refer the construction violation case to the Commission for Articles (99) and (100) of the Municipality Law and the violation of the engineering system supervisors to the Disciplinary Council of the National Construction Engineering System Organization for determination of responsibility.
From the date this law comes into effect, employees of executive agencies are not allowed to act as executors or representatives of executors in the construction process of buildings.
The executive regulations of this section, including the duties of the agencies, technical, executive and building supervision factors, the processes for preparing and issuing the building's technical-civil identity certificate, and the rules and criteria for industrialization and energy efficiency, will be prepared within three months of the entry into force of this law, upon the proposal of the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development and in cooperation with the Ministries of Interior, Oil and Power, Organization, the Construction Engineering System Organization, and the Supreme Council of Provinces, and will be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Note - The provisions of this paragraph only include cases for which licenses are issued after the effective date of this law.
C- The provincial construction engineering system organizations are required to introduce to the Social Security Organization, upon request, real members with professional licenses and no insurance. In order to support construction engineering professionals, the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development's share of the aforementioned insurance premium is twenty percent (20%), in addition to three percent (3%) of mandatory unemployment insurance, the government's share and the professional's share are seven percent (7%). The basis for calculating the aforementioned insurance premium is based on the minimum wage announced by the Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare. The sources for providing the government's share are provided by increasing the tariffs subject to Article (39) of the Construction Engineering and Control System Law approved on 12/22/1374.
The executive regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development in cooperation with the Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers. The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development shall be required to submit an annual report on the performance of this clause to the Civil Affairs Commission of the Parliament.
Chapter 12 – Transit and the Maritime Economy
Article 56 – Action shall be taken to implement paragraphs (10) and (11) of the general policies of the Seventh Plan and to achieve the following quantitative objectives in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:
Table (13) – Quantitative targets for transit and maritime economy performance indicators
