The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit a report on the performance indicators of transit and the maritime economy of this article to the Parliament annually.
Transit Management
Article 57 – In order to regulate and create coherence in the management of international transit and logistics, and with the aim of creating mutual and strong economic linkages between countries through Iran and active presence and increased participation in regional and trans-regional value chains based on the relative advantages of different regions of the country and Iran’s new economic advantages, as referred to in Article (48) of this law, the following measures shall be taken during the implementation of the program:
A- The “National Headquarters for Border-to-Border Transit” shall be established as the coordinator and responsible for the field of transit and logistics, headed by the President (and in his absence, the First Vice President) and with the membership of the Ministers of Economic Affairs and Finance, Industry, Mines and Trade, Interior, Oil, Foreign Affairs, Roads and Urban Development, Defense and Support of the Armed Forces, and the Police Command of the Islamic Republic of Iran, the head of the organization, and one observer member from the Civil Affairs Commission elected by the Parliament. The secretariat of this headquarters shall be established in the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development, and the Minister of Roads and Urban Development shall be the secretary of the headquarters. Those duties of the Supreme Council for the Coordination of Transportation of the Country that deal with international transit and logistics shall be withdrawn from this Supreme Council and transferred to the National Headquarters for Border-to-Border Transit. The duties of this headquarters are as follows:
1- Policy-making and planning in all matters related to the field of international transit and logistics, including transportation, customs, banking, insurance, and fuel, and determining the relevant mandatory licenses and providing new incentives and support in compliance with the laws.
2- Preparation and approval of the "National Transit Program Document" in order to achieve the goals mentioned at the beginning of this article within a maximum of one year from the entry into force of this law.
This document includes designing regional and international multilateral initiatives and determining priorities for the development of transit corridors with a quantitative target of at least forty million tons of annual transit of goods through Iran over a five-year horizon.
3- Reforming international transit and logistics processes (software measures) including reviewing regulations (within the framework of laws and approvals of legal authorities, including the Council of Ministers) and existing procedures, eliminating unnecessary licenses and limiting the response time of related agencies, determining the criteria for the transit service information system regarding the possibility of tracking and ensuring the approximate delivery date of goods with the aim of increasing the desirability of transit corridors through Iran and accelerating transit processes.
4- Determining the method of managing infrastructure and process matters, as well as coordination between organizations and institutions located at air, sea, rail, and road border terminals, coordination between border terminals on both sides of the border, and coordination with the countries of origin and destination of transit goods.
B- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is designated as the custodian of the single window for integrated transit services at the country's entry and exit points. Executive agencies located at the entry and exit points, including military, law enforcement, security, and economic institutions, are required to provide their legal duties effectively and timely to applicants for the said services in the form of a single window in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law.
C- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is designated as the person responsible for civilian logistics in the country. The government is required to take legal action to determine the manner of issuing licenses for companies providing such services and related centers, the criteria, and the manner of dividing the work of the executive agencies.
D- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development, in compliance with the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, is authorized to:
1- In order to increase efficiency and improve service delivery, promote productivity, reduce government costs, and rationalize and streamline, transfer the management of the country's airports (including airports affiliated with executive agencies, with the exception of airports belonging to the armed forces) to the private and public sectors or domestic and foreign partnerships in the form of transferring the aforementioned management, with priority given to domestic airlines, while maintaining government ownership and continuing to provide air navigation services by the government, and respecting the legal rights of employees.
The executive regulations of this section shall be prepared by the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development and in cooperation with the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Note - The government is authorized to impose special extraordinary measures for the Civil Aviation Organization and other departments that govern and supervise airports in order to strengthen governance and supervision and to implement the provisions related to airports and airlines correctly and legally by strengthening and maintaining a committed and capable human resource.
This extraordinary decision is made using legal capacities, including clauses (5), (6), and (10) of Article (68) of the Civil Service Management Law.
2- In order to finance and develop infrastructure, improve the level of services, increase passenger and cargo traffic, and optimize airport management, take action to accept investment from the private sector or with the participation of foreign investors in return for the transfer of exploitation rights commensurate with the amount of investment, in compliance with Article 80 of the Constitution, and in compliance with Sharia and security regulations in the form of a legal contract.
3- In order to provide financial resources for the implementation of development projects and the improvement of airport services at international airports, passengers on foreign flights shall be charged an amount equivalent to 10 euros at the exchange rate per passenger, which shall be separately stated on the ticket and collected from the passengers, and shall be deposited into the relevant account in the National Treasury. Flights for pilgrimage purposes shall be exempt from this ruling.
4- Financing the purchase and lease of aircraft and helicopters from domestic and foreign sources in the form of facilities, in compliance with Article 80 of the Constitution, for Iranian airlines through various means, including the Transportation Development Fund and the National Development Fund. The government is also permitted to provide technical and credit assistance in the form of annual budgets in this regard.
E- In order to achieve the goals mentioned in Article (56) of this law in the field of railway transportation and to improve the productivity of this sector by attracting the participation of the non-governmental sector, the following measures shall be taken:
1- The Islamic Republic of Iran Railways Company is required to launch or transfer the defunct locomotives that have been idle for more than five years, whose renovation is economically viable, by the end of the second year of the program using public-private partnership methods.
2- The Ministry of Industry, Mine and Trade is required to issue import licenses for rail trucks, taking into account the annual domestic production capacity, in compliance with the Law on Facilitating the Issuance of Business Licenses for Vehicles Less Than 15 Years Old, with Priority Given to New Trucks. The executive regulations of this section shall be prepared by the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development in coordination with the Central Bank and in cooperation with the Ministry of Industry, Mine and Trade, taking into account the necessary legal incentives, including granting discounts on customs duties, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
3- The Islamic Republic of Iran Railways Company is required to run freight trains according to an origin-destination schedule and grant permits for the formation and operation of trains (complete trains) to the private, non-governmental, and cooperative sectors, so that by the end of the second year of the program, all freight trains in the country will run regularly and according to a schedule. The executive regulations of this component will be prepared upon the proposal of the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development and will be approved by the Council of Ministers. The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit a report on the performance of this component to the Civil Engineering Commission of the Parliament every six months.
C- In order to strengthen and improve the quality of passenger and cargo services of the country's air fleet:
1- The Civil Aviation Organization shall, within a maximum of six months from the entry into force of this law, review all previous guidelines and regulations related to the establishment, operation, management, and supervision of airlines, separately for cargo and passenger, in compliance with the laws, in the form of executive regulations, and after obtaining the approval of the Supreme Council of Civil Aviation, submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval.
2- Airlines are required to regulate and adapt their activities and services in accordance with the regulations referred to in subsection (1) of this paragraph. The Civil Aviation Organization is required to continuously monitor the activities and services of the above companies, assess the risks resulting from possible discrepancies, and notify these companies of corrective measures. After the expiration of the deadline specified in the aforementioned regulations, the continuation of the activities of unqualified companies is subject to the implementation of corrective measures and the achievement of the desired indicators, so that by the end of the third year of the program, these companies achieve the quality level specified in the aforementioned regulations through various means, including mergers, dissolutions, or expansion of services. The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit an annual report on the performance of this paragraph to the Parliament.
G- In order to increase the capacity of Imam Khomeini International Airport with the participation of domestic and foreign investors and to transform this airport into one of the regional hubs in the transportation and transit of international passengers and cargo, the government is required to take facilitating measures such as granting freedom of flight to foreign airlines on foreign routes along with determining competitive rates for fuel and airport and navigation services.
H- The Civil Aviation Organization is required to provide the necessary mechanisms for joint commercial cooperation between airlines in Iran through cooperation methods such as mergers or alliances, establishing codeshare flights, establishing a national clearing house between airlines, and other management and software measures.
X- The government is required to take legal action within a maximum of six months from the enactment of this law, with the aim of harmonizing and enhancing the effectiveness of economic policies in industrial, transportation, commercial, and land planning affairs, and enhancing the country's position in the global production and trade market, and increasing its share of regional and global value chains, based on the relative advantages of different regions of the country, towards the necessary policymaking for the integrated management of economic value chains and the development of a decision-support system for these chains, and to encourage and support the private sector in setting up value chains and processing, preparation, and support (logistics) centers, with priority given to deprived areas, while observing Islamic principles and security considerations.
Incentives and support
Article 58 – In order to increase the competitiveness of transit via Iran compared to competing routes, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The incentives and supports subject to the Law on the Development and Support of Maritime Industries, approved on 15/2/1387, will be restored and prescribed until the end of the program.
B- The Ministries of Oil, Roads and Urban Development, as appropriate, are required to work in cooperation with the Ministries of Industry, Mines and Trade, and Foreign Affairs, the Central Bank, and the Supreme Council of Free Trade-Industrial and Special Economic Zones to establish and develop export infrastructure such as offshore facilities, docking centers, and covered spaces to facilitate the export of Iranian goods and ensure the security of exporters.
The organization is required to submit an annual report to the Parliament on the performance of clauses "A" and "B" of this article, including the performance of each of the responsible agencies.
C- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to submit other incentives and supports to the Council of Ministers for approval and implementation after approval by the National Headquarters for Border-to-Border Transit in compliance with the laws, in order to increase the competitiveness of transit through the Iranian route compared to competing routes by reducing time and cost to achieve the goal mentioned in Article (56) of this law.
D- The Ports and Maritime Organization is permitted to enter into partnerships with reputable international companies (domestic and foreign) to form a company to invest in and operate major ports with international functions, in compliance with the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, the Law on the Implementation of General Policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution, and the Law on the Encouragement and Support of Foreign Investment, in order to establish a company to invest in and operate major ports with international functions. The share of the Ports and Maritime Organization and the domestic private sector is at least fifty-one percent (51%).
Infrastructure
Article 59–
A- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to prepare a schedule of tolls for compensation for damage caused to roads based on the amount of axle load and the amount of damage caused to the country's roads by various types of trucks and vans within the first six months of the program, and after approval by the Supreme Council for Transport Coordination, submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval.
B- In order to prevent the destruction of the country's roads due to excess capacity (tonnage) of transporting mineral products, all mines in the country are required to issue a bill of lading in coordination with the provincial General Directorate of Road Administration and Road Transport at the output of the production unit. The allocation of fuel quota to the fleet transporting the products of sand and salt mine production units is subject to obtaining a bill of lading and survey approval by the provincial General Directorate of Road Administration and Road Transport.
The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade, in cooperation with the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development, took legal action by the end of the first year of the program regarding how to compensate for damage to infrastructure and roads in various ways, including through the beneficiaries.
Note: Mines of radioactive materials are excluded from the scope of this clause.
C- The government is authorized to grant a license to import a bus or road tractor less than ten years old to the owner of the bus or tractor in exchange for scrapping any bus or road tractor that is more than twenty-five years old. The executive regulations of this clause shall be approved by the Council of Ministers, taking into account the necessary legal incentives, including granting discounts on customs duties.
D- The Supreme Council for the Coordination of Transportation and National Safety must approve the “Operational Program for Improving the Safety of the National Roads” within a maximum of six months from the entry into force of this law, in order to reduce by ten percent (10%) the annual number of fatalities resulting from traffic accidents on the country’s roads, as referred to in Subsection (3) of Clause “C” of Article (30) of the Law on Permanent Provisions on National Development Programs. All programs and measures in the field of national road safety and the budget required for them must be foreseen in the form of annual budget bills, and the Supreme Council for the Coordination of Transportation and National Safety is responsible for its management.
Maritime economy
Article 60 – In order to direct the population and water-bearing and export-oriented activities to the country's susceptible territories within the framework of land planning documents and integrated coastal management documents, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare is required to give priority to the active population in these areas in providing support and incentives for the creation or development of business plans and employment creation.
B- The Ministry of Energy is required to provide water for industries located in the southern coastal provinces of the country through the construction of desalination facilities, either directly or with the participation of the private sector.
C- The Ministries of Oil and Energy are required to sustainably supply the electricity and gas needed by industrial towns, refineries, petro-refineries, steel complexes, and fishing and aquaculture towns in these areas.
D- The Environmental Protection Organization is required to take action, in cooperation with Iranian fisheries research institutions and relevant executive agencies, to restore sensitive habitats, especially aquatic habitats containing endangered species.
E- The government is required to take the necessary legal action within three months of the entry into force of this law to transfer the right to exploit the area and create infrastructure, grant facilities, apply necessary exemptions and incentives on the southern and northern coasts and coastal backwaters to the provinces for the development of maritime-based economic activities.
The organization is required to submit an annual report on the performance of this article, including the performance of each of the responsible agencies, to the parliament.
Article 61–
A- The government is obliged to take action to maximize the activation of the diverse capacities of Abu Musa County in Hormozgan Province, focusing on the relevant islands, with an emphasis on establishing and providing superior services at the transnational, national and local levels, and taking into account the transportation system, logistics and commercial services, and the effective development of energy and communications infrastructure, industry and mining, and the creation and distribution of social services including higher education, healthcare, culture, and sports, and the identification and expansion of the capacity of tourism and residential areas and the sea-based economy. The organization and the Ministry of Interior are obliged to submit a report on the performance of this clause to the Parliament every six months.
B- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance, in cooperation with the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development, is required to take steps to ensure that customs activities are carried out 24/7 at the country's land borders and major and busy ports within six months of the law coming into force.
C- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required, in cooperation with the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade, to reform the port services tariff system within six months of the entry into force of this law and to establish the necessary mechanisms to make it competitive compared to regional ports within the framework of the laws.
Article 62 – In order to increase the country’s share of the market for providing fuel and ancillary services to ships (bunkering) in the Persian Gulf and the Sea of 
Oman, with priority given to the ports of Shahid Rajaee and Qeshm, to an annual fuel supply of at least five million tons along with ancillary services, the following measures will be taken during the implementation of the program:
A- The Ministry of Petroleum is required to produce and deliver half-percent (0.5%) low-sulfur fuel oil with an annual growth rate of twenty-five percent (25%) to companies providing ancillary services to ships (bunkering) and to facilitate the import and fuel procurement processes based on marine fueling standards.
Note - In order to sustainably supply fuel to applicants for the production of half-percent (0.5%) low-sulfur fuel oil, give priority to the allocation of export fuel oil to companies providing ancillary services to ships (bunkering), facilitate the import and procurement processes for marine fueling applications, and regulate the operations of fueling companies, the Ministry of Oil is required to prepare the required executive regulations in cooperation with the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development and submit them to the approval of the Council of Ministers.
B- The Ministry of Roads and Urban Development is required to transfer the right to exploit the land to the private and non-governmental sector, in compliance with the laws and regulations, for the construction of infrastructure for ancillary services to ships (bunkering).
The Ministries of Oil and Roads and Urban Development are required to submit a report on the performance of this article to the Parliament's Energy Commission every six months.
Article 63 – In order to increase the country’s fishery catch and promote the role and position of marine protein in the household food basket, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Ministries of Energy and Petroleum are required to provide water, electricity, and gas to fishing complexes up to their entrances, and the fuel needed to develop the offshore fishing fleet.
B- The Ministry of Agricultural Jihad is required, in cooperation with the Presidential Vice-President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy, to localize the equipment required for fish farming in cages and facilitate the necessary conditions for establishing fish and shrimp feed centers and fish reproduction.
Chapter 13 – Development of the National Information Network and Digital Economy
Article 64 - Action shall be taken to implement paragraphs (19) and (20) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and to achieve the following quantitative objectives in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:
Table No. (14) - Quantitative objectives of digital performance indicators
