The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to submit a report on the performance of digital performance indicators to the Parliament annually.
National Information Network
Article 65 – In order to increase access to the national information network, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to use the investment capacity and participation of the private sector, cooperatives and public institutions and to improve the economic model, to provide the possibility of connecting administrative, commercial and residential places in the cities of each province to the national information network through an access network based on optical fiber and high-speed access to villages with more than twenty households. The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to submit a report on the performance of this section to the Parliament every six months.
Note: The adjustment of tariffs for communications and information technology services, based on paragraph "c" of Article (5) of the Law on Duties and Authorities of the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology, approved on September 19, 2003, is the responsibility of the Communications Regulatory Commission.
B- The National Cyberspace Center of the country is authorized to take the necessary legal action to review, complete, and update the document "National Information Network Master Plan and Architecture" approved on 16/7/1399, pursuant to row (1) of the table in paragraph "D" of the "Strategic Document of the Islamic Republic of Iran in Cyberspace" approved on 11/5/1401 by the Supreme Council of Cyberspace.
C- Executive agencies and non-governmental public institutions and organizations, with the exception of the Ministry of Information, the Atomic Energy Organization, and the Armed Forces, are required to provide telecommunications operators with permission to use their buildings and infrastructures, such as transmission beams, ground and underground communication routes, ducts, and suitable spaces for the installation of communication equipment, in accordance with the tariffs approved by the Communications Regulatory Commission, upon the announcement of the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology.
Note 1- The provisions of this paragraph shall be implemented in compliance with Article (13) of the Law on the Establishment of the Iranian Telecommunications Company, approved on 29/3/1350.
Note 2 - The tariffs of this paragraph must be approved by the Communications Regulatory Commission within three months of the entry into force of this law and must be updated and notified during the implementation of the program each year, no later than the end of Khordad of the following year.
Note 3 - The provisions of this clause do not apply to buildings whose interests are in the possession of other persons, provided that the aforementioned use is not foreseen in the contract.
Note 4 - If there is a compelling interest, as determined by the Communications Regulatory Commission, the use of private sector walls overlooking passages is also permitted, subject to Article (13) of the Law on the Establishment of the Iranian Telecommunications Company, approved on 29/3/1350.
D- The Supreme Council of Cyberspace is the authority for policy-making, decision-making, and coordination on issues related to cyberspace, and its approvals are binding on all executive bodies, as the case may be.
Note - The National Cyberspace Center of the country is required, in cooperation with other relevant agencies, to formulate the regulations on the institutional division of labor, the governance of cyberspace, especially in the field of cyberspace security, and the executive indicators of the "Strategic Document of the Islamic Republic of Iran in Cyberspace" and submit it to the Supreme Cyberspace Council for approval, and to follow up on the results of the actions of the executive agencies and report to that council every six months.
E- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is authorized to establish an “International Communications Company” within the limits of its resources and credits, using its own powers and the development organization, as well as the participation and investment of the non-governmental sector. The articles of association of this company shall be approved by the Council of Ministers upon the proposal of the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology.
C- The government is required to take legal action to implement the "National Program for the Development of Artificial Intelligence" within a maximum of six months from the entry into force of this law, in order to support the development of a transformative ecosystem of reliable and sustainable artificial intelligence and to determine the frameworks and mechanisms for the interaction of all stakeholders, to provide technical, social, ethical and legal knowledge and infrastructure, and to promote and increase awareness about the functions of artificial intelligence in various fields and its potential risks, in compliance with the general policies of the system, the approvals of the Supreme Council of the Cultural Revolution, and the strategic document of the Islamic Republic of Iran in cyberspace.
Digital economy
Article 66 – In order to increase the share of the digital economy in the gross national product, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to prepare the "Digital Economy System" document in cooperation with the member agencies of the government's special working group on the digital economy, in accordance with the "Strategic Document of the Islamic Republic of Iran in Cyberspace", within three months of the entry into force of this law, and submit it to the Supreme Council for Cyberspace for approval.
B- In order to maximize the use of telecommunications operators' infrastructure capacities and develop the fixed broadband Internet access network based on optical fiber, a "Fiber Optic Network Development Fund" is established.
The fund's statute, including its components, duties, powers, methods of operation, management, and supervision within the framework of this law, must be approved by the Council of Ministers within three months of the law coming into force, upon the proposal of the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology. Furthermore, all executive processes of this fund are the responsibility of the Radio and Communications Regulatory Authority without any increase in the organizational and executive structure.
The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to create at least five million fixed broadband internet subscriptions based on optical fiber in the country annually, using the resources of this fund and the investment of telecommunications operators, and to submit a performance report on this fund to the Parliament's Program and Budget, Accounting, and Industries and Mines committees annually.
The financial resources of the fund include the remaining resources in the optical fiber network development account, subject to paragraph "S" of Note (7) of the 1402 (2023) budget law for the whole country, and a part of the annual gross income of communication and information technology operators, approved by the Cabinet of Ministers from the Law on Authorizing the Determination and Collection of Privileges for the Non-Governmental Sector in the Field of Post and Telecommunications, approved on 19/8/1932, in compliance with the laws and credits contained in the annual budget, and are included in specific rows, so that they can be spent in cases and to the extent determined in the laws in the form of technical and credit assistance and facility interest subsidies, in compliance with the laws.
C- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to provide the necessary infrastructure for the development of the digital economy, including communication and information (cloud) and fast storage and processing for presence and competition in domestic and international markets, with the participation and investment of the non-governmental sector through its subsidiary development organization.
D- In order to educate and train at least 500,000 skilled and specialized human resources for the development of the country's digital economy and cyberspace during the implementation of the program, the subject agencies of rows (14), (28), and (30) of the table, paragraph "D" of the strategic document of the Islamic Republic of Iran in cyberspace, are required, within the framework of the aforementioned document, to prepare the "National Program for the Growth of the Country's Digital Skills", which includes the creation of new academic fields and courses and the revision of the syllabus of existing academic fields and skill courses at all levels, within six months of the entry into force of this law, and to take legal action.
E- The Statistics Center of Iran, in cooperation with the Ministries of Communications and Information Technology and Industry, Mines and Trade, is required to prepare a system for measuring the contribution of the digital economy ecosystem to the total added value of the country's economy within three months of the law coming into force and to update it annually.
C- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to provide digital businesses with access to the required data and information through the National Data Exchange Center, while maintaining the security of personal data, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law, in order to provide and facilitate data-based innovations in services and products.
Note - The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to take the necessary legal measures to develop a "document of policies and requirements for the protection and protection of personal data" within three months of the entry into force of this law.
G- In order to provide financial resources for the development of the digital and knowledge-based economy and enable the participation of all people, the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is obliged, in cooperation with the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology, to provide the possibility of accepting active companies in this field in the securities market by creating a specialized stock market, establishing special stock market indices, creating new financial instruments and accepting digital assets, as well as accepting all properties and assets, including real estate, benefits, claims and financial rights, movable and immovable properties, goodwill, exploration rights, tangible and intangible properties such as urban or rural residential or commercial units, agricultural land, production machinery and equipment, precious metals, securities, disposable income from stocks, disposable income from contracts or the implementation of projects, the balance of termination bonuses and reserves for employee claims, continuous salaries and benefits received, contractual claims, trademarks (brands), intellectual properties, cash subsidies and inventory (raw materials or products) of production units from credit institutions, financial funds and The Securities and Exchange Organization, with the ability to trade in the market, shall act in the processes of validation, collateralization, guarantee, and underwriting in compliance with relevant laws and regulations, including the Law on Facilitating the Issuance of Business Licenses.
The executive regulations of this paragraph shall be prepared by the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance in cooperation with the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology and other relevant executive agencies, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
H- In order to create uniformity of procedure and protect the rights of users and facilitate healthy competition among stakeholders, the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is responsible for issuing licenses for all communication services (through the country's national licensing portal) in compliance with the Law on Facilitating the Issuance of Business Licenses, Information Technology and Intelligence Services, and Messaging Platforms, compiling and approving tariff tables, and determining their subscription fees within the framework of the country's laws and regulations, in compliance with the approvals of the Supreme Council for Cyberspace.
The Ministry also takes legal action to determine fines for violations of legal obligations in accordance with the quality of the violation and the circumstances of the violator.
Article 67–
A- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required, in cooperation with the Ministry of Science, Research and Technology and the General Staff of the Armed Forces, based on the document "Policies and Major Programs of the Country's Space Sector" approved by the Supreme Space Council, to accelerate the growth of the country's space industry and develop the use of space-based services and space data in economic sectors (government institutions, non-governmental public institutions and organizations, and the private sector) to implement space programs with the following priorities:
1- Establishing the ability to access low-orbit satellites quickly and cheaply and maintaining the country's orbital locations.
2- Creation and development of testing infrastructure for satellite systems and satellite launchers
3- Completion of the National Launch Base
4- Improving the capability of indigenously manufacturing measurement, telecommunications, television broadcasting, and navigation satellites
5- Developing the capability to achieve high altitude and geosynchronous orbits
6- Covering the risks of non-governmental sector investment in the provision, development of technology, and launch of satellite systems providing communication, measurement, and Internet services.
7- Expanding access to space technology-based services for businesses
8- Creating mechanisms for the economic growth of the country's space industry with an annual growth rate of eight percent (8%).
9- Participation and investment in international space systems in order to meet the needs of the country and aligned countries such as BRICS member countries and the Shanghai Cooperation Organization, Islamic countries and member countries of the Non-Aligned Movement, in compliance with Article Seventy-Seven (77) of the Constitution.
Note - The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is obliged to meet the needs of executive agencies, the private sector and the cooperative sector for satellite images and data based on competitiveness with priority given to users and knowledge-based companies. The tariff for these services shall be approved by the Communications Regulatory Commission upon the proposal of the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology. Data from military, security and sensitive institutions are excluded from the scope of this note and its responsibility lies with the General Staff of the Armed Forces. Also, the legal duties and responsibilities of executive agencies, including the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization, shall be valid.
Civilian security information related to the Ministry of Intelligence is excluded from the scope of this note.
B- In order to coordinate and monitor the advancement of the national information network and the development of the country's communication and information technology infrastructure, the selection and activity of the CEO and members of the board of directors of communication and information technology operators licensed by the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is possible after the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology issues their professional and technical qualifications. The selection and activity of the CEO is carried out within the framework of the laws.
Note - Regulations on the procedure for determining eligibility, objections, and their handling shall be prepared by the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology within three months of the effective date of this law and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Chapter 14 – Improving the Health System
Article 68 – In implementing paragraph (12) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and in order to achieve the following quantitative goals, action shall be taken in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:
Table No. (15) - Quantitative objectives of performance indicators for improving the health system
Quantitative goal at the end of the program	Current status (base year)	One known	Performance measure
۳۰ 	– 	Percentage	Out-of-pocket contribution index
۲ 	– 	Percentage	Index of the maximum percentage of households that experience unaffordable (catastrophic) expenses
۱۰۰ 	۹۵ 	Percentage	Full health insurance coverage for the entire Iranian population
۲.۳ 	۱.۷ 	A thousand people	Per capita doctor to population
۷.۵ 	۱۵.۷ 	Percentage	Deaths from heart attacks in people under 55 years of age compared to the base year in the form of family physicians
۱.۴ 	۲.۱ 	Percentage	Decrease in DMF in 12-year-olds compared to the baseline year in the form of a family doctor
۵۰ 	۴۰ 	Percentage	Monitoring index (identification and control) of diabetic patients in the form of a family doctor
۶۰ 	۴۵ 	Percentage	Monitoring index (identification and control) of patients with high blood pressure over 30 years of age in the form of a family doctor
۸۵ 	۶۰ 	Percentage	Monitoring index (identification and control) of patients with blood lipid disorders in the form of family physicians
۴۰ 	۲۰ 	Percentage	Monitoring (control) index of three factors: blood sugar, blood pressure, and lipids in diabetic patients in the form of a family doctor
۱۰ 	۱۴ 	Percentage	Tobacco use index in the form of family doctor
The Ministry of Health and Medical Education is required to submit an annual report on the performance indicators of the health system to the Parliament.
Improving service quality
Article 69 – The following measures shall be taken to improve the quality of services, reduce costs, and increase patient satisfaction:
one thousand-
1- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to establish a smart health information system and fully establish a family doctor and referral system on an electronic platform within two years of the entry into force of this law, by preparing secure data centers and establishing electronic signatures, all systems of centers providing health services and goods, including hospital systems, outpatient prescription and prescription filling, health software (first level of health services), health document monitoring and auditing systems, and self-care systems, and by collecting all health data generated from these sources and storing them securely and centrally in the national health database based on the National Data and Information Management Law, while protecting citizens' health information, make available the available information to treating physicians or any individual or group that is legally or based on a license obtained from the main owner of the information (citizen). The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to prepare the country's e-health roadmap document within three months of the law coming into force, with the aim of establishing an integrated e-health architecture system, and submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval.
2- Health service providers, including government, public, non-government, charitable, and private, are required to submit health and medical data of Iranians and non-Iranian citizens online and simultaneously with the provision of services based on the National Data and Information Management Law (National Health Database) to the Ministry of Health, Treatment, and Medical Education. From the beginning of the second year of the program, any renewal of the technical responsible license, renewal of the license of doctors' offices and other health care and service providers, as well as renewal of the establishment and operation license and accreditation certificate in the outpatient and inpatient departments of all centers and institutions providing health services in all sectors is subject to the fulfillment of the above tasks.
3- In order to integrate and improve the level of regularity of the health service purchasing system and consolidate insurance rules in the field of outpatient and inpatient health services, and facilitate and accelerate Iranians' access to benefiting from these services:
1-3- All basic and supplementary health insurance companies and funds of any legal nature, including government, public, non-government, charitable and private, as well as companies and funds affiliated with individuals whose coverage by law requires mentioning or specifying their names, are required to complete all stages of eligibility assessment, including identity verification and insurance coverage, and monitoring (control) of insurance overlap, exclusively based on the National Data and Information Management Law (National Health Insurance Database of the Country), by the end of the first year of implementation of this law. These companies and funds are required to keep the data related to the insurance information of their insured persons updated in the database and make all stages of their service provision subject to the use of the database.
2-3- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to launch the "Health Rules Database" (an integrated system for assessing the eligibility rules for health services, the identity and qualification of all prescribers of medical prescriptions and orders, as well as the signatories of documents in jobs and professions related to the health system) by the end of the first year of implementation of this law, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law and the requirements contained in the country's electronic health roadmap document, with the aim of strictly applying the rules for prescribing and strategic purchasing of services and implementing clinical guidelines, monitoring (controlling) the authenticity of medicines and consumables and equipment, monitoring (controlling) the identity and qualification of prescribers of medical prescriptions and orders, as well as the signatories of medical documents in jobs and professions related to the health system, and making it available to systems approved by the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education.
4- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to prepare, approve and notify, within the first six months of the program's implementation, the necessary regulations for providing integrated e-health services based on the e-health regulatory and operational system, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law and within the framework of laws and regulations.
The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to grant e-health operating licenses to qualified companies through a call and evaluation, in compliance with the Law on Facilitating the Issuance of Business Licenses, no later than the beginning of the second year of the program. The flow of health data in the regulatory-operating system will be based on the National Data and Information Management Law.
The regulations, including technical and managerial capabilities in the legal statute, the capabilities of facilities and equipment, and financial resources commensurate with the amount of services related to the electronic health record, are prepared by the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education in cooperation with the organization and the Ministry of Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare, and are approved by the Council of Ministers.
5- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to establish and operationalize electronic signatures with the aim of managing and monitoring health services by creating the necessary mechanisms, including the "Health Rules Database", by fully activating the public key infrastructure by granting licenses to the Medical System Organization of the Islamic Republic of Iran and other electronic signature certificate issuing centers under the intermediate center, and by exercising hierarchical supervision over them, in compliance with Articles (10) and (80) of the Electronic Commerce Law approved on 10/17/1382 and other relevant laws and regulations.
6- From the first year of implementation of this law, all health service providers, including government, public, non-government, charitable, and private, are required to enter into contracts with basic health insurance and send documents electronically, at the request or need of basic insurance organizations.
The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to formulate the executive regulations of this clause, including a strategy for managing emergency situations such as force majeure events and internet outages, in compliance with the laws, within three months of this law coming into force, and submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval. It is also required to submit a report on the performance of this clause, broken down into its components, to the Health and Treatment Commission and the Parliamentary Oversight Office every six months.
B- None of the physicians, dentists, pharmacists, and those covered by the Law on Improving the Productivity of Clinical Staff in the Health System, approved on 1/30/1388, who are officially, contractually, and under contract employed by executive agencies working in the headquarters or centers and institutions providing health services subject to the aforementioned law, are permitted to engage in for-profit medical activities in diagnostic, educational, and therapeutic centers and private, public, non-governmental, and charitable hospitals, in compliance with Note (1) of Article One of the Law on Prohibition of Holding More than One Job, approved on 11/10/1373, or engage in for-profit medical activities in the private sector related to the headquarters area other than their executive agency. The responsibility for implementing this ruling, as appropriate, lies with the relevant ministers and the head of the Medical System Organization of the Islamic Republic of Iran.
In order to implement this provision, the government is required to compensate the beneficiaries for the services provided by them within the framework of the annual budget by applying the relevant tariff and reforming the fee-for-service payment system based on the difference in the tariff for diagnostic and treatment services in the public and private sectors, subject to paragraph "A" of Article (9) of the Law on Permanent Provisions on National Development Programs. The executive regulations of this paragraph shall be approved by the Council of Ministers upon the proposal of the Ministry of Health and Medical Education.
Non-profit activities in charitable diagnostic, educational, and treatment centers are excluded from the scope of this clause.
C- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to plan and take action to increase the annual specialized medical capacity by at least twelve percent (12%) by obtaining a commitment to serve in the required areas in compliance with the Law on Establishing Educational Justice in the Admission of Students in Postgraduate and Specialized Education Courses, approved on September 21, 2009, with subsequent amendments and additions, and to provide educational infrastructure within the approved budget ceiling, in order to develop the quantitative and qualitative aspects of the medical education system, increase access to health services, especially in underprivileged areas, prepare for the aging population, and prevent the burnout of medical personnel.
The Ministry of Health and Medical Education is required to prepare a plan to increase the training capacity of the medical team, with priority given to nursing, midwifery, paramedical, pharmacy, and intermediate fields, and submit it to the approval of the Council of Ministers.
D- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to take steps to promote the status of Iranian traditional medicine services by organizing traditional medicine services based on scientific evidence and developing educational, research, health, treatment and pharmaceutical services, preparing a list of the country's traditional and herbal products and medicines, and supervising their distribution and supply in authorized centers and places.
E- In order to provide pre-hospital emergency medical services and ensure fair access to these services for people in all parts of the country, the Emergency Medical Services Organization of the country is required to develop urban land, road, air (providing or purchasing services), and sea bases for pre-hospital emergency medical services within the annual budget ceiling.
C- From the beginning of the second year of the program, all automobile and motorcycle manufacturing and importing companies are required to allocate, as appropriate, for the sale of each automobile, heavy and light machinery, and motorcycle, one percent (1%) of their sales price after the treasury turnover, for the purchase and delivery of ambulances and motor lances, with fifty percent (50%) for the Red Crescent Society of the Islamic Republic of Iran and fifty percent (50%) for the country's Emergency Medical Services Organization.
G- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education, in cooperation with the medical and nursing system organizations of the Islamic Republic of Iran and other stakeholders, is required to prepare a comprehensive health care document (policy) in the first year of the program's implementation, submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval, and begin implementing it from the beginning of the second year of the program.
Health system leadership
Article 70 – In order to promote efficiency and fair access to health services and create a competitive environment between different service providers with the aim of satisfying service recipients, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The health system, including health insurance, including executive policy-making, strategic planning, evaluation, accreditation, and monitoring, with an emphasis on strategic procurement of services and performance-based payment based on clinical guidelines for the transfer of management affairs, in compliance with Article (13) of the National Services Management Law and Service Leveling, and strengthening and streamlining the comprehensive and universal health service network system through the implementation of the family physician program and the referral system, in compliance with general health policies and this law and Article (7) of the Law on Permanent Provisions of National Development Programs, and by considering the priority of prevention over treatment with the participation of basic health insurance organizations, protecting people's health rights, promoting indicators of people's equitable benefit from basic services, adjusting and managing (controlling) demand, and paying attention to social, economic, political, and cultural factors affecting health, shall be centralized in the Ministry of Health, Treatment, and Medical Education. All natural and legal entities, both governmental and non-governmental, including providers of health services (health, diagnostic, pharmaceutical, care, treatment, and rehabilitation) in outpatient and inpatient departments, basic and supplementary health insurance organizations and companies, and providers of digital services, as well as in other health areas, are required to comply with the guidelines and policies of the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education.
B- The organization is required to allocate the resources of the public health budget, which is of an insurance nature, solely through the insurance system centered on the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education and in cooperation with other centers and institutions. Health and treatment centers of the armed forces are exempt from the provisions of this paragraph.
C- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to implement the country’s health-treatment network system, including integrated health, diagnostic, treatment, care, pharmaceutical and outpatient and inpatient rehabilitation services with priority to health and prevention, by the end of the first year of the program’s implementation, to establish a family doctor program and referral system for the entire population of the country, using all the capacities of government and non-government professionals. Simultaneously with the full establishment of the aforementioned program, the Supreme Council of Health Insurance is required to take the necessary legal action to coordinate the payment of incentives determined in the program for the quantitative and qualitative development of the basic health insurance package and to reform the insurance payment system in accordance with Subsection (7) of Clause (9) of the General Health Policies.
D- The Supreme Council of Health Insurance of the country is obliged to change the tariff for common diagnostic and therapeutic medical services from the “fee-for-service” method to the “global payment for service costs” method by the end of the first year of the program and submit it for approval by the Council of Ministers, so that the tariff method of at least four hundred service identifiers by the end of the program is subject to this change and the services are purchased by basic and supplementary insurance after separating pharmaceutical items and medical equipment and consumables using the new payment method. The Supreme Council of Health Insurance of the country is obliged to send a report on the performance of this clause to the Health and Medical Treatment Commission of the Parliament every six months.
E- All doctors, paramedics, institutions and centers providing services, medicines and health products in the country, including government, public, non-government, private and charitable, are required to comply with the government-approved tariffs. Any payment in excess of the government-approved tariff by the aforementioned natural and legal persons is subject to relevant legal penalties, as applicable. The tariff for pharmaceutical services, like other health services, is determined annually based on paragraph "A" of Article (9) of the Law on Permanent Provisions of the National Development Programs.
C- In order to implement the family physician program and referral system in hospitals affiliated with the government and social security, hospitals affiliated with executive agencies, and private hospitals that cooperate within the framework of the leveling and referral system, specialist physicians in these hospitals are required to provide daily services to at least a number of patients referred from the first level as determined by the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education.
G- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to take the following measures during the implementation of the program in order to continuously improve the quality of health care and services, increase effectiveness and efficiency, and optimally use the country's health, treatment, and rehabilitation facilities:
1- Rationalize (standardize) the provision of medical services and reduce false and induced services by the end of the first year of program implementation, and develop and communicate clinical guidelines, medical service criteria, and drug prescription guidelines.
2- Developing indicators for monitoring, supervising, evaluating health care and services and accreditation, taking into account geographical distribution and population size, and supervising all centers and institutions for outpatient and inpatient care, health, diagnostic, therapeutic, pharmaceutical, and rehabilitation services based on established indicators, criteria, clinical guidelines, compliance with tariffs, and the approved payment system.
3- Evaluating new technologies and services and improving current health system services based on them.
Note - Basic and supplementary health insurance organizations are required to upload and use the above items, as applicable, within a maximum of one month from the effective date of this law in the context of smart health systems, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law.
H- In line with the management of the risk of accidents and disasters, the government, in cooperation with relevant institutions, is obliged to formulate appropriate executive measures, giving priority to measures aimed at prevention, damage reduction and preparedness, increasing resilience and providing sustainable resources to deal with accidents and disasters. Also, considering the need for seismic reinforcement and safety, dealing with fires, and the importance of improving resilience and overhauling the mechanical, electrical and cyber systems of hospitals, government health-care centers, and pre-hospital emergency medical bases, the plan to improve the safety and resilience of hospitals and health-care centers in the country will be implemented in the years of the program.
X- Pursuant to Article (117) of the Civil Service Management Law, the financial, accounting, transactional, employment regulations, and the organizational structure and organizational positions (posts) of the Red Crescent Society of the Islamic Republic of Iran are subject to Subsection (4) of Clause (B) of Article (10) of the Statute of the Red Crescent Society of the Islamic Republic of Iran, as amended on 24/2/1382.
D- In order to improve the health of blood and its products and save the lives of patients in need of hematopoietic stem cell transplants, the Iranian Blood Transfusion Organization is required to conduct molecular (NET) and antibody screening tests and histocompatibility (HLA) tests based on modern methods from the first year of the program.
Medicine and medical equipment
Article 71 – In order to ensure the sustainable supply of strategic stocks of quality medicines, predict and prevent medicine shortages, and reduce the share of urgent imports in meeting the country's needs, the following measures will be taken during the implementation of the program:
A- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education, in cooperation with the relevant executive agencies, is required to regulate by the end of the first year of the program implementation in such a way that strategic reserves of quality medicines and medical consumables are provided to the country's needs for at least six months, with priority given to domestic production and official imports. The government is required to forecast the required resources in the annual budgets through the relevant agencies and make them available to the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education. The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to submit a report on the performance of this section to the Health and Treatment Commission and the Parliamentary Oversight Office every six months.
B- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required, in cooperation with the organization and the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education, to establish a mechanism for paying the government subsidy share by the end of the first year of the program's implementation through electronic and credit settlement of claims in the supply chain of medicines, medical equipment and supplies, as appropriate, to pharmacies, hospitals, and drug distribution and supplier companies.
C- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to complete the system for tracking, tracing and monitoring the authenticity of health-oriented goods for medicines, medical equipment and supplies in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law, in such a way that by the end of the third year of the program’s implementation, the entire market is covered by this system. After completing the system, basic and supplementary medical insurance in the outpatient and inpatient departments are authorized to pay for the medicines, medical equipment and supplies covered by it, if they receive a certificate of authenticity from this system.
D- The government is obliged to take action within the framework and in compliance with the laws, including the law on regulations on medical, pharmaceutical, food and beverage affairs approved in 1955 with its subsequent amendments, regarding the pricing of consumable medical equipment and supplies, pharmaceutical supplements, dietary, nutritional and pharmaceutical raw materials, pharmaceutical products and vaccines that are subject to subsidies or are considered exclusive goods (subject to sub-paragraph (2-1) of paragraph "e" of Article (48) of this law), except for high-tech and biotechnology products, taking into account the cost of the product and the normal profit, by announcing rules and in a systematic manner. The Secretary of the Supreme Council of Health Insurance of the country, who is a government employee, is added to the members of the drug and medical equipment pricing commissions with voting rights.
Note - In the case of persons subject to paragraphs (3) and (4) of Note (3) of Article (20) of the Law on Regulations of Medical, Pharmaceutical, Food and Beverage Affairs, it is necessary to have the necessary Sharia conditions, including trustworthiness and honesty.
E- The official drug list of Iran is compiled and published by the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education, based on the country's national drug system (generic plan), at most once every three months. Prescribing drugs outside the aforementioned list is considered a violation, and the violator, considering the severity of the act committed and its frequency and repetition, will be sentenced to the penalties stipulated in Note (1) of Article (28) of the Law of the Organization of the Medical System of the Islamic Republic of Iran, approved on 15/01/1383, as the case may be. The executive regulations of this paragraph will be prepared by the Organization and the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education within three months of the entry into force of this law and will be approved by the Council of Ministers.
C- The government is required to take legal action within a maximum of six months from the entry into force of this law regarding the formulation of a program for the modernization and reconstruction of the pharmaceutical, health products, medical equipment and supplies, and immunization (vaccine) industries, which is carried out by the Ministries of Industry, Mines and Trade, Health, Medical Treatment and Education, Cooperatives, Labor and Social Welfare, and Agricultural Jihad with the aim of increasing the efficiency and quality of domestic products and their competitiveness, as well as strengthening the country's domestic production and export capacity, achieving ninety percent (90%) self-reliance, increasing its share of the regional market, and providing the necessary facilities, and to submit its performance report to the parliament annually.
G- The Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to prepare the statute of the Food and Drug Administration within a maximum of three months from the entry into force of this law and submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval. Failure to submit the proposed statute by the relevant managers of the aforementioned ministry to the Council of Ministers within the prescribed period will be subject to the punishment referred to in Article (598) of Book Five of the Islamic Penal Code (Penalties and Deterrent Punishments).
H- In line with the growth and development of humanitarian services, promotion of social capital, strengthening public participation, increasing the participation of youth and volunteers in relief and public benefit services, and helping to increase the resilience of society, reducing damage caused by accidents and disasters and climate change, and developing support affairs, assistance from natural and legal persons (governmental, private, and public) to the Red Crescent Society of the Islamic Republic of Iran is considered an acceptable tax expense.
X- The Ministry of Agricultural Jihad is required, in coordination with the Ministry of Health, Medical Education and the National Organization of Standards of Iran, after establishing a system for tracking, tracing, packaging, identification and branding for raw agricultural, livestock, poultry and aquatic products from the farm and livestock level, to evaluate and announce these products in terms of agricultural pesticide residues, nitrates, heavy metals and animal drug residues in the supply chain in order to take the necessary legal action. The executive regulations of this clause are prepared by the Ministry of Agricultural Jihad in coordination with the Ministry of Health, Medical Education and the National Organization of Standards of Iran and are subject to approval by the Council of Ministers. The Ministry of Agricultural Jihad and the National Organization of Standards of Iran are required to submit a report on the performance of this clause to the Health and Medical and Agriculture, Water, Natural Resources and Environment Commissions of the Parliament every six months.
D- The government is authorized to implement a free milk feeding plan in government elementary schools.
Article 72 – In order to transform the Islamic Republic of Iran into a health care hub in the Southwest Asia region, achieve annual exports of more than one billion (1,000,000,000) euros in medicines and vaccines and more than one billion (1,000,000,000) euros in medical equipment, increase the country’s annual income from health tourism to six billion (6,000,000,000) euros, and increase the annual income from attracting foreign students in medical sciences to more than seven hundred million (700,000,000) euros, the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education is required to take the following measures:
A- In order to increase the self-sufficiency rate in the supply of raw materials for medicines, pharmaceutical products and agricultural products, consumer goods and medical equipment, by the end of the first year of the program’s implementation, in cooperation with the Ministries of Industry, Mines and Trade and Agricultural Jihad, an appropriate mechanism should be established to comply with the necessary criteria for the export of agricultural products and medicines, and to set up a system for registering export contracts and ensuring the rights and security of these contracts. The Ministry of Agricultural Jihad and the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education (through the relevant subsidiary organization) are required to announce export bans at least one year before their implementation, except in cases of necessity. In the event of export bans, contracts concluded within the framework of the aforementioned mechanisms and criteria are not subject to these bans. Necessities are determined in each case by the determination of the Ministries of Health, Treatment and Medical Education and Agricultural Jihad.
B- By the end of the second year of the program, by conducting bilateral and multilateral negotiations with priority given to the countries of the region, the civilizational sphere, and the members of the Eurasian Economic Union, take the necessary measures to accept the raw materials of medicines and pharmaceutical products, consumer goods, and medical equipment registered in Iran by these countries, as well as to issue registration certificates and market entry permits and joint production quality certificates.
Health insurance
Article 73 – In order to provide sustainable financial resources for the health sector, develop the quantity and quality of health insurance, and manage health resources through the insurance system, centered on the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education, the following measures shall be taken:
A- Basic insurance coverage is mandatory for the entire population of the country, and the government subsidies for the insurance premiums of the head of the household and his dependents are provided through a means assessment, free of charge for at least the bottom five income deciles, and for other deciles, by charging per capita, based on the following criteria and a regulation that is prepared upon the proposal of the Supreme Council of Health Insurance and approved by the Council of Ministers.
Note: All Iranians without basic health insurance are considered insured by the Iranian Health Insurance Organization. The organization's claims for insurance premiums and late payment damages, based on the provisions of this law, are enforceable as claims documented by documents and are collected upon the announcement of the Iranian Health Insurance Organization from the individual's claims from executive agencies, including cash subsidies, in accordance with the executive regulations prepared by the Iranian Health Insurance in cooperation with the Subsidy Targeting Organization and approved by the Council of Ministers.
The Ministry of Health and Medical Education is required to submit a report on the performance of this section to the Parliament every six months.
B- The basic family health insurance premium is a share of the family income as follows:
1- Families of villagers, tribes, and needy groups covered by support institutions: equivalent to seven percent (7%) of the minimum wage for those subject to the Labor Law, one hundred percent (100%) of which is provided by the government in the form of an annual budget, based on paragraph "A" of this article.
2- Executive agency employees: equivalent to seven percent (7%) of their ongoing salaries and benefits, part of which is financed from the government's general budget in an amount determined in the annual budget.
3- Insured persons and subscribers of the Social Security Organization: According to the Social Security Law
4- The share of households from other strata, proportional to income groups: equivalent to seven percent (7%) of income, with a maximum equivalent to the income ceiling of government employees.
C- The government is required to fully anticipate the per capita payment of basic health insurance premiums for the individuals it is responsible for in annual budget bills and allocate one hundred percent (100%) of it to the Iranian Health Insurance Organization in compliance with Article (30) of the National Plan and Budget Law and Article (28) of the Law on the Addition of Certain Articles to the Law on the Regulation of Part of the Government Financial Regulations (2), and similar to the payments of the first quarter of salaries and wages.
D- In order to reduce the costs of the people, the Supreme Council of National Health Insurance is required to conduct a financial affordability assessment based on data from the Iranian Welfare Database in order to strengthen appropriate health and medical behaviors of households by establishing a variable and stepped self-payment system for the aforementioned package based on the financial burden of services, and submit the matter to the approval of the Council of Ministers. The ceiling in rials for payment from the patient’s pocket shall be determined annually in line with the quantitative target stated in Table No. (15) until the end of the program and through the mechanism of Article (9) of the Law on Permanent Provisions of National Development Programs.
E- The government is authorized, starting from the first year of implementation of the program, in compliance with Article Twenty-Ninth (29) of the Constitution, based on the capacity test and within the approved budget ceiling, to implement a supportive treatment program in excess of the basic insurance package in government hospitals and medical centers for retirees and low-income deciles (at least three deciles) based on a regulation that is proposed by the organization and the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education and approved by the Council of Ministers.
C- The insurance company's share (franchise) in cases of hospitalization for clients covered by the Imam Khomeini Relief Committee (RA) and the National Welfare Organization, disabled veterans, and disabled female heads of households shall be determined free of charge with the approval of the relevant institutions, and for other groups in the first to fifth deciles, two percent (2%) and for other deciles, ten percent (10%). The implementation of this clause is subject to the provision of the required financial resources by the government in the annual budget laws.
G- During the implementation of the program, basic health insurance organizations are required to spend at least five percent (5%) of their annual approved funds to promote prevention principles at the community level in the areas of self-care (monitoring of metabolic risk factors), exercise, healthy nutrition, mental health, and tobacco control based on information available in the national health database or electronic health record in the form of various incentives for insured persons, including discounts on insurance premiums. The executive regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the Supreme Council of Health Insurance of the country and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
H-
1- In addition to the specific value-added tax on tobacco products subject to paragraph "T" of Article (26) of the Value-Added Tax Law approved on 2/3/1400, the performance tax, input tax, and monopoly right on tobacco products, from the beginning of 1403, the tax on each cigarette and each fifty-gram pack of tobacco will increase annually compared to the 1402 National Budget Law approved on 24/12/1401 as follows:
1-1- Every domestically produced cigarette with an Iranian brand is fifteen percent (15%)
2-1- Each domestically produced cigarette with an international brand is twenty-five percent (25%)
3-1- Each imported cigarette with any fifty percent (50%) mark
4-1- Each fifty gram pack of domestically produced tobacco is twenty percent (20%)
5-1- Each fifty gram pack of imported tobacco ready for consumption is fifty-five percent (55%)
One hundred percent (100%) of the revenues from the implementation of this component will be collected by the National Tax Affairs Organization and deposited into the National Treasury, and will be allocated in annual budgets to reduce tobacco consumption, prevent and treat diseases caused by it, develop sports facilities with priority given to underprivileged areas, and develop sports facilities in schools.
The Ministries of Economic Affairs and Finance, Health, Medical Education, Education, Sports, and Youth are required to submit an annual performance report of this component to the Health, Treatment, and Culture Commissions and the Parliamentary Oversight Office.
2- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is obliged to:
1-2- Provide the Tax Affairs Organization with online access to information systems related to the import, production, and distribution of cigarettes and various tobacco products, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law.
2-2- Take action to identify all production units and suppliers of tobacco products that are produced and supplied illegally, and while preventing their activities, introduce the violators to the competent legal authorities.
3- The Headquarters for Combating Smuggling of Goods and Currency, in cooperation with the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education and the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade, should take action to collect all smuggled and counterfeit tobacco products without tracking identification (code) and introduce the violators to the competent legal authorities.
4- The Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance is required to identify printing houses that print items required by tobacco producers, especially honeyed tobacco, with various foreign and domestic brands without a legal license, and to refer the violators to the competent legal authorities.
Chapter 15 – Promoting Public Culture and the Media
Article 74 – In implementing paragraph (13) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and in order to achieve the following quantitative goals, action shall be taken in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:

It is the Supreme Council of the Cultural Revolution.
Article 75 – In order to enhance public culture and strengthen the Islamic-Iranian lifestyle, promote the culture of sacrifice and martyrdom, justice and service, strengthen solidarity and national self-confidence, promote national identity and the spirit of resistance, work and effort in society, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance and the country's Administrative and Employment Organization are required, in coordination with the Secretariat of the Supreme Council for the Cultural Revolution and in consultation with the Center for the Management of Seminaries and other relevant cultural organizations, to prepare a plan to reform the country's cultural structure with the approach of reforming the mentality, culture, and software that governs society, with the aim of increasing efficiency and avoiding overlapping and conflicting missions and duties, and with the approach of establishing a model of intelligent, networked, interactive, people-based, value-based, and revolutionary governance, by the end of the second year of the program, and submit it to the approval of the competent authorities.
B- In order to accurately and online collect the statistical data needed to facilitate processing, accurate analysis, and create a suitable platform for future research on lifestyle trends in Iranian society, recognizing cultural-communication developments, and publishing them, the Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance is required, in cooperation with the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization and the Iranian Statistical Center, and under the guidance and supervision of the Monitoring, Planning, and Evaluation Center of the Secretariat of the Supreme Council for the Cultural Revolution, and in compliance with Article Twenty-Five (25) of the Constitution and the National Data and Information Management Law, to launch a system for continuous observation, monitoring, and measurement of indicators of public culture, people's lifestyle, media authority, and the state of communications in the country. Executive agencies and database owners subject to this paragraph, except for those directly under the supervision of the Supreme Leader, are required to continuously and comprehensively submit data to this system online. The Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance is required, in addition to establishing online access for the Parliament to the above system, to annually send a report on changes in public culture indicators to the Parliament's Cultural Commission.
C- The Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance is obliged to take the necessary legal action in order to address the violations of all license holders or activists subject to the matters stated in Article (2) of the Law on the Objectives and Duties of the Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance approved on 12/12/1365 and other laws and regulations in the field of culture and art and relevant criteria approved by the competent authorities, except for cases that have previously been determined in the laws or approvals of the Supreme Council for the Cultural Revolution, such as the "Press Law", "Rules for the Establishment and Supervision of Free Art Schools" and "Rules and Regulations for the Establishment of Cultural Centers, Institutions, Associations and Associations and Supervision of Their Activities" in the form of primary and higher boards for addressing violations, as well as determining the composition of the board members, the manner of addressing violations and the type of punishments.
Note 1- Whenever the committees investigating violations encounter a violation that qualifies as a criminal offense during their investigation process, they are required to report the matter to the competent judicial authority for necessary investigation.
Note 2 - The handling of objections regarding the final decisions of the first and second instance boards, subject to this clause, is within the jurisdiction of the appeals branches of the Administrative Court of Justice, in compliance with Note (2) of Article (3) and Article (10) of the amended Administrative Court of Justice Law of 10/2/1402.
T-
1- Executive agencies, especially the Ministries of Culture and Islamic Guidance and Foreign Affairs, as well as the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization, the Islamic Propaganda Organization, the Islamic Culture and Communications Organization, and the Islamic Propaganda Office of the Qom Seminary, are required to cooperate with the Institute for the Compilation and Publication of Imam Khomeini's Works (in compliance with the statutes of that institution) and, using all cultural, artistic, visual and public media facilities, to explain, propagate, promote and publish the works, thoughts and practical conduct of the founder of the Islamic Republic of Iran, Imam Khomeini (may Allah have mercy on him), nationally and internationally.
2- Executive bodies are obliged to explain and promote the ideas of the Supreme Leader, His Highness Ayatollah Ali Khamenei (may Allah protect him), nationally and internationally.
The organization is required to prepare the executive regulations of this part within three months of the entry into force of this law and, after approval by the Office for the Preservation and Publication of the Works of His Highness the Ayatollah Khamenei (may Allah protect him), submit them to the Council of Ministers for approval.
E- In order to popularize cultural activities and utilize the capacity of mosques, the Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance is required to take the necessary legal measures to prepare and approve a mosque-centric plan in neighborhoods within three months of the entry into force of this law, after completing legal formalities, in cooperation with the Center for Addressing Mosque Affairs, the Basij Organization for the Oppressed, the Islamic Propaganda Organization, the Endowments and Charity Affairs Organization, and with the advice of the Supreme Council of Seminaries, the Friday Imams Policy Council, and the Islamic Propaganda Coordination Council.
C- The Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance (Awqaf and Charity Organization) is required to prepare, in cooperation with the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization and the Islamic Propaganda Organization, a plan to revive and activate endowments in order to support and strengthen Quranic activities, committees, mosques, and holy sites, taking into account the intentions of the endowments, by the end of the first year of the program and submit it to the approval of the Council of Ministers.
G- The government is obliged to take action, in compliance with Islamic standards, through the Foundation for Martyrs and Veterans Affairs, the Foundation for Preservation of Monuments and Propagation of Values 
of Sacred Defense, and municipalities across the country, to preserve and promote the monuments, values, epics, and experiences of the Islamic Revolution and Sacred Defense by creating, developing, and maintaining museums, monuments, symbols, and signs of jihad, resistance, and sacrifice, and to preserve the sanctity and high status of martyrs, and to organize and maintain them appropriately as cultural centers, and to renovate and restore the flower gardens of martyrs across the country in coordination with the families of the martyrs, subject to paragraph "g" of Article (1) of the Comprehensive Law on Providing Services to Veterans approved on 2/10/1931, and in compliance with the rights of entitled persons. The Ministries of Power, Oil, Roads and Urban Development, and the Interior are obliged to take action, as appropriate, to provide the necessary infrastructure, including water, electricity, gas, and access roads, from their internal resources within the limits of the annual budget bills.
H- The costs of water, electricity and gas connection and consumption of cultural, artistic, Quranic, media, cinema, press and religious-propaganda centers licensed by the competent authorities, subject to compliance with the laws and regulations implemented by the Public Places Police of the Islamic Republic of Iran Police Command, as long as they only engage in cultural activities and their activities and entitlements are approved by the competent authorities, shall be calculated based on the cultural (educational) tariff if the consumption pattern is observed. The costs of water, electricity and gas connection and consumption of social-cultural creative industries, publishing houses in various platforms, bookstores and movie and theater theaters, subject to compliance with the aforementioned conditions, shall be calculated solely at the amount foreseen in the annual budget laws from the resources obtained from subscribers above the consumption pattern, based on the cultural (educational) tariff.
The implementing regulations for this clause shall be prepared upon the joint proposal of the Ministries of Energy, Petroleum, and Culture and Islamic Guidance and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
X- In order to create the necessary incentives for the government to carry out its duties and increase public and charitable participation in the construction and development of places, the National Tax Affairs Organization is required to consider the expenses of legal and natural persons in the construction, completion, equipping and development of cultural, artistic and sports places in deprived and underprivileged areas as one hundred percent (100%) as acceptable tax expenses, in compliance with Article (23) of the Law on the Addition of Certain Articles to the Law on the Regulation of Part of Government Financial Regulations (2) and, as the case may be, with the coordination and approval of the Ministries of Sports and Youth, Culture and Islamic Guidance, and Cultural Heritage, Tourism and Handicrafts, with priority given to semi-completed projects.
The provisions of this clause regarding the construction of schools and the protection of registered cultural heritage in deprived and underprivileged areas are subject to compliance with the aforementioned conditions and only apply to the extent foreseen in the annual budget laws.
D- The Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance, in coordination with the Basij Mostazafin Organization and in cooperation with the Cultural and Social Headquarters of the Most Merciful, may our souls be sacrificed, shall prepare, within one year of the entry into force of this law, an executive regulation to support and popularize the culture and the flow of the middle circles promoting the discourse of the Islamic Revolution in areas such as Quranic movements, family, women, chastity and hijab, cyberspace and media content production, Iranian-Islamic writing, the demand for progress and justice, the software movement, popular sports and educational activities, and a healthy lifestyle, and submit it to the approval of the Council of Ministers.
Z- The Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance and the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization are required to take the necessary legal action to support people of culture, art, and the media in order to cover social security insurance, including medical and retirement services, in compliance with paragraph "X" of Article (28) of this law.
R- The Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance is required to study the infrastructure of the country's cultural climates in cooperation with the Ministry of Cultural Heritage, Tourism and Handicrafts in order to strengthen the Iranian Islamic lifestyle and strengthen national solidarity, focusing on introducing the country's distinguished scholars and scientific and cultural thinkers.
Article 76 – In order to effectively confront the combined war of the enemies of the Islamic Revolution, with an emphasis on effective media confrontation, promoting national identity, strengthening religious culture, promoting the cultural economy, consolidating the Islamic-Iranian lifestyle, and strengthening religious, political, cultural, and social bases, the government and relevant agencies are required to take the following measures:
A- In order to support the production of content in cyberspace with the approach of expanding and deepening Iranian Islamic culture and effectively confronting the psychological warfare and cultural and political aggression of the enemies, “the division of labor and determination of the limits of duties of the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization and the Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance” will be carried out in accordance with the regulations approved by the Supreme Council of the Cultural Revolution. The aforementioned agencies are required to submit their performance reports to the Parliament’s Cultural Commission every six months.
B- In order to promote Islamic ethics and culture, state-owned companies, banks, and government-affiliated for-profit institutions listed in Appendix (3) of the Annual Budget Law are required to allocate one percent (1%) of their current expenses to enhance and promote cultural activities and productions such as Quranic, theatrical, youth, press, new media, publishing and book production, and the production of high-quality Persian cultural content in cyberspace and tourism, and the development and training of media literacy.
The executive regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance in cooperation with the Ministries of Cultural Heritage, Tourism and Handicrafts, Economic Affairs and Finance, and Communications and Information Technology, the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization, the Islamic Propaganda Organization, and the Seminary Management Center, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
C- The Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance, in cooperation with relevant agencies, is required to take the following measures and support the non-governmental sector in order to increase the amount of animation production to seven thousand three hundred hours by the end of the program:
1- The Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance is required to take the necessary legal measures to provide customs support and provide facilities for the import of hard and soft equipment and technologies related to animation production.
2- The Presidential Vice President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy is responsible for supporting the development of large animation production companies by providing long-term facilities from the Innovation and Prosperity Fund, so that its minimum annual share is not less than three percent (3%).
3- In order to develop and equip the technical infrastructure required to increase the domestic animation production, the Presidential Vice-President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy is required to establish at least two science and technology parks specifically for animation production and is authorized to establish at least one animation production innovation factory in each province, considering the talent and needs of each province. The aforementioned parks and factories are subject to tax exemptions and facilities subject to the Knowledge-Based Production Leap Law approved on 11/2/1401.
The executive regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the Ministry of Culture and Islamic Guidance in cooperation with the Ministries of Education (Center for Intellectual Development of Children and Adolescents) and Communications and Information Technology, the Vice Presidency for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy, the Organization and the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization within three months of the entry into force of this law and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
D- In order to support and assist the affairs of the country's mosques without interfering in the internal and executive affairs of the mosques, a council will be formed in the provinces, chaired by the representative of the Supreme Leader of the province and the secretary of the head of the Islamic Propaganda Organization, and members of representatives from the Basij Organization for the Underprivileged, the Department of Endowments and Charity Affairs, the Islamic Propaganda Coordination Council, the director of the Brothers and Sisters Seminaries, the municipality of the provincial center, centers for handling mosque affairs (if any), and institutions and executive bodies related to mosque affairs.
Note 1- Executive agencies and non-governmental public institutions and organizations are permitted to provide their public and communal services to the people at the local level through mosques and, in line with the implementation of Article Eight (8) of the Constitution and the establishment of the divine duty of enjoining good and forbidding evil, implement a program to popularize this duty by utilizing the capacity of mosques and coordinating with the Headquarters for the Revival of Enjoining Good and Forbidding Evil.
Note 2 - In order to be self-sufficient in managing the country's mosques, municipalities across the country, districts, and villages are required to grant permits for a maximum of 500 square meters of cultural, administrative, and commercial use without charging a fee on surrounding land belonging to mosques (owned by the mosque or dedicated to the mosque), in compliance with laws and regulations, including the detailed plan.
Regarding non-surrounding lands, a maximum of 500 square meters for cultural, administrative, and commercial use for each mosque, including (minus) the area of 
the existing endowments of that mosque, is subject to this ruling solely in the form of a general endowment of the mosque and the trustee of the Endowment and Charity Affairs Organization in the city and municipal district where the mosque is located.
Note 3: Mosque attendants who are covered by the Imam Khomeini Relief Committee (RA) or the Welfare Organization, or who are in income deciles one to four, are added to the list of target communities subject to clause "X" of Article (28) of this law.
Note 4: Support from the government, municipalities, villages, and executive agencies to the council subject to this clause is provided in the form of annual budget bills.
E- All cultural and executive institutions and organizations subject to Article (29) of the Law on the Sixth Five-Year Plan for the Economic, Social and Cultural Development of the Islamic Republic of Iran are required to promote the culture of Mahdism and expectation by using urban symbols, cultural awards, educational packages, specialized fields, computer games, culture-building and storytelling programs using the budget of the same organization and national capacities in various platforms, including the Iranian Broadcasting Corporation and cyberspace.
Article 77 – In order to establish the media authority of the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization and strengthen the efficiency and effectiveness of the national media to expand and deepen Islamic-Iranian culture, effectively confront the psychological warfare and cultural and political aggression of the enemies, and create changes in content, approach, and mechanism, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization is required to take action to achieve the indicators in the table below by the end of the program and submit an annual performance indicator report to the Parliament in order to promote the national media as a media authority, provide maximum coverage, and respond to the needs of all audiences and enhance their national and revolutionary identity indicators by organizing networks, outsourcing and purchasing services, industrialization through the promotion of production technologies, and 100% coverage of the provinces, quantitative and qualitative development of production programs (national, provincial, and overseas), and support for the production of cultural and artistic content in cyberspace. The government is required to provide the resources required for these measures.
