The Ministry of Science, Research and Technology is required to submit a report on performance indicators for the promotion of the scientific, technological and research system to the Parliament annually.
Research and investigation
Article 94-
A- In order to direct research and technological activities towards meeting the real needs of the country and to improve the productivity and effectiveness of research and development, with an emphasis on interdisciplinary research with a priority in the humanities, the system for financing government research (including research projects, theses and dissertations) of universities, Farhangian University, research institutes and higher education and research centers affiliated with the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology, Health, Treatment and Medical Education, and other executive agencies will be amended in such a way that by the end of the program, at least fifty percent (50%) of the public budget resources related to this research will be spent in the form of targeted and prioritized research projects based on the needs, advantages, and future research of scientific and technological developments included in the Ideas and Needs System (NAN) and the priorities of the country's comprehensive scientific map.
The executive regulations (comprehensive study) of this article shall be prepared by the Ministry of Science, Research and Technology, in cooperation with the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education and the organization, within three months of the entry into force of this law, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
B- Educational, research and technological institutions are required to allocate at least twenty percent (20%) of their postdoctoral researchers to demand-oriented "applied", "industrial" and "technological" postdoctoral courses in accordance with the regulations for attracting and employing postdoctoral researchers approved by the Supreme Council for Science, Research and Technology.
C- In order to enhance the productivity and effectiveness of research and fulfill the social responsibility of universities and higher education and research centers in the country, promote the participation movement and the role of middle, popular and elite circles, executive and governmental agencies in solving the problems of the country's progress, the Ministry of Science, Research and Technology is required to take the necessary legal measures within six months of the entry into force of this law to formulate and approve the method of establishing, organizing, supervising and supporting the activities of centers and institutions for policy research, think tanks, strategic studies, and colleges and schools of governance.
Education
Article 95 - In implementation of Article 30 of the Constitution and in order to unify the approach and strengthen coordination and convergence in the process of developing higher education, research and technology, the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education are required to prepare their plan, including determining the total capacity and share of students by field, level of education and subsystems of higher education in the country, the distribution of students in fields, levels of education, as well as the development and creation of fields and levels of education needed in higher education groups, based on considerations of higher education planning and land planning, within six months of the entry into force of this law, and submit it to the approval of the Higher Education Development and Planning Councils of the aforementioned ministries, and update it every year.
Note 1- The Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education are required to take action to eliminate overlaps in active fields and trends based on the policies of the Supreme Council of the Cultural Revolution.
Note 2 - The Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education in non-clinical fields are required to anticipate and present practical and skill courses in each of the possible academic levels in the fields, in addition to theoretical courses, in universities and public and private higher education institutions, Islamic Azad University, in such a way that after graduating from the aforementioned field, the university graduate will have the practical skills needed by the country in at least one specialized field. The executive agencies are required to make the necessary contributions to the implementation of practical courses in their executive agencies. The executive regulations of this note shall be approved by the Council of Ministers within six months of the entry into force of this law by the Ministry of Science, Research and Technology and in cooperation with the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education.
The Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education are required to submit a report on the performance of this article to the Parliament every six months.
Article 96 - The Ministries of Science, Research and Technology, Health, Treatment and Medical Education, and the Organization are required to take the necessary legal measures to reform the system of financing higher education costs based on qualitative and quantitative monitoring (control) of educational services, in compliance with Article 30 of the Constitution, from public resources, in order to achieve the goals of higher education planning, regulate the relationship between education and employment, enhance the responsiveness of universities and higher education, research and technology institutions to the needs of the labor market and social demand, increase the attractiveness of education in priority fields of the country, and eliminate unnecessary fields.
A- The organization is required to prepare, in cooperation with the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education, a regulation on how to determine the credits of universities and higher education, research and technology institutions based on factors such as per capita student, faculty member, local service rate, per capita scientific output, the amount of services provided to students, type of fields including theoretical, applied and practical, and educational levels within three months of the entry into force of this law, and submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval.
Note - The Social Security Organization is required to review and issue the accounts of research contracts of universities and governmental and non-governmental higher education and research institutions approved by the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education, and contracts related to the production of knowledge-based products approved by the Presidential Vice-President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy solely on the basis of Article (38) of the Social Security Law, without applying the insurance premium coefficients referred to in Article (28) of the aforementioned law, and independently of other contracts of the institution, without any conditions.
B- Talented and outstanding university students who are admitted to the country's required fields within a limit of twenty percent (20%) of the field capacity of full-time places and based on the capacity of the first year of the program, will be paid educational assistance through the Student Welfare Fund, provided that the educational quality is maintained.
The executive regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the Ministry of Science, Research and Technology in cooperation with the Ministry of Health, Treatment and Medical Education and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
C- The Central Bank is required to provide facilities from banks through operating banks to complete capital asset acquisition plans, with priority given to the construction, purchase, completion, and equipping of workshops and laboratories of universities, Shahid Rajaee Educational and Secretary Training Universities, with the approval of the Board of Trustees and upon verification of the assets and properties at their disposal.
Scientific authority
Article 97–
A- The Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education are required to take the necessary legal measures in the first year of the program to review and amend the evaluation indicators, educational, research and technology programs, regulations and rules related to recruitment, status change, promotion, and the comprehensive regulation on "University Management, Evaluation and Motivation System and the Method of Providing Mandatory Services to Faculty Members" based on a program-oriented approach, including mission-oriented and problem-oriented, student-oriented and professor-oriented.
Note 1- With the aim of amending the missions and the proportion between the scientific needs and capacities of each of the higher education subsystems, the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education are required, within one year of the enactment of this law, to amend the regulations for the promotion of faculty members in accordance with the mission orientation, problem-centeredness, and program-centeredness of each of the governmental and non-governmental higher education subsystems, and according to the scientific groups (as necessary) and the nature of the discipline, and submit them to the approval of the competent authorities so that from the beginning of the second year of the program, each of these centers and scientific groups will follow their own specific promotion and advancement regulations.
Note 2 - In view of the important and sensitive role of basic sciences and humanities in the path of growth and excellence of society, the Ministry of Science, Research and Technology is obliged, based on an agreement with the Seminary Management Center and in cooperation with the Specialized Council for the Development and Promotion of Humanities, to prepare basic documents on the above subjects and have them approved by the competent authorities. Starting from the second year of the program, it will implement the relevant measures at a rate of ten percent (10%) annually, so that in the field of humanities, relevant books are revised and in the field of basic sciences, at least in two specialized fields, the scientific status of the country is raised to an internationally acceptable level and to the first rank in the region.
B- Research institutions and centers affiliated with executive agencies are required to fulfill at least twenty percent (20%) of their annual research priority capacity and Jihad of Explanation topics by the end of the program by registering them in the Ideas and Needs System (NAN) through student theses and dissertations of students of that agency or students studying at universities and higher education institutions affiliated with the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology, Health, Treatment and Medical Education, and the Teachers Mobilization Organization. Confidential topics are not subject to this ruling.
The Faculty Recruitment Center affiliated with the Ministry of Science, Research and Technology is required to consider the necessary points for researchers who have conducted research activities in the aforementioned field in the recruitment process of faculty members.
Note: Research institutions and centers affiliated with the judiciary and legislative branches, and the ministries of science, research, and technology, and health, treatment, and medical education are exempt from the provisions of this paragraph.
C- In order to enhance the international scientific status of the Islamic Republic of Iran and become a regional scientific and technological authority, the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology, Health, Treatment and Medical Education, and the Presidential Vice Presidency for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy, as appropriate, are required to identify leading scientific centers and scientific poles in specialized fields that advance science and technology in the country and, during the implementation of the program, provide the necessary funds for the renovation of relevant scientific equipment, devices and instruments within the annual budget limits.
The relevant executive regulations will be prepared by the aforementioned deputy, in cooperation with the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology, and Health, Treatment and Medical Education, within three months of the law coming into force, and will be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Article 98 – In order to activate the territorial capabilities and strategic position of the Islamic Republic of Iran and effectively interact with the international and regional environment, the following measures shall be taken:
A- In order to connect, attract, and return elites and specialists and their role in the cycle of serving the country, the Vice Presidency for Science, Technology, and Knowledge-Based Economy, in cooperation with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, is required to prepare, within three months of the entry into force of this law, an executive regulation for connecting Iranian elites abroad and submit it to the Council of Ministers for approval, in a way that will enable effective interaction with at least twenty percent (20%) of the target community by the end of the program.
B- The Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education are required, in cooperation with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, to accept foreign students within the capacity of public and private universities and the Islamic Azad University by developing student exchange programs and facilitating the necessary conditions for admission, making tuition pricing competitive, strengthening the interchangeability of curricula of the country's universities with target foreign universities, and facilitating attendance during the study period, especially granting the right of residence for the duration of study, frequent entry and exit, part-time work, health insurance, and banking services to foreign students.
C- The Vice Presidency for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy, in cooperation with the Ministry of Cooperation, Labor and Social Welfare, is required to provide employment, residence and consular facilities for elite international graduates who are in demand for work in the country within one year of the entry into force of this law. The executive regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the said Vice Presidency in cooperation with the Ministries of Foreign Affairs, Interior, Information, Science, Research and Technology, and Health, Treatment and Medical Education, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
The Presidential Vice President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy is required to submit a report on the performance of this clause, broken down by implementing agencies, to the Parliament's Education, Research and Technology Committee every six months.
Financial resources
Article 99 – With the aim of improving the productivity and effectiveness of higher education, research and technology resources, increasing the acceleration of scientific, technological and innovation progress, and achieving a seven percent (7%) share of medium-to-high technology products in the gross domestic product:
A- The payment of credits allocated from public sources and in the form of annual budgets to universities and educational and research institutions subject to Article (1) of the Law on Permanent Provisions of the National Development Programs is based on the indicators of each of the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology and Health, Treatment and Medical Education and the reciprocal agreement between the organization and the relevant universities and institutions. The compliance of spending with the aforementioned indicators is the responsibility of the head of the institution or university. Article (1) of the Law on Permanent Provisions of the National Development Programs governs the provisions of this law.
Note - The annual budget and credits of the universities of the Ministry of Science, Research and Technology must be regulated by the organization in such a way that at least fifteen percent (15%) of the credits are foreseen and allocated for research affairs and at least five percent (5%) of the credits are allocated for cultural affairs.
B- In order to strengthen the innovation financing system, helping to increase the capital of the Innovation and Prosperity Fund or joint investment with the fund management are considered examples of Subsection (2) of Clause (T) of Article (11) of the Knowledge-Based Production Leap Law.
C- In order to implement the Knowledge-Based Production Leap Law and develop the production value chain and move beyond raw sales, the export of all mineral materials and products, metallic and non-metallic mineral industries, and oil, gas, and petrochemical products included in the list prepared by the Ministry of Industry, Mines, and Trade in cooperation with the Ministries of Economic Affairs, Finance, and Petroleum and the Presidential Vice-President for Science, Technology, and Knowledge-Based Economy, and approved by the Council of Ministers, shall be subject to income tax and duties in all parts of the country. The definitive amount of these duties shall be prepared annually by the aforementioned agencies and approved by the Council of Ministers. All sources of income subject to this paragraph, as well as the input rights of machinery and equipment for production, industrial, mining, and agricultural lines, shall be made available to the Presidential Vice-President for Science, Technology, and Knowledge-Based Economy, in accordance with the provisions of the annual budget laws and in compliance with Article 53 of the Constitution, in line with the implementation of the Knowledge-Based Production Leap Law, in such a way that fifty percent (50%) of these resources shall be spent on increasing the capital of the Innovation and Prosperity Fund. This deputy is required to submit its performance report to the parliament and the organization every six months.
D- The government (Deputy President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy) is required to take the necessary measures in the following areas within the approved budget, in cooperation with relevant executive agencies and organizations, with the aim of providing the integrated infrastructure needed to improve the technological ecosystem in leading and empowering areas, attracting and empowering elites, and facilitating access to infrastructure with the participation of the private sector and using the capacities of the Knowledge-Based Production Leap Law:
1- Artificial Intelligence
2- Electric charge (quantum)
3 – Bioengineering
4- Advanced materials and construction
5- Microtechnology and microelectronics (microelectronics)
6- Neurotechnology, brain and cognitive sciences
The executive regulations of this clause will be prepared by the Presidential Vice President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy in cooperation with the organization and will be approved by the Council of Ministers.
E- In order to address the challenges and technological bottlenecks of the executive agencies and to internalize the strategic items subject to Article (1) of the Law on the Leap of Knowledge-Based Production and the Implementation of Pioneering Projects, the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is obliged, in cooperation with the Vice Presidency for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy of the Presidency and using the capacities of the Innovation and Prosperity Fund and other legal capacities, to take the necessary measures to internalize at least ten percent (10%) of the strategic items required by its sector subject to Article (1) of the aforementioned law every year, utilizing the capacity of knowledge-based companies and institutions and academic jihad, if the relevant ministry determines that these companies and institutions are capable of providing the aforementioned goods and services.
The executive regulations of this clause, including the method of determining strategic items and the capabilities of the aforementioned companies and institutions, in compliance with the Knowledge-Based Production Leap Law, will be prepared by the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade in cooperation with the Presidential Vice-President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy and the organization, and will be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Chapter 21 – Foreign Policy
Political diplomacy
Article 100 – In implementing paragraph (21) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan, which emphasizes active activism in official and public diplomacy by creating a transformation and capacity-building of values 
and revolution in human resources in the diplomatic apparatus and purposeful and effective cooperation of organizations and institutions responsible for foreign affairs, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is responsible for implementing the provisions of the aforementioned paragraph by using all its legal capacities and other laws, and all agencies are also required to coordinate and cooperate with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in all their actions in the field of foreign relations and the aforementioned matters, as the case may be, within the framework of laws and regulations. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is required to take the following measures in addition to building capacity in human capital and strengthening and promoting its affiliated educational and research centers:
1- Implementing political measures and general policies of the regime, especially in the dimension of fighting global arrogance and the Zionist regime, supporting the oppressed and supporting Palestine with emphasis on the Law of Support for the Islamic Revolution of the Palestinian People, approved on February 19, 1936, and the Law of Obligation of the Government to Comprehensively Support the Oppressed People of Palestine, approved on October 11, 1938, and establishing and strengthening the authority of the resistance axis and supporting unifying currents in the Islamic world, bringing religions and sects closer, and confronting the enemy's conspiracy to create division in the Islamic world, and explaining the views and achievements of the Islamic Republic of Iran and the resistance economy policies in the cross-border area, with priority given to regional and neighboring countries, using new political tools (diplomacy).
2- Active activism on various international issues, including issues related to human rights, disarmament, the environment, protecting the country's peaceful nuclear program, lifting oppressive sanctions, managing crises and regional conflicts, confronting "violence, terrorism, and extremism," and inspiring the Islamic Revolution to the world's oppressed community.
Note - The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is required to establish balanced relations with the countries of the region and to develop them during the implementation of the program, with the aim of increasing the regional role of the Islamic Republic of Iran and strengthening the multipolar system through political (diplomatic) measures.
3- Supporting and safeguarding the rights, identity, and social capital of compatriots abroad within the framework of national interests, facilitating their participation in the country's economic, cultural, and scientific activities, striving to continue cultural ties with the homeland by facilitating their movement into the country, facilitating access to legal advisory services, and strengthening the status and performance of the Supreme Council for Iranians Abroad in cooperation with all relevant executive agencies.
In this regard, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is required, in cooperation with the organization, to review the regulations of the Supreme Council for Iranians Abroad in light of the above provisions within three months of the entry into force of this law and submit them to the Council of Ministers for approval. The Ministry is also required to submit a report on the implementation of this article to the Parliament every six months.
Note - The provision of this article regarding the armed forces is subject to clause "p" of Article (118) of this law.
Economic policy (diplomacy)
Article 101 - In implementing paragraphs (10) and (22) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and in order to strengthen the economy-oriented approach in foreign policy and regional and global relations and strengthen economic ties with priority to neighbors, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is required to take the following measures, as appropriate, in compliance with the seventy-seventh (77), eightieth (80) and one hundred and twenty-fifth (125) principles of the Constitution, using all the facilities and capacities of foreign policy, bilateral relations, neighborhood policy (diplomacy), and multilateral and international policy (diplomacy) to advance economic policy (diplomacy):
A- Preparing a comprehensive plan to improve the efficiency and effectiveness of economic policy (diplomacy), especially in the field of knowledge-based economy, focusing on economic ties with neighbors, Asian, African, Latin American countries, emerging powers, and international organizations, including the Shanghai Cooperation Organization, within three months of the entry into force of this law, in cooperation with other relevant executive agencies and in the framework of the Coordination Headquarters for Foreign Economic Relations.
B- Concluding and deepening preferential and free trade agreements, with priority given to concluding preferential trade agreements with target countries in the medium term and free trade in the long term (including Eurasia), and deepening preferential trade agreements with neighboring countries, taking into account cultural affinities, in cooperation with the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade.
C- Providing the basis for utilizing the capacities of the private and cooperative sectors in order to further develop foreign economic and trade relations in cooperation with the Iranian Chamber of Commerce, Industries, Mines and Agriculture and the Iranian Chamber of Cooperatives.
D- Assistance and support in establishing joint ventures with target countries in order to benefit from the facilities provided to international contractors in the reciprocal trade policy document with the aforementioned countries.
E- Making the necessary agreements with Iran's trading partner countries regarding compliance with standards accepted by the parties, in cooperation with the National Standards Organization of Iran and other relevant agencies.
C- Determining the amount and manner of granting development aid to target countries within the framework of the operational plan of the relevant executive agencies, with the approval of the Council of Ministers.
G- Facilitating animal quarantine regulations in cooperation with the Quarantine and Biosecurity Office of the National Veterinary Organization.
H- Increasing the facilities for electronic commercial and multiple-entry visas for foreign traders with a history of trading with Iran and approved by the Iranian Chamber of Commerce, Industries, Mines and Agriculture.
X- Helping to enhance the status of the Islamic Republic of Iran at regional and international levels with an emphasis on utilizing the capacity of the Shanghai, BRICS, ECO, and Eurasian Economic Union organizations through strengthening various aspects of transit (energy, goods, passengers, and tourism), developing the Makran coast with priority on completing Chabahar Port, completing and connecting all transit ports on the northern and southern coasts of the country with an emphasis on the Arvand Free Zone and the Amirabad Special Economic Zone, diversifying the country's export and import markets as much as possible, attracting foreign investment, finding mechanisms to deal with banking and insurance sanctions, especially through the expansion of alternative banking messengers to SWIFT, helping to attract foreign capital and technology, and benefiting from extraterritorial cultivation in order to improve the country's food security, pursuing rights issues with neighboring countries, and allowing the country to benefit from the scientific and technological achievements of other countries in the consumption and distribution of water, connecting the energy networks of neighboring countries to the country's domestic network, promoting the tourism industry, including health, sightseeing, scientific, and pilgrimage tourism, and improving the country's status in the field of trade. With an emphasis on technology and knowledge-based trade and the export of technical and engineering services, energy transfer and swap services, including gas, oil and electricity, in cooperation with all relevant agencies, especially the ministries of roads and urban development, agricultural jihad, cultural heritage, tourism and handicrafts, oil, power and industry, mining and trade, the Supreme Council of Free Trade, Industrial and Special Economic Zones, revolutionary institutions and non-governmental sectors, including cooperative and private sectors, including the Iranian Chambers of Commerce, Industries, Mines and Agriculture, and the Central and Provincial Cooperatives.
The Ministry of Foreign Affairs is required to submit a report on the implementation of this article to the Parliament every six months.
Chapter 22 – Defense and Security
Article 102–
A- The government is required to allocate at least five percent (5%) of the general policies of the Seventh Plan in order to increase the country's defense capability in the regional power balance and to ensure national interests and security, as a share of defense capacity strengthening in the lines of defense capacity strengthening in the annual budget of the country. The aforementioned minimum share cannot be reduced during the implementation of the plan.
Resources and credits for strengthening the defense force are provided one hundred percent (100%). If, for any reason, this is not possible, the government is obliged, upon request of the General Staff of the Armed Forces of the Islamic Republic of Iran, to deliver a portion of the determined share in rials, in compliance with Article 53 of the Constitution, by applying the rial equivalent to the treasury of various types of crude oil and gas condensates.
The armed forces are allowed to use part of their crude oil and gas condensate quota to export products and derivatives in affiliated and related refineries and petrochemical plants.
B- In order to enhance the capabilities and capacities of the defense industries with other industrial sectors and make maximum use of the overflow of defense sector technologies to the country's economic and technological enterprises and benefit from national capacities in the defense innovation system and supply chain and their dual-purpose, the Ministry of Defense and Armed Forces Support is obliged to use the scientific capacity of scientific centers and growth centers of science and technology parks to transfer the overflow of technical knowledge and achievements of the defense sector and to participate with the private sector, cooperatives, non-governmental public institutions and institutions in industries such as aviation, maritime, energy, automobile, microelectronics, mining, agriculture and services. The Ministry of Defense and Armed Forces Support, in cooperation with relevant authorities in the government and non-governmental sectors, shall identify and determine the requirements for dual-purpose capacity of these sectors for defense and security production by establishing a joint specialized working group with relevant agencies and also by launching joint investment companies with the private and cooperative sectors in compliance with Article 44 (44) of the Constitution.
The executive regulations of this clause shall be prepared by the Ministry of Defense and Armed Forces Support in cooperation with the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade, the Vice Presidency for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy and the Organization, and with the approval of the General Staff of the Armed Forces, within four months of the entry into force of this law, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Note - All measures in this section must be carried out with due regard to security and protection considerations.
C- The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is required to issue licenses for the exploitation of mines located in existing barracks owned by the armed forces, upon request from the General Staff of the Armed Forces, in compliance with the general policies of Article 44 (44) of the Constitution and its implementing law, as well as the Mining Law and other laws.
The executive regulations of this clause, including the method of paying government salaries and the exploitation process and other necessary measures, shall be prepared by the Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade in cooperation with the General Staff of the Armed Forces and the organization within the framework of the laws, in compliance with Article Fifty-Three (53) of the Constitution, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
D- In order to strengthen the defense of the country's independence and territorial integrity, utilize national capacities, and create the necessary motivation for young people to perform their military service, and to foster excellence, empowerment, and increase their skills during the years of program implementation, the General Staff of the Armed Forces shall take action to reduce military service to an average of fourteen months, including the period of training and replacement of other members, by providing sustainable resources by the government, determining the duties of absentees and students studying at reputable universities abroad, which shall be approved by the Ministries of Science, Research, and Technology, Health, Treatment, and Medical Education, and the Supreme Council of Seminaries, in compliance with Article (4) of the Public Service Law.
Note 1 – In line with general population policies, those over the age of 35, with at least two children, and who are not absent are exempt from the mandatory period of public service.
Note 2: Continuing education abroad for those with a diploma or higher and students of seminaries is permitted in accordance with the Public Service Law, and the instructions on how and conditions for issuing educational exemptions are prepared and implemented by the General Staff of the Armed Forces in cooperation with the Ministries of Science, Research and Technology, Health, Treatment and Medical Education, and the Supreme Council of Seminaries.
E- In order to quantitatively and qualitatively strengthen the Basij for the Oppressed Organization and implement the decree to enhance the Basij and play a greater role in all areas of the second stage of the Islamic Revolution, including security, defense, cultural, social, economic, and scientific, the government is obligated to provide the necessary resources and support during the implementation of the program to implement the following items through the Basij for the Oppressed Organization:
1- Recruiting, training, organizing, maintaining cohesion, and playing a role until the mobilization of tens of millions is realized.
2- Countering soft war and cultural invasion in real and virtual space
3- Promoting the Iranian Islamic lifestyle and helping to combat social anomalies and harms by providing the necessary platforms and public capacities.
4- Quantitative and qualitative improvement of the role and activities of the Basij with the interaction of relevant executive bodies through mobilization of strata and experts, neighborhood-based public security programs, relief and rescue, scientific nuclei, growth centers and knowledge-based companies, deepening and promoting the values 
of the Islamic Revolution and the Sacred Defense, preserving their works, expanding the camps of the Path of Light and the Path of Progress, holding congresses and memorials for the martyrs.
5- Development and participation of the Basij Sazandegi Organization in assisting the government in the issues of alleviating deprivation, resistance economy, employment, and construction in deprived areas and villages of the country.
6- Creating appropriate infrastructure for Basij mission ranks
The Basij Mostazafin Organization and the organization are required to submit a report on the performance of this section every six months to the "Internal Affairs and Councils" and "National Security and Foreign Policy" committees of the parliament.
C- The government is required to take the following measures, in cooperation with the General Staff of the Armed Forces, in order to enhance, empower, and achieve deterrence power and solve the problems of the Armed Forces and the Basij Organization of the Underprivileged, during the implementation of the program and within the approved budget:
1- Collective settlement - Expenses for the accounts of water, electricity and gas debts of the ranks of the armed forces from the armed forces budget, with the exception of organizational houses
Note - The executive regulations for saving energy and water consumption in the armed forces and the method of spending the resources obtained from it within the framework of the laws and in the form of annual budgets shall be prepared by the organization in cooperation with the General Staff of the Armed Forces and the Ministries of Energy and Oil and relevant agencies within three months of the entry into force of this law and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
2- Support and advocacy in the construction of military, cultural and welfare infrastructures of the Islamic Republic of Iran Navy in the Makran region and the implementation of facilities and infrastructures of the First Naval Region in Jask.
3- Helping to equip, develop, and improve the technical and quality level of military airports that are under joint public and military operation, from the specific income of the airport itself.
4- Support and advocacy for the advancement of the country's aerospace industry and space-based services.
5- The housing allowance for armed forces personnel (military and law enforcement) residing in organizational houses is deducted from their income and deposited into a special account with the National Treasury, and the equivalent of the deposited funds is deposited into the accounts of the armed forces budget lines to cover the costs of repairing and maintaining organizational houses during the implementation of the program.
6- In order to pay special attention to the mobilization of the oppressed, the government is authorized to provide land and construct buildings for the mobilization ranks up to the level of the resistance areas and to provide the necessary resources and support, including defense and security equipment, in the provincial centers.
Article 103 – In implementing paragraph (24) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and in order to strengthen infrastructure and optimize public and institutional mechanisms to protect and enhance resilience and reduce the vulnerability of infrastructure and national capital, and to safeguard and protect national interests and the people against perceived threats, including cyber, biological, chemical and radiological, electromagnetic and military, with priority given to passive defense, the following measures shall be taken:
A- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to provide security services and annual assessment and ranking of the cyber security of executive agencies in accordance with the standards and regulations approved by the Permanent Working Group (Committee) of the Country's Passive Defense, in coordination and cooperation with the Ministry of Intelligence, the IRGC Intelligence Organization, the country's Passive Defense Organization, and by utilizing companies and institutions with a secure audit license or certificate from the Information Technology Organization of Iran, and to submit its report to the three branches of government as appropriate.
B- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to take steps, in cooperation with the Ministry of Intelligence and the IRGC Intelligence Organization, to prepare for the formation of security operators certified to provide cyber security services to meet the needs of government and non-government sectors and strengthen the supply side of these services.
C- In order to improve the sustainable security factor and reduce security crimes, the Secretariat of the Supreme National Security Council, in cooperation with relevant agencies, including the Ministry of Intelligence and the IRGC Intelligence Organization, is required to prepare a security strategic document and a comprehensive plan for the country's intelligence monitoring with a national division of labor with the approach of combating bioterrorism, insecurity, disruption, and threats to the country's security, and to submit its plan to the Supreme National Security Council for approval by the end of the first year.
Note 1- The organization is required to provide the foreign exchange resources required to implement the programs approved by the Ministry of Intelligence during the years of the program in such a way that the share of foreign exchange resources required from the first year of the program is not less than the foreign exchange resources anticipated in 1401.
Note 2 - The organization is required to maintain the rank of the IRGC Intelligence Organization within the framework of the approvals of the Supreme National Security Council and to provide foreign exchange resources for the rank of "Technical Martyr" throughout the years of the program in such a way that the share of foreign exchange resources required from the first year of the program is not less than the foreign exchange resources anticipated in 1401.
D- Military, law enforcement and other responsible institutions located at the border, in coordination with the General Staff of the Armed Forces, are required to establish and support access of the Ministry of Intelligence and the IRGC Intelligence Organization to the data of their border systems and to provide appropriate facilities for the deployment of the Ministry of Intelligence’s dedicated systems at the border. The Ministry of Intelligence and the IRGC Intelligence Organization are required to meet the information needs of the security, military and law enforcement institutions located at the border by using the existing information data, observing all security considerations, and based on the special border task of the National Security Council. The instructions on how to exchange information and the duties of the institutions will be issued by the National Security Council within six months of the entry into force of this law.
E- In order to promote public order and security, provide sustainable and effective support for the performance of officers, increase the reliability of reports, and prevent possible violations, the Police Command of the Islamic Republic of Iran is required, by the end of the first year of the program, within the ceiling of the credits stipulated in the annual budget laws, to record spatial data and take pictures of the place of operations, including inspection, entry, examination of the place, investigation of the crime scene, arrest and detention of suspects and criminals, discovery of crime tools, and seizure and storage of discovered objects, while respecting privacy and citizen rights, through cameras installed on officers' clothing, vehicles, and related places, while maintaining the confidentiality of the camera information. In addition to continuously monitoring and supervising the correct operation of the equipment and preserving the recorded content for at least six months, it shall provide the judicial authority with access to the aforementioned data as an attachment to the case file. The Ministry of Interior and the Police Command of the Islamic Republic of Iran are required to submit a report on the performance of this section to the Internal Affairs Commission and the Councils of the Parliament every six months.
Note - Filming the crimes against chastity, as referred to in this paragraph, is prohibited, as is the note to Article (306) of the Criminal Procedure Code, and if any of the aforementioned crimes are filmed, they must be immediately destroyed.
Cases where the crime was committed in plain sight and in the public eye, as well as cases where the proof of a more important matter, such as the security and morality of society, depends on this matter, are not subject to the provisions of this note.
C- All national and provincial executive agencies are required to take action to prevent the occurrence of unexpected and unfortunate incidents, reduce vulnerability and the consequences thereof in the country's buildings and infrastructure facilities, and increase the deterrence and resilience of infrastructure by requiring and prioritizing technical inspections of vital, sensitive, and important buildings in the country on an annual basis and preparing reports on the safety status by qualified companies with a history of relevant activities and licenses from competent authorities such as the National Crisis Management Organization, the National Passive Defense Organization, and the National Standards Organization of Iran. The Ministry of Interior is required to submit its performance report to the Parliament annually.
G- Executive agencies are required to cooperate with the National Cyberspace Center of the country in order to enhance the cyber power of the Islamic Republic of Iran to the level of influential global powers, as well as to prevent and deal with cyberspace incidents and protect and safeguard the security of the country's cyberspace.
H- In order to develop sustainable security, enhance the sense of security, reduce crime, and enhance the status, dignity, and livelihood of the personnel of the Islamic Republic of Iran's Police Command, the following measures will be taken:
1- The government is required, through the Provincial Planning and Development Council, to take action to construct, complete, reconstruct, and equip law enforcement ranks, with priority given to police stations and police stations, and to include the necessary funds in the country's annual budget bills.
2- In order to prevent and expedite the detection of crimes, the Islamic Republic of Iran's Police Command should provide online access to databases and systems related to the missions of the Islamic Republic of Iran's Police Command, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law and the protection of individuals' privacy, at the disposal of government agencies, the list of which is determined by the General Staff of the Armed Forces.
X- Intelligent monitoring (control) and surveillance systems for all main thoroughfares, squares, and highways in provincial centers and metropolitan cities, as well as main roads and freeways, which are installed, maintained, and updated by municipalities and the Ministry of Roads and Urban Development, and their access is provided online to the Islamic Republic of Iran's Police Command.
The cost of the above measures, in cases carried out by municipalities, is covered by the municipalities' share of traffic fines after the treasury turnover.
Chapter 23 – Reform of the Administrative System
Article 104 – In implementing paragraph (25) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and in order to achieve the following quantitative goals, action shall be taken in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:
Table No. (22) - Quantitative objectives of performance indicators for administrative system reform
Performance measure	One known	Quantitative goal at the end of the program
Redesigning and improving work methods	Percentage	۶۵
Reducing the total number of employees in executive agencies	Percentage	۱۵
Reduction of government buildings and office spaces, with the exception of public schools.	Percentage	۵
Delegation of tasks and powers that can be delegated to provincial and county levels	Percentage	۷۵
Conducting all government transactions electronically	Percentage	۱۰۰
Providing all government services to citizens electronically	Percentage	۱۰۰
Improving the country's ranking in the e-government development index	Rank	۷۵
The country's administrative and employment organization is required to submit an annual report on the performance indicators of administrative system reform to the parliament.
Note: It is mandatory to observe local and domestic considerations and criteria in monitoring and reporting on performance indicators for administrative system reform and e-government development.
Government structure
Article 105 – In order to improve the efficiency of the administrative system, reduce current costs, and make the government more agile, intelligent, rational, and proportionate, based on the government’s role in policymaking and regulation, and reduce bureaucracy, the following measures should be taken:
A- Executive agencies are required to redesign their organizational structure in accordance with the matters mentioned in this paragraph and submit it to the approval of the State Administrative and Employment Organization by the end of the third year of the program in such a way that each year, at least five percent (5%) of organizational units are reduced. The State Administrative and Employment Organization is required to submit a report on the implementation of this paragraph, broken down by executive agencies, to the President and the Parliament on a quarterly basis.
1- The country's administrative and employment organization is required to identify, by the end of the first year of the program, activities and duties outside the inherent missions of executive agencies and parallel and unnecessary organizations and submit a proposal to eliminate them for approval to the Supreme Administrative Council. The Supreme Administrative Council is required to act on the approval of the referred cases within a maximum of six months and submit a performance report to the parliament. Allocating any budget to activities and duties outside the legal missions of executive agencies and parallel and unnecessary organizations is prohibited.
2- Service delivery processes should be reformed and shortened by focusing on results and ensuring quality and equitable access.
3- Executive agencies, in cooperation with the country's administrative and employment organization, are required to:
1-3- Take action to transfer governance affairs from state-owned companies to the relevant agency in compliance with the Law on the Implementation of General Policies, Article 44 (44) of the Constitution.
2-3- Take steps to transfer non-governmental management matters, for which it is possible to purchase services, to the private sector.
3-3- Take action to transfer those enterprises that can be transferred to provinces and cities with the approach of enabling optimal local decisions.
4-3- Identify and transfer those enterprises that can be legally and executively transferred to municipalities with an integrated urban management approach and strengthen the government's policy-making, coordination, facilitation, and supervisory role, upon the proposal of the Supreme Council of Provinces.
The country's administrative and employment organization and the organization are required to submit a performance report on the implementation of this component to the parliament every six months.
4- Any quantitative expansion of the services of executive agencies in relation to the services provided in 1402 (2013) shall be carried out solely by virtue of Articles (13), (14) and (15) of the Civil Service Management Law, through the purchase of services from the non-governmental sector by paying costs proportional to the cost price of similar services. Also, the provision of current services shall be carried out in the same manner and gradually.
Note: Executive agencies are required to empower the private and cooperative sectors to participate in providing services.
5- The creation of any executive body by the government is prohibited except through merger or consolidation.
B- The country's administrative and employment organization is required to make the necessary legal arrangements with the approval of the Supreme Administrative Council, with the aim of integrating the decision-making system by the end of the first year of the program, in cooperation with relevant authorities, to merge councils with similar or overlapping duties, except for councils that have been established pursuant to the Constitution, the permission of the Supreme Leader, or by law.
The country's administrative and employment organization is required to submit an annual performance report on this clause to the parliament.
Note 1: The provisions of this article do not include the Guardian Council, the Assembly of Experts of the Supreme Leader, the Expediency Discernment Council, the Supreme National Security Council, the Parliament, the Armed Forces of the Islamic Republic of Iran, and the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization.
Note 2: The transfer and assignment of employees between agencies subject to the Civil Service Management Law and others, including government companies and non-governmental public institutions and organizations, is permitted in compliance with the laws.
C- The government is required to transfer the offices of industrial and mining companies that are state-owned or whose shares are partly owned by public property and funds, except for essential cases and to the extent necessary, under the responsibility of the Ministry of Economic Affairs and Finance, from Tehran to the city where the factory is located, by the end of the third year of the program. If the transfer is not made by the end of the third year of the program, the country's Tax Affairs Organization is required to impose a double annual performance tax on these companies.
Government human capital
Article 106 – In order to improve the productivity of human capital, increase the motivation of government employees to provide quality services, organize the recruitment, employment, and also the qualitative development of employees of ministries, state-owned companies, and state institutions subordinate to the executive branch, the following measures shall be taken:
A- All powers of ministries and government institutions subordinate to the executive branch regarding the recruitment and employment of human resources, with the exception of the Ministry of Intelligence, the General Inspectorate of the State (with due observance of Article (3) of the Law on the Establishment of the General Inspectorate of the State approved on 19/7/1360 with subsequent amendments and additions), and the Atomic Energy Organization of Iran, are suspended during the implementation of the program. Any recruitment, whether formal, contractual, permanent or temporary labor, and similar titles, and the employment of human resources, whether specific work contracts, labor contracts, contracts from capital asset acquisition projects, corporate contracts, and other titles, shall be carried out solely on the basis of information registered in the integrated system of the administrative system, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law, and based on the joint authorization of the organization and the country's administrative and employment organization, if the organization provides funding. Any request by agencies to recruit and employ new personnel is subject to the registration of the list of names of needed or surplus personnel in the above system and the confirmation of the country's administrative and employment organization that there is no adequate personnel in the aforementioned system.
for-
1- The government is authorized to take legal action until the end of the second year of the program to establish the criteria for transferring new employees who will be employed after the entry into force of this law, among agencies solely within the same city where the originating agency is employed, while respecting their acquired legal rights, including their rights and benefits in the originating agency.
2- The transfer, assignment, and leave of contract employees are the same as those of regular and permanent employees.
Note: The transfer of contract employees is only permitted if they have a government employee ID (code) approved by the country's administrative and employment organization, and the destination agency declares its need and the originating agency agrees.
3- The government is authorized to take legal action regarding special extraordinary situations subject to deductions in order to ensure fairness in payment, increase productivity, and maintain human resources in executive agencies, as well as strengthen governance and oversight, including agencies that oversee the activities of companies.
C- The Public Administration Training Center is required to design a "Government Employee Training Monitoring and Evaluation System" as an integrated subsystem of the administrative system within three months of the effective date of this law, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law, in such a way that monitoring and evaluation of executive agency training centers and training courses held are carried out based on the performance recorded in this system, and issuing employee training certificates is carried out through it.
D- The country's administrative and employment organization is required, in cooperation with executive agencies, to conduct an educational needs assessment based on a database of managers' records and performance, job needs, and the results of the evaluation of professional competence centers, and to design and organize training and development programs for managers in the form of in-service training modules and courses. Each of the in-service training centers of the agencies will be responsible for holding the courses under the supervision of the Public Administration Training Center. In implementing this clause, issuing any type of educational certificate or diploma or its equivalent for the aforementioned courses is prohibited.
Note - The above clauses do not include the Guardian Council, the Assembly of Experts of the Supreme Leader, the Expediency Discernment Council, the Supreme National Security Council and the Parliament, the Armed Forces of the Islamic Republic of Iran, and the Islamic Republic of Iran Broadcasting Organization.
E- The government is required to consider firefighting and radiation work as difficult and harmful jobs. During the implementation of the program, the Radiation Protection Law approved on 1/20/1368 shall be considered valid.
Smartization and e-government
Article 107 – In order to make the government smart and realize e-government, executive agencies are required to take the following measures in compliance with Articles (7) and (10) of the National Data and Information Management Law and the Law on Facilitating the Issuance of Business Licenses:
A- Connect their main and backup data centers to the integrated cloud infrastructure of the smart government. The executive regulations of this clause, including the connection of the aforementioned devices and the data transfer of the devices subordinate to the executive branch, as well as the data transfer of other devices if they agree, and the timing and method of doing so, shall be prepared by the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology in cooperation with the Ministry of Information and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Note 1- The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology is required to create, strengthen, and deploy an integrated cloud infrastructure for the smart government by the end of the first year of the program, with priority given to using the public-private partnership model.
Note 2 - The Atomic Energy Organization of Iran, the Ministry of Intelligence, and the Armed Forces are exempt from the provisions of this paragraph.
B- The country's administrative and employment organization is required to establish a deputy or center or organization for "Innovation, Intelligence and Security" in accordance with the mission of each of the country's executive agencies by the end of the first year of the program, in cooperation with other executive agencies, by integrating the mission, structure, and human resources of the information technology and cyberspace security units, the administrative modernization and transformation center, research and development centers, and similar titles.
Note - The executive regulations of this clause, including the description of duties and organizational structure, dismissal and appointment of managers, and the method of supervision, shall be prepared by the country's administrative and employment organization in cooperation with the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology, and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
C- Prepare and implement an operational plan for establishing and implementing the smart cycle, reforming processes, and establishing a data-based governance system within one year of the entry into force of this law.
D- Design and manage common systems in the headquarters units of ministries and independent government institutions and eliminate parallel systems within the framework of their digital transformation program and implement it.
Note - In order to avoid parallel work and save government costs during the program years, the launch of any new national and cross-sectoral system is possible only after obtaining permission from the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology and in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law. The said ministry is obliged to determine the necessity of launching and non-parallel work within one month from the date of receipt of the request and to notify the result. If the said ministry, in its discretion, does not consider the mentioned deadline sufficient, the said deadline will be extended for another month and the applicant will be informed of this. After the extended deadline, the applicant can proceed to launch the system without the approval of the said ministry. Failure of the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology to respond within the mentioned deadlines is considered a violation and can be investigated by the competent legal authorities. The executive agencies are obliged to cooperate and implement the provisions of this notification.
E- Implement the necessary measures for the development of smart government in order to improve national and international indicators, including the International E-Government Development Index, while observing local and domestic considerations and standards and the National Data and Information Management Law. The Ministry of Communications and Information Technology, in cooperation with the country's administrative and employment organization, is required to prepare and announce the relevant guidelines and criteria.
C- Provide their services online and securely by the end of the first year of the program's implementation and provide at least twenty percent (20%) of their electronic services annually to all legal entities and individuals over the age of eighteen through the "National Smart Government Services Window" in a smart manner without in-person visits, human intervention, or manual collection of documents and information. The executive regulations of this clause, including examples of services and the method of making the relevant processes smart and optimizing them, shall be prepared by the Ministry of Communications and Information Technology in cooperation with the country's Administrative and Employment Organization within three months of the law coming into force and shall be approved by the Council of Ministers.
Note - The National Civil Registration Organization is required to launch a national database of the identity of natural persons with the ability to identify causal and relative relationships of natural persons and identify households.
G- All executive agencies in charge of the basic databases subject to the National Data and Information Management Law are required to complete their databases by the end of the first year of the program at the latest, and from the beginning of the second year of the program, exchange data and information and respond to any inquiries required by other executive agencies and businesses in a completely real-time and online manner based on the National Data and Information Management Law. The e-Government Interoperability Working Group shall submit an annual report on the implementation of this clause to the Parliament.
H- Within one year of the entry into force of this law, refrain from receiving any evidence or document related to databases and basic information subject to Article (10) of the National Data and Information Management Law manually or requiring users to upload it.
X- In order to improve productivity and increase the share of the digital economy, all ministries, organizations, the country's administrative and employment organization, the Environmental Protection Agency, the Central Bank, and the Presidential Vice-President for Science, Technology, and Knowledge-Based Economy, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law, are required to prepare a digital transformation program for their sector and its leading projects, along with its financing mechanisms, in accordance with the proposals and executive capabilities of the non-governmental sector, by the end of the first year of implementation of the program, and submit them to the Cabinet for approval. The progress report of this paragraph must be submitted annually to the Supreme Council for Cyberspace and the Parliament.
Note - The National Computer Guild Organization can, by utilizing the maximum capacity of all organizations active in the field of information and communication technology, present a proposed program for transformation and improving productivity using information technology and smartening each of the sectors and present it to the relevant executive body. Executive bodies will also consider the proposed plans of the National Computer Guild Organization in formulating their digital transformation programs.
Article 108 – The Judiciary is required to take the following measures in order to develop intelligence:
A- The auctions of the enforcement branches, the enforcement departments of registration and liquidation of bankruptcy affairs shall be held through the government's electronic procurement system (Setad). The Ministry of Industry, Mines and Trade is obliged to provide the possibility of holding these auctions in this system. The auction of all properties, except for perishable properties, subject to Article (66) of the Civil Enforcement Law approved on 1/8/1356, shall be held through this system and there is no need to sell the property at the place subject to Articles (115) and (116) of the aforementioned law. In order to participate in the auction and submit a price offer, persons must submit ten percent (10%) of the price stipulated in Articles (73) to (75) of the aforementioned law as a cash guarantee for participating in the auction to an account specified through the system. In this case, there is no need to pay ten percent (10%) of the price stipulated in Article (129) of the aforementioned law, and if the winner of the auction does not pay the remaining price of the property on the due date, his guarantee shall be confiscated in favor of the government and deposited into the account of the National Treasury. The instructions on how to use collateral in lieu of cash collateral, as well as the amount and manner of obtaining and releasing these collaterals, shall be approved by the Head of the Judiciary within three months of the entry into force of this law. The Anti-Narcotics Headquarters is also required to hold auctions of the assets subject to Article (30) of the Amended Anti-Narcotics Law of 9/5/1389 through the government's electronic procurement system (Stad). The Ministry of Justice is required to submit a report on the performance of this section to the Parliament every six months.
B- By creating the necessary infrastructure during the program years, take action to issue all ownership documents (except for motor vehicles) electronically in the country's national database of documents, real estate and land cadastre, in compliance with the National Data and Information Management Law. The contents of the issued ownership document are sent to the owner in the Judiciary Notification System, and the details are sent to the owner by SMS by sending the unique ID of the ownership document.
C- The verification of the identity of persons whose signature is required to receive all registration services, such as receiving services from notary offices, marriage and divorce offices, and company registration offices, is subject to obtaining an electronic signature certificate, as referred to in Article (31) of the Electronic Commerce Law approved on 10/17/1382. Foreign nationals who do not have a user account in the Electronic Judicial Notification System (SANA) and persons who are present in prisons and detention centers as convicts or defendants, as well as providing services subject to this clause abroad, are exempt from the provisions of this clause.
Article 109 - Non-judicial authorities whose decisions, opinions and orders must be notified to the beneficiary according to laws or regulations, such as branches of the Government Penal Organization, tax dispute resolution boards, social security organization claims determination boards, employee-employer dispute determination and resolution boards, commissions subject to Articles (99) and (100) of the Municipality Law and the Commission of Article (12) of the Urban Land Law, are required to send their notifications to the beneficiary through the aforementioned system if the beneficiary has a user account in the Judicial Electronic Notification System (SANA) from the beginning of the second year of the program, and in case the beneficiary does not have a user account, through the previous methods. The aforementioned authorities are required to comply with the provisions of this article and notify through the aforementioned methods. The judiciary is also required to provide the aforementioned authorities with the possibility of notifying the subject of this article through the Judicial Electronic Notification System (SANA) to individuals who have a user account (SANA).
The Ministry of Justice is required to submit a report on the implementation of this article to the Parliament every six months.
Performance evaluation and competitiveness enhancement
Article 110 – In order to improve the performance management system, including the evaluation of the performance of the organization, managers, and employees, in accordance with the Cabinet resolution, which will be announced within six months of the entry into force of this law, ministries, state-owned companies, and state institutions under the executive branch shall be evaluated annually and ranked based on scores, based on indicators for measuring the quality of services, cost, speed of provision, and degree of electronicization of services, as well as the level of people’s satisfaction with receiving services, in compliance with the Law on Facilitating the Issuance of Business Licenses, all service-providing agencies (such as educational, health, welfare, agricultural, banking, tax, civil registration, and document registration) at the national and provincial levels, and the report shall be submitted to the President for public information in a transparent manner by the end of June of the following year at the latest.
Executive agencies and provincial units in the top ten percent (10%) of the ranking will be encouraged, and the bottom ten percent (10%) will be disciplined.
Productivity system
Article 111 – In order to fully establish a transparent productivity system and achieve a thirty-five percent (35%) share of total factor productivity growth in ensuring the economic growth target of the program, the following measures will be taken:
A- The government is required to prepare, within a maximum of six months from the entry into force of this law, quantitative and qualitative tables of productivity indicators in different seasons of the program to achieve the thirty-five percent (35%) share of total factor productivity growth in ensuring the economic growth target of the program (eight percent (8%)), and submit them to the approval of the Supreme Steering Council of the program subject to clause "A" of Article (118) of this law, and submit its performance report annually to the Parliament.
B- In order to enhance the effectiveness and coherence of the actions of productivity managers in the country and strengthen the regulatory role, the government is required to submit a plan for the national productivity system, including quantitative targeting, a description of the tasks of its role players, and a national and provincial division of labor based on the following orientations, to the approval of the Supreme Steering Council of the program within a maximum of six months from the entry into force of this law, and to submit a report on the performance of the national productivity system to the parliament annually:
1- Design and implement a system for measuring the productivity of key services of executive agencies and the required statistical and information infrastructure, and implement budget allocation for productivity performance in a way that at the end of the implementation of this law, the productivity index of government services increases by at least ten percent (10%).
2- In order to increase the participation of knowledge-based companies and management consulting and experts in improving the productivity of all factors of production, the government is obliged to use all capacities and the capacity of the Presidential Vice-President for Science, Technology and Knowledge-Based Economy to prepare instructions to increase the role of knowledge-based companies and share the benefits of their participation in improving productivity by the end of the first year of the program and to present its results to the parliament annually.
Chapter 24 – Judicial and Legal Development
Article 112 – In implementing paragraph (26) of the general policies of the Seventh Five-Year Plan and in order to achieve the following quantitative goals, action shall be taken in accordance with the provisions of this chapter:
